1 of 423 DOCUMENTS


Goodson v. State


No. 32701


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


115 Nev. 443; 991 P.2d 472; 1999 Nev. LEXIS 75; 115 Nev. Adv. Rep. 63



December 29, 1999, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a judgment of conviction, pursuant to a jury verdict, of one felony count of driving while under the influence of alcohol. Fourth Judicial District Court, Elko County; Jack B. Ames, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed judgment of the Fourth Judicial District Court, Elko County (Nevada) convicting him of one felony count of driving while under the influence of alcohol; conviction was enhanced to a felony based on a prior misdemeanor conviction resulting from a trial before a nonlawyer justice of the peace.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of felony driving while under the influence of alcohol. The conviction was enhanced to a felony based in part on a prior misdemeanor conviction resulting from a trial before a nonlawyer justice of the peace. The supreme court affirmed the conviction holding it was constitutional for nonlawyer justices of the peace, instructed pursuant to statutory mandates, to preside over criminal misdemeanor trials. The court found that such a trial violated neither the due process or equal protection guarantees of the United States Constitution nor the Nevada Constitution.


OUTCOME: The supreme court affirmed the conviction holding that it was constitutional for nonlawyer justices of the peace, instructed pursuant to statutory mandates, to preside over criminal misdemeanor trials.

 

2 of 423 DOCUMENTS


McNelton v. State


No. 32448


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


115 Nev. 396; 990 P.2d 1263; 1999 Nev. LEXIS 71



December 13, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied March 1, 2000.
Rehearing denied by, 03/01/2000


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from an order of the district court denying a post-conviction petition for a writ of habeas corpus in a death penalty case. Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County; Donald M. Mosley, Judge.
McNelton v. State, 111 Nev. 900, 900 P.2d 934, 1995 Nev. LEXIS 112 (1995)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the order of the Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County (Nevada) denying a post-conviction petition for a writ of habeas corpus on the grounds of ineffective assistance of trial and appellate counsel in a death penalty case.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of first-degree murder with the use of a deadly weapon. The jury returned a verdict of death. Appellant's conviction was upheld on direct appeal. Appellant filed a post-conviction petition for a writ of habeas corpus claiming ineffective assistance of trial and appellate counsel, asserting in part that appellate counsel was ineffective for failing to argue the district court erred in admitting a prior bad act; trial counsel was ineffective for failing to call appellant's mother in the penalty phase; and appellate counsel was ineffective for failing to argue that the district court abused its discretion in denying appellant's Nev. Rev. Stat. § 178.620, Article III(a) motion to dismiss. The court affirmed, concluding that all contentions properly raised lacked merit, and that, regarding appellant's claims raised for the first time on appeal, appellant had failed to show cause and prejudice.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the district court's order denying appellant's post-conviction petition, concluding that none of appellant's contentions properly before the court had merit, and denying relief with respect to those claims raised for the first time on appeal, because appellant failed to show cause and prejudice.

 

3 of 423 DOCUMENTS


Wood v. State


No. 30608


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


115 Nev. 344; 990 P.2d 786; 1999 Nev. LEXIS 66; 115 Nev. Adv. Rep. 51



December 13, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Modified March 9, 2000.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment of conviction pursuant to a jury verdict of attempted murder, conspiracy to commit murder, and solicitation to commit murder. First Judicial District Court, Carson City; Michael R. Griffin, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a judgment, based upon a jury verdict, of the First Judicial District Court, Carson City (Nevada) convicting him of attempted murder, conspiracy to commit murder, and solicitation to commit murder.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted for his role in an assault committed against his ex-wife by two juveniles. On appeal, appellant alleged numerous errors, including that the admission of out-of-court statements implicating him in the conspiracy was reversible error, that he was improperly convicted of solicitation to commit murder, and that Nevada's Fast Track criminal appeal procedure was unconstitutional. The court concluded that appellant's rights under the U.S. Const. amend. VI were violated, and therefore, reversed his convictions. The testimony of a witness, which concluded that one of the juveniles arrested in the attack admitted he intended to kill appellant's ex-wife at appellant's request, was hearsay, did not fall within any exception to the hearsay rule, and was not supported by particularized guarantees of trustworthiness. Thus, the erroneous admission of the witness's testimony was not harmless error. The court also held that Nevada's Fast Track criminal appeal procedure was constitutional.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed and case was remanded; the admission of an out-of-court statement made by a co-conspirator implicating appellant in the conspiracy to kill his ex-wife was reversible error as it was inadmissible hearsay and violated appellant's constitutional right to confront a witness.

 

4 of 423 DOCUMENTS


Mortensen v. State


No. 30855, No. 33293


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


115 Nev. 273; 986 P.2d 1105; 1999 Nev. LEXIS 53



September 27, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Amended October 14, 1999. Rehearing Denied December 27, 1999.
Rehearing denied by, 12/27/1999
Habeas corpus proceeding at, Decision reached on appeal by Mortensen v. State, 126 Nev. 741, 367 P.3d 803, 2010 Nev. LEXIS 1727 (July 15, 2010)
Habeas corpus proceeding at, Motion granted by, in part, Motion denied by, in part, Dismissed by, in part Mortensen v. Neven, 2013 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 11830 (D. Nev., Jan. 28, 2013)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Mortensen v. State, 2014 Nev. Unpub. LEXIS 1393 (Sept. 16, 2014)
Related proceeding at, Dismissed by Mortensen v. State, 2017 Nev. Unpub. LEXIS 716 (Aug. 24, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY: Consolidated appeals from a judgment of conviction, pursuant to a jury verdict, of one count of first-degree murder with the use of a deadly weapon and from a denial of a motion for a new trial based on newly discovered evidence. Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County; Joseph S. Pavlikowski, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged both his conviction for first-degree murder entered in the Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County (Nevada), and the denial of his request for a new trial based on newly discovered evidence.


OVERVIEW: The trial court properly refused to allow the introduction of two incidents reported to police internal affairs to show witness' pattern of behavior because the probative value of the evidence was marginal and was outweighed by its prejudicial effect under Nev. Rev. Stat. § 48.045(2). The trial court did not abuse its discretion in denying appellant's mistrial motion because any prejudice from the late delivery of the expert witness' reports was harmless and the expert was competent to give testimony regarding bullet trajectories. Appellant's due process rights were not violated because he failed to show that the state acted in bad faith when it failed to preserve or provide the truck used in the crime or the witness' clothing before they could be altered. Trial court did not abuse its discretion in denying appellant's motion for new trial because newly discovered statements and letters would not be likely to render a different probable result on retrial.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed because the trial court did not abuse its discretion in excluding witness' prior bad acts or denying motion for mistrial, defendant's due process rights were not violated when state failed to preserve evidence, and newly discovered evidence did not provide basis for new trial.

 

5 of 423 DOCUMENTS


County of Clark v. Buckwalter


No. 29477


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


115 Nev. 58; 974 P.2d 1162; 1999 Nev. LEXIS 14



April 9, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Denied March 20, 2000, Reported at: 2000 U.S. LEXIS 1924. Rehearing Denied October 1, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment upon a jury verdict and an order denying a motion for new trial in a condemnation action. Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County; Don P. Chairez, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant county government challenged the judgment of the Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County (Nevada), which held that respondent homeowners were entitled in an eminent domain proceeding to the "highest price," not the "probable price," for the value of their land.


OVERVIEW: Appellant enacted a eminent domain proceeding for respondents' land to build a convention center. Respondents refused to sell, and appellant sued under eminent domain. At trial, respondents convinced the trial judge to tell the jury they were entitled to the "highest price" on the value of their land, and not merely the "probable price." Appellant objected and challenged the jury verdict with a high award in respondents' favor. On appeal, the court reversed the trial judge. The court held that the legislature properly changed the definition upon which a jury may base its award from highest price to most probable price. The court determined that it was within the province of the legislature to change the definition and was not unconstitutional. The court concluded that the lower court error was not harmless and remanded for further proceedings.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the lower court and held that the trial judge erred in telling the jury to give respondents the highest value, and not the most probable value, for their land in an eminent domain proceeding.

 

6 of 423 DOCUMENTS


Middleton v. State


No. 31499


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


114 Nev. 1089; 968 P.2d 296; 1998 Nev. LEXIS 133



November 25, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of certiorari denied Middleton v. Nevada, 528 U.S. 927, 145 L. Ed. 2d 251, 120 S. Ct. 322, 1999 U.S. LEXIS 6871 (1999)
Post-conviction proceeding at, Remanded by Middleton v. Warden, 2004 Nev. LEXIS 98 (2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a judgment of conviction, pursuant to a jury verdict, of two counts of first-degree murder, two counts of first-degree kidnapping, one count of grand larceny, one count of fraudulent use of a credit card, and two counts of ex-felon in possession of a firearm and from two sentences of death. Second Judicial District Court, Washoe County; Peter I. Breen, Judge.
Sheriff, Washoe County v. Middleton, 112 Nev. 956, 921 P.2d 282, 1996 Nev. LEXIS 120 (1996)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of two counts of first-degree murder, two counts of kidnapping, and other offenses. Defendant appealed the judgment of conviction and two sentences of death imposed by the Second Judicial District Court, Washoe County (Nevada) based on the jury verdicts in the guilt and sentencing phases of the trial. Defendant appealed on grounds of insufficiency of evidence and alleged errors in the conduct of the trial.


OVERVIEW: At trial, the state presented evidence that defendant committed two separate murders, in each case abducting a woman from her home, holding her captive in a leased storage unit, killing her, and then dumping her body. On appeal, the court held (1) there was sufficient evidence that defendant committed the murders, kidnappings, and fraudulent use of a credit card, (2) the trial court under Nev. Rev. Stat. §§ 173.115 and 174.165(1) did not err in refusing to sever the counts relating to the two victims, (3) the holding of the trial two and a half years after defendant's arrest did not violate his U.S. Const. amend. VI right to a speedy trial because defendant was responsible for most of the delay, (4) the trial court did not err in admitting evidence of defendant's statements made to police, (5) the jury instruction on reasonable doubt was not unconstitutional, (6) alleged instances of prosecutorial misconduct did not prejudice defendant, (7) the evidence supported the finding of aggravating circumstances under Nev. Rev. Stat. § 177.055(2) and the death penalties imposed on defendant were not excessive, and (7) the state's death penalty statutes were constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment of conviction and the death sentences imposed on defendant.

LEARY v. CORPORATION LICENSED TO DO BUSINESS IN WEST VIRGINIA


No. 28609


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


114 Nev. 1031; 967 P.2d 432; 1998 Nev. LEXIS 131



November 25, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from an order of the district court denying appellants' motion for declaratory relief or for a determination that the judgments against them were in rem. Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County; Jeffrey D. Sobel, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, Nevada residents who made capital contributions as limited partners to a Nevada corporation, appealed from an order of the Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County (Nevada), which denied their motion for declaratory relief or for a determination that two West Virginia judgments obtained against them by respondent Texas corporation were in rem as to certain West Virginia property, and not in personam as to the limited partners.


OVERVIEW: Texas corporation filed suit against the limited partners and others, alleging it did not receive payment for drilling a well on the West Virginia property. The West Virginia court assumed personal jurisdiction over the non-resident defendants under West Virginia's long-arm statute. It later entered default judgments against several of the defendants, including limited partners. When Texas corporation attempted to enforce the judgments in Nevada, limited partners moved to dismiss the suit. The trial court dismissed the judgments, but the court reversed this decision, holding that West Virginia's notice provision did not violate their procedural due process rights. On remand, the limited partners filed the instant motion. On appeal, the court held the West Virginia complaint was sufficient to put limited partners on notice that Texas corporation was seeking personal judgments against them. However, the West Virginia court's exercise of in personam jurisdiction was improper because the limited partners lacked sufficient minimum contacts with that state. They were passive investors in a Nevada corporation and they never did business in West Virginia.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment.

CALAMBRO v. SECOND JUDICIAL DIST. COURT OF NEVADA


No. 32489, No. 32496


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


114 Nev. 961; 964 P.2d 794; 1998 Nev. LEXIS 115



September 25, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original postconviction petition for a writ of habeas corpus and appeal from a district court order denying a postconviction habeas petition. Second Judicial District Court, Washoe County; Steven P. Elliott, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Petition denied; order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant's mother (mother) challenged the decision of the Second Judicial District Court of Nevada, which denied her postconviction petition as next friend for a writ of habeas corpus, and petitioned for an original writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: A mother sought review of the lower court's denial of her postconviction petition as next friend for a writ of habeas corpus, and requested an original writ of habeas corpus. Defendant faced execution for two first-degree murder convictions and told the lower court at a competency hearing that he understood that he was going to be put to death and that he did not wish to challenge either his conviction or sentence. The court affirmed the denial of the mother's postconviction petition and denied the original petition because defendant was competent and the mother lacked standing as next friend.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of the mother's postconviction petition for a writ of habeas corpus, and denied her original petition for a writ of habeas corpus.

 

9 of 423 DOCUMENTS


Levingston v. Washoe County


No. 26265


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


114 Nev. 306; 956 P.2d 84; 1998 Nev. LEXIS 36



April 2, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for rehearing in an appeal from a final judgment in a forfeiture action. Second Judicial District Court, Washoe County; Mills Lane, Judge.

Original Opinion of April 30, 1996, Reported at 1996 Nev. LEXIS 67.



DISPOSITION: Rehearing granted; opinion modified; remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent county petitioned the court for a rehearing of its prior decision to reverse the judgment of the Second Judicial District Court, Washoe County (Nevada), which granted the civil forfeiture of appellant's interest in a house. The court's prior decision held that the forfeiture of the house under Nevada forfeiture statutes was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The civil forfeiture of the house was based on Nev. Rev. Stat. § 179.1158 et seq., which provided for forfeiture of housing linked to illegal drug activity. The court's prior decision in the matter held that forfeiture of the house, in addition to the criminal penalty imposed on the owners, violated the Double Jeopardy Clause. Since that time, the United States Supreme Court had rendered a decision, which provided a two-part test to determine whether the forfeiture of real estate in addition to a criminal penalty violated the Double Jeopardy Clause. The first part of the test required a determination of whether the legislature intended the forfeiture statutes to be civil or criminal. The court determined that the Nevada Legislature's intent was that its forfeiture statutes were civil. Secondly, the test required a showing, under the clearest proof, that the forfeiture was not punitive in fact, such as to indicate that it could not legitimately be seen as civil. The court held that there was no clear proof that the forfeiture was not civil in this case because it served the non-punitive goal of preventing further use of the house for illegal drug activities.


OUTCOME: The court granted rehearing and modified its previous opinion to conclude that the forfeiture of the property did not place the owners in double jeopardy. It remanded the case to the district court for review of whether the forfeiture violated the Excessive Fines Clause of the Eighth Amendment with respect to other ownership interests in the house.

 

10 of 423 DOCUMENTS


Sonner v. State


No. 26485


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


114 Nev. 321; 955 P.2d 673; 1998 Nev. LEXIS 37



April 2, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal dismissed by Sonner v. Warden, 116 Nev. 1408, 62 P.3d 1196, 2000 Nev. LEXIS 1479 (2000)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On rehearing, appeal from a judgment of conviction of one count of first-degree murder with use of a deadly weapon and a sentence of death and one count each of ex-felon in possession of a firearm, possession of a stolen vehicle, and resisting a public officer. Sixth Judicial District Court, Pershing County; Richard Wagner, Judge.

Original Opinion of December 20, 1996, Reported at: 112 Nev. 1328, 930 P.2d 707, 1996 Nev. LEXIS 173.
Sonner v. State, 112 Nev. 1328, 930 P.2d 707, 1996 Nev. LEXIS 173 (1996)



DISPOSITION: Rehearing granted in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of first-degree murder and other offenses and was sentenced to death. The court affirmed his judgment of conviction and sentence. Defendant sought a rehearing on a number of issues.


OVERVIEW: The court affirmed defendant's conviction of first-degree murder with use of a deadly weapon and corresponding death sentence. The court also affirmed defendant's convictions of being an ex-felon in possession of a firearm, possession of a stolen vehicle, and resisting a public officer. Defendant filed a motion for rehearing. The court denied the motion on the jury instruction issue because a jury instruction on the power of the Pardons Board to modify sentences had not prejudiced defendant because the prosecutor had not argued future dangerousness and the jury was not presented with a false choice between a death sentence or a limited term of incarceration. However, because of a change in the law under Nev. Const. art. 5, § 14(2); Nev. Rev. Stat. 213.085 (1995), the court instructed trial courts that could not longer give a previously approved instruction on sentence modification. Defendants other issue that the jury instructions improperly failed to instruct on aggravating circumstances, which was raised for the first time on rehearing, had no merit. The court held that it had not overlooked precedent on a prior recusal issue.


OUTCOME: The court held that a jury instruction on sentence modification had not prejudiced defendant and therefore denied rehearing on that issue. The court recognized that defendant had not abandoned issues relating to the non-murder counts but concluded those claims had no merit. It directed trial courts to no longer instruct juries on the matter of sentence modification. The court affirmed defendant's convictions and sentences.

 

11 of 423 DOCUMENTS


Browning v. Dixon


No. 29019


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


114 Nev. 213; 954 P.2d 741; 1998 Nev. LEXIS 17



February 26, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from an order of the district court denying appellant's motion to set aside a default judgment. Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County; Jack Lehman, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded with instructions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following an automobile accident, respondent filed a complaint against appellant and served the summons and complaint pursuant to the substitute service provisions of Nev. Rev. Stat. 14.070(2), and mailed a notice of service with the summons and complaint to appellant's incomplete address. Respondent obtained a default judgment. The Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County (Nevada) denied appellant's motion to set aside the default judgment.


OVERVIEW: After the accident, the parties exchanged information about their names, addresses, telephone numbers, and insurers. Appellant also gave respondent information about appellant's employer. The apartment number was included in the address that appellant gave to respondent. Appellant moved to a different residence, but his employer and employment address remained the same. Appellant informed the post office and Department of Motor Vehicles of his new residential address shortly after his move. The court concluded that respondent did not exercise due diligence in attempting to serve appellant. Respondent mailed his initial letter to appellant's incomplete address, reducing the likelihood that he would know that respondent was represented by counsel. Although respondent made "routine checks" to locate appellant, respondent made no apparent attempt to locate appellant through his employer or insurer, both of which were known to respondent. In so doing, respondent ignored other reasonable methods for locating appellant and failed, under the circumstances, to apprise appellant of the action pending against him.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the district court's order denying appellant's motion to set aside the default judgment entered against him. The court remanded the matter to the district court with instructions to set aside the default judgment.

 

12 of 423 DOCUMENTS


Sereika v. State


No. 28826


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


114 Nev. 142; 955 P.2d 175; 1998 Nev. LEXIS 23



February 26, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a judgment of conviction pursuant to a jury verdict of one count of driving under the influence of intoxicating liquor. First Judicial District Court, Carson City; Michael R. Griffin, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision of the First Judicial District Court, Carson City (Nevada) which entered a judgment of conviction pursuant to a jury verdict of one count of driving under the influence of intoxicating liquor in violation of Nev. Rev. Stat. § 484.379(1)(c).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of driving under the influence of intoxicating liquor pursuant to Nev. Rev. Stat. § 484.379(1)(c). Defendant sought review of his conviction, arguing that the statute was unconstitutionally vague and overbroad. The court concluded that the statute was not unconstitutionally vague. The court found that the statutory language was very specific, and defendant did not suggest any alternative interpretations as evidence of vagueness. The court also rejected defendant's argument that the statute was unconstitutionally overbroad. The court held that there was at least one conceivable rational basis for the enactment of the statute -- traffic safety. The court found that the state had a legitimate interest in preventing people from driving after ingesting any substance that would render them incapable of driving safely at any time in the following several hours. The court found that the statute was rationally related to this legitimate state interest, and was not overbroad with respect to the rising blood alcohol defense. The court affirmed the judgment entered by the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the district court convicting defendant of driving under the influence of intoxicating liquor because the statute prohibiting having a blood alcohol level above .10 within two hours of driving was neither vague nor overbroad.

 

13 of 423 DOCUMENTS


Department of Motor Vehicles & Pub. Safety v. Evans


No. 27947


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


114 Nev. 41; 952 P.2d 958; 1998 Nev. LEXIS 3



January 22, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from an order of the district court granting respondent's petition for judicial review and reinstating respondent's driving privileges. Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County; Donald M. Mosely, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded with instructions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the State of Nevada, Department of Motor Vehicles and Public Safety (DMV), sought review of an order of the Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County (Nevada), which granted respondent licensee's petition for judicial review of his license revocation and reinstated the licensee's driving privileges.


OVERVIEW: The licensee was arrested for driving under the influence of intoxicating liquor and refused to submit to a blood or breath test. The officer served him with notice of revocation of his driving privileges, and the licensee requested an administrative hearing. The hearing officer upheld the license revocation. The district court reversed the license revocation and ordered the reinstatement of the license. The court reversed and remanded with instructions that the revocation of the license privileges be reinstated. The court found that the hearing officer properly admitted hearsay evidence that consisted of one police officer's statement to the testifying officer as to whether the licensee was the driver of the vehicle. The evidence was of a type commonly relied upon by reasonable and prudent persons in the conduct of their affairs. The licensee was permitted to cross-examine the officer on any matter relevant to the issues. The DMV was only required to prove that the officer directing him to be tested had reasonable grounds to believe that the licensee had been driving while under the influence of alcohol.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order that reversed the license revocation and reinstated the licensee's license privileges. The court remanded with instructions to reinstate the revocation of the licensee's driving privileges.

 

14 of 423 DOCUMENTS


Calambro v. State


No. 29121


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


114 Nev. 106; 952 P.2d 946; 1998 Nev. LEXIS 8



January 22, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Denied February 22, 1999, Reported at: 1999 U.S. LEXIS 1173.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment of conviction entered pursuant to a guilty plea of first degree murder and a sentence of death. Second Judicial District Court, Washoe County; Peter I. Breen, Nancy A. Becker, Archie E. Blake, Judges.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the judgment of the Second Judicial District Court, Washoe County (Nevada), which convicted him of first-degree murder and sentenced him to death. The conviction was entered upon defendant's guilty plea.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contested the death sentence imposed for his first-degree murder conviction, claiming that the trial court erred in finding the following aggravating circumstances: 1) 16 prior felony convictions involving the use or threat of violence, under Nev. Rev. Stat. § 200.33(2); 2) that the murder involved depravity of mind and mutilation; and 3) that the murder was committed at random and without apparent motive. In affirming the judgment, the court ruled that under § 200.33(2) the pertinent date was the date of the conviction, not of the commission of the crime. Thus, though the acts leading to the felony convictions were committed after the murder, because the convictions therefor occurred prior to the conviction in this case, they were correctly considered by the trial court. The evidence that the victim was gagged and bound and his head smashed in through hammer blows supported the aggravating circumstance of depravity of mind and mutilation. Though the murder was committed shortly after a robbery, there was no error in finding that it was a random act without apparent motive because the killing did not take place until after the robbery was completed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment, which convicted defendant of first-degree murder and sentenced him to death.

 

15 of 423 DOCUMENTS


Anthony Lee R. v. State


No. 27772, No. 27889, No. 28130


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


113 Nev. 1406; 952 P.2d 1; 1997 Nev. LEXIS 161



December 30, 1997, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals from orders from the juvenile division of the district court certifying minors to adult status. Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County; Gerald W. Hardcastle, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Three juveniles challenged their certification for trial as adults by the Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County (Nevada). The juvenile court found that the juveniles had not established the exceptional circumstances required under Nev. Rev. Stat. 62.080(2)(b) (1995) that would prevent certification.


OVERVIEW: Three juveniles contested their transfer to adult court, two claiming that their crimes were the result of their substance abuse problems and one claiming that he was not the principal actor in an assault during a gang melee. The court on appeal found that the juvenile court had read Nev. Rev. Stat. 62.080(2)(b) (1995) too restrictively and ruled that the juveniles were not required to show that substance abuse caused their crimes, only that substance abuse substantially influenced their actions. The court further ruled that the third juvenile could not be a "principal actor" merely because he was involved in the melee and that his burden of proof on remand would involve showing only that he did not commit the assault and did not counsel others to commit it.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the certifications and remanded the cases to the juvenile court for reconsideration.

 

16 of 423 DOCUMENTS


Nika v. State


No. 27331


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


113 Nev. 1424; 951 P.2d 1047; 1997 Nev. LEXIS 159



December 30, 1997, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a judgment of conviction pursuant to a jury trial of one count of first degree murder with the use of a deadly weapon and from a sentence of death. Second Judicial District Court, Washoe County; Brent T. Adams, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury found the defendant guilty of first degree murder with the use of a deadly weapon. At the penalty hearing, the jury found that the murder was committed at random and without apparent motive, Nev. Rev. Stat. 200.033(9), and that there were no mitigating circumstances. The Second Judicial District Court of Washoe County (Nevada) entered judgment according to the verdict and sentenced the defendant to death. The defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The defendant challenged his conviction and sentence. The court held that a jury, acting reasonably, could have been convinced of the defendant's guilt beyond a reasonable doubt by the defendant's confession to his cell mate, the condition of the victim's body when it was discovered, blood spatters consistent with the victim's blood found on the defendant's clothing, his numerous inconsistent versions of the evening's events, and his statement to a sheriff that he had assaulted a man and the man was dead. The court examined the record on appeal, Nev. Rev. Stat. 177.055(2)(b), and held that the jury's finding that the defendant acted at random and without apparent motive, an aggravating circumstance under Nev. Rev. Stat. 200.033(9), was supported by the evidence. The court held that the sheriff's standardized questioning of the defendant as part of the placement process in order to determine what kind of threat, if any, he posed to other prisoners was not a custodial interrogation. As required by Nev. Rev. Stat. 177.055(2)(c) and (d), the court determined that the sentence was not imposed under the influence of passion, prejudice, or any arbitrary factor and was not excessive.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the defendant's conviction of first degree murder with the use of a deadly weapon and sentence of death.

 

17 of 423 DOCUMENTS


Rice v. State


No. 26111


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


113 Nev. 1300; 949 P.2d 262; 1997 Nev. LEXIS 153



November 20, 1997, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a judgment of conviction, pursuant to a jury trial, of one count of child neglect causing substantial bodily harm. Second Judicial District Court, Washoe County; Brent T. Adams, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part; remanded for a new sentencing hearing.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant accused child abuser challenged her conviction and sentence for felony child neglect, entered in the Second Judicial District Court, Washoe County (Nevada), on the grounds that the jury was improperly instructed with regard to willfulness and that the trial court erred by relying on impermissible evidence at her sentencing.


OVERVIEW: Appellant accused child abuser, convicted of felony child neglect after her husband was convicted of murdering their child, appealed her conviction and sentence. The court affirmed her conviction but reversed and remanded for resentencing. The trial court properly instructed the jury concerning the definition of willfully as used in Nev. Rev. Stat. 200.508 (1977). Child neglect was a general intent crime and respondent government did not have to prove that appellant intended to violate the law or injure her child. The evidence, which demonstrated that appellant knew or should have known that her delay in providing medical treatment was unreasonable and caused the child to suffer unjustifiable physical pain and mental suffering, established that appellant willingly committed the act or omission that constituted child neglect. The record also demonstrated, however, that at sentencing the trial court relied on her husband's presentence report, accepted statements therein, and used them in arriving at appellant's sentence. Accordingly, the court ruled that use of and reliance on her husband's presentence report without providing appellant with a copy constituted prejudicial error.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for felony child neglect below because the evidence supported the trial court's jury instruction on the issue of willfulness, but the court reversed and remanded for resentencing because at sentencing the trial court committed prejudicial error by relying on the presentence report of her husband, who had been convicted of murdering the child, without giving appellant a copy of the report.

 

18 of 423 DOCUMENTS


In re Davis


No. 27757


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


113 Nev. 1204; 946 P.2d 1033; 1997 Nev. LEXIS 142



October 1, 1997, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from final report of proceedings, findings of fact, conclusions of law, and decision of the Nevada Commission on Judicial Discipline removing appellant from his judicial office as municipal court judge for the City of North Las Vegas.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant municipal court judge challenged a decision of the Nevada Commission on Judicial Discipline, which removed him from office for multiple violations of the Nevada Code of Judicial Conduct. The judge asserted that the commission had no jurisdiction under Nev. Rev. Stat. 1.440(1) and that his due process rights under the Fifth and Fourteenth Amendments were violated.


OVERVIEW: A municipal court judge, during the period from 1981 to 1993, committed multiple ethical violations including borrowing money from his staff, soliciting charitable contributions in lieu of fines, conducting a personal antiques business from his office, and violating zoning laws. The court found that the commission had jurisdiction under Nev. Rev. Stat. 1.440(1) to order his removal because the statute was lawfully enacted under Nev. Const. art. 6, § 21(9)(d). The court further found that the lack of a limitations period did not violate the judge's due process rights because the commission considered his earlier actions only to show a recurring pattern of conduct. The court then held that the judge's Fifth Amendment rights were not violated where the commission considered his silence when he refused to answer questions to which the privilege could not apply. Finally, the court found that removal, rather than a lesser sanction, was appropriate and was supported by clear and convincing evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the removal from office of the municipal court judge.

 

19 of 423 DOCUMENTS


Barrios-Lomeli v. State


No. 27484


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


113 Nev. 952; 944 P.2d 791; 1997 Nev. LEXIS 120



August 28, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied July 28, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Nev. LEXIS 91.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment of conviction, pursuant to a guilty plea, of one count of trafficking in a controlled substance. First Judicial District Court, Carson City; Michael E. Fondi, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the decision from the First Judicial District Court, Carson City (Nevada), which convicted defendant, pursuant to a guilty plea, of one count of trafficking in a controlled substance. Defendant entered into a plea bargain, whereby he plead guilty to the felony charge, but reserved the right to appeal the trial court's denial of his motion to suppress.


OVERVIEW: An individual, arrested for the sale of a controlled substance, agreed to provide "substantial assistance" in arresting other narcotic traffickers. The individual informed the police that he had contacted defendant and that defendant was going to deliver a controlled substance. The individual gave the police a description of defendant, the model and color of the car that defendant would be driving, and the time and place of his arrival. The police arrived at the parking lot, detained defendant, and conducted a pat-down search. The police, without a warrant and without defendant's consent, searched his car and discovered the controlled substance. The court reversed and remanded, holding that: (1) although probable cause existed to support an anticipatory search warrant, the state's failure to do so did not require suppression of the seized evidence; (2) the trial court's reliance exclusively on federal law to uphold the warrantless search was error; (3) no exigency existed to justify a warrantless search of defendant's car; and (4) the one-hour statutory period of Nev. Rev. Stat. § 171.123(4) should have provided the police with an opportunity to procure a telephonic warrant.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction for one count of trafficking in a controlled substance for further proceedings and remanded the cause for further proceedings.

Worldcorp v. Department of Taxation


No. 28135


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


113 Nev. 1032; 944 P.2d 824; 1997 Nev. LEXIS 118



August 28, 1997, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from an order of the district court denying appellant's claim for a refund of sales and use taxes. First Judicial District Court, Carson City; Michael E. Fondi, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded with instructions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayers filed a claim for a refund of sales and use taxes paid to appellee state under protest. The First Judicial District Court, Carson City (Nevada) granted judgment in favor of the state. The taxpayer appealed.


OVERVIEW: The state revoked a sales and use tax exemption when the taxpayer airline's main office was relocated to another state. The taxpayers paid an additional assessment levied by the state under protest and a claim was filed for refund of the assessment as well as part of the previous taxes paid. The taxpayers claimed that gross receipts of the lease payments were exempt from sales and use tax under Nev. Rev. Stat. 372.317 or that 372.317 violated the Commerce Clause of the United States Constitution because it unfairly burdened interstate commerce by exempting from sales and use tax only those entities with central offices located in state. The district court ruled that two of the taxpayers did not have standing because they were not responsible for paying the tax, and the others could not challenge the exemption because as lessors of the aircraft they did not possess the proper air transportation certificate required by Nev. Rev. Stat. 372.317. The court reversed the order of the district court and held that it was the transaction itself that was exempted, not the parties to the transaction. The court struck the statute as unconstitutional for violating the Commerce Clause.


OUTCOME: The district court's judgment was reversed and remanded with directions for the district court to instruct the state to refund a stipulated amount of taxes.

Sun City Summerlin Community Ass'n v. State by & Through its Department of Taxation


No. 26419


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


113 Nev. 835; 944 P.2d 234; 1997 Nev. LEXIS 121



August 28, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied January 23, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from an order of the district court denying a petition for judicial review of a decision by the Nevada State Board of Equalization. Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County; Jeffrey D. Sobel, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant residential community sought review of an order from the Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County (Nevada), which denied a petition for judicial review of an order upholding tax assessments by respondent county.


OVERVIEW: The county assessed real property taxes against the residential community. The residential community appealed the assessments to the county board of equalization, which upheld the assessments. The residential community appealed the decision to the state board of equalization, which denied the appeal. The residential community then petitioned for judicial review, and the trial court denied the petition. On appeal, the court reversed the trial court's order and remanded for further proceedings. The court found that while Nev. Rev. Stat. § 116.1105(2)(b) applied to the case, the statute was unconstitutional insofar as it precluded taxation of common elements in a planned community. The court further found that restrictions on the use of the property were relevant to its valuation and that the county assessor erred in disregarding the restrictions in valuing the property.


OUTCOME: The order denying the residential community's petition for judicial review of the order upholding tax assessments was reversed and remanded for further proceedings.

 

22 of 423 DOCUMENTS


Ducksworth v. State


No. 25415


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


113 Nev. 780; 942 P.2d 157; 1997 Nev. LEXIS 94



July 15, 1997, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition denied by Ducksworth v. State, 114 Nev. 951, 966 P.2d 165, 1998 Nev. LEXIS 114 (1998)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Ducksworth v. State, 2010 Nev. Unpub. LEXIS 227 (2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals from separate judgments of conviction, pursuant to jury verdicts, of two counts of murder with use of a deadly weapon, two counts of first degree kidnapping with use of a deadly weapon, and one count each of burglary with use of a deadly weapon, sexual assault with use of deadly weapon, and robbery with use of a deadly weapon. Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County; Sally L. Loehrer, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part with regard to appellant Ducksworth; reversed and remanded with regard to appellant Martin.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed from separate judgments of the Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County (Nevada), which, pursuant to jury verdicts, convicted them of two counts of murder with use of a deadly weapon, two counts of first degree kidnapping with use of a deadly weapon, and one count each of burglary with use of a deadly weapon, sexual assault with use of a deadly weapon, and robbery with use of a deadly weapon.


OVERVIEW: Both defendants appealed their convictions on a variety of theories. On appeal, the court affirmed as to defendant on all convictions except one. The premeditation instruction given at the trial was constitutional because the instruction, which stated that premeditation could be formed instantaneously, did not misstate the amount of time necessary for premeditation. The court found that the evidence adduced at trial was sufficient for the jury to find defendant guilty of sexual assault, but insufficient to find him guilty of first degree kidnapping as to one victim. The evidence showed that the victim was dead before defendant moved his body. Because the sentence for the kidnapping ran concurrent to the sentences for the murder convictions, defendant's sentence was not reduced. As to co-defendant, the court reversed, holding that the trial court erred in refusing to grant a severance. The court found that co-defendant was prejudiced by joinder at trial with defendant because the evidence against co-defendant was largely circumstantial. Because defendant did not testify, the admission of his confession violated co-defendant's right of cross-examination under the Sixth Amendment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment as to all convictions of defendant except the conviction for kidnapping. As to co-defendant, the court reversed his convictions and remanded the case to the trial court for a new trial.

 

23 of 423 DOCUMENTS


Calloway v. City of Reno


No. 25628


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


113 Nev. 564; 939 P.2d 1020; 1997 Nev. LEXIS 71



May 22, 1997, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Granted December 3, 1998. Order Granting Rehearing of December 3, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Nev. LEXIS 170.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from district court orders granting summary judgment in a construction defect case. Second Judicial District Court, Washoe County; James A. Stone, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part, affirmed in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant homeowners asserted that their homes were built with defective framing that was responsible for extensive water damage from rain and snow. The homeowners sought review of orders of the Second Judicial District Court, Washoe County (Nevada) that summarily dismissed the homeowners' negligence and strict liability claims. Cross-appellant city sought review of the summary dismissal of its cross-claim for indemnity and contribution.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the court concluded that the district court's interpretation and application of the statute of repose and the district court's use of the economic loss doctrine to preclude the homeowner' negligence and strict liability claims were erroneous. With respect to the subcontractor and the city's cross-appeals, the court concluded that the district court's rulings were proper. The district court was bound by prior caselaw and improperly varied from that mandate by attempting to predict what future actions the legislature might take. Such predictions were improper. Thus, the homeowners should not have been allowed to pursue a strict products liability action against the subcontractors. The court concluded that a city inspector could not be held strictly liable for defects in construction that were approved by that inspector because a city and its inspectors are not in the business of supplying or manufacturing products that are later thrust into the stream of commerce. Accordingly, the district court properly dismissed the homeowner' strict liability claims against the subcontractors and the city.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the orders of the district court that summarily dismissed the city and the subcontractors' cross-claim. The court reversed the orders of the district court that summarily dismissed the actions brought by the class of homeowners whose homes were completed before the 1983 statute of repose enactment. The court remanded the case to the district court.

G & H Assocs. v. Ernest W. Hahn, Inc.


No. 27101


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


113 Nev. 265; 934 P.2d 229; 1997 Nev. LEXIS 29



February 26, 1997, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied July 22, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from an order granting summary judgment in an action concerning construction defects. Second Judicial District Court, Washoe County; Jerry Carr Whitehead, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant owners sought review of a decision of the Second Judicial District Court, Washoe County (Nevada), which determined that appellants' claims for negligence, willful misconduct and fraudulent concealment, breach of warranty, and breach of fiduciary duty against respondent builders barred by a statute of repose, Nev. Rev. Stat. 11.204.


OVERVIEW: After a roof section collapsed in appellant owners' commercial building, appellants brought suit against respondent builders for negligence, willful misconduct and fraudulent concealment, breach of warranty, and breach of fiduciary duty. The district court determined that the statute of repose, Nev. Rev. Stat. 11.204, barred appellants' claims. On appeal, the court affirmed as to all claims except that for willful misconduct and fraudulent concealment. If 1991 Nev. Stat., ch. 70, § 1.1, which made Nev. Rev. Stat. 11.204 retroactive, was unconstitutional only as applied to parties whose claims accrued prior to April 10, 1991, it was not unconstitutional as applied to appellants because their claim did not accrue until January 1993. If 1991 Nev. Stat., ch. 70, § 1.1 was unconstitutional in its entirety, appellants' claim was still barred by the amended version, 1995 Nev. Stat., ch. 449, § 1 at 1439-40, because their claim did not accrue for statute of limitations purposes prior to April 10, 1991. However, the claim for willful misconduct and fraudulent concealment could be brought at any time after the substantial completion of the improvement to real property.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that held that appellant owners' claims for negligence, breach of warranty, and breach of fiduciary duty against respondent builders were barred by a statute of repose, but remanded the claim for willful misconduct and fraudulent concealment, which could be brought anytime after completion of the building.

Browne v. State


No. 28378


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


113 Nev. 305; 933 P.2d 187; 1997 Nev. LEXIS 31



February 26, 1997, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari Denied October 6, 1997, Reported at: 1997 U.S. LEXIS 5568.
Writ of certiorari denied Browne v. Nevada, 522 U.S. 877, 118 S. Ct. 198, 139 L. Ed. 2d 136, 1997 U.S. LEXIS 5568 (1997)
Writ of habeas corpus denied, Decision reached on appeal by Browne v. Baker, 2013 U.S. App. LEXIS 23453 (9th Cir. Nev., Nov. 21, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a judgment of conviction and sentence of death, pursuant to a jury verdict. Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County; Lee A. Gates, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the decision of the Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County (Nevada), which convicted him of first degree murder with an aggravating factor of mutilation and sentenced him to death.


OVERVIEW: On review, appellant argued that certain statements made by the prosecutor during opening arguments constituted reversible error, certain hearsay statements were improperly admitted, jury instructions on mutilation were constitutionally infirm, and the evidence was insufficient to support his conviction. The court affirmed. The court found that the statements at issue did not amount to prosecutorial misconduct. The court also found that, even though certain statements which the victim made to her father could not be admitted as excited utterances, the trial court's error in admitting them was harmless and did not require a reversal. The court determined that the trial judge did not abuse his discretion when he admitted into evidence certain gruesome autopsy photos. The court concluded that the evidence was sufficient for any rational trier of fact to have found the essential elements of the crime beyond a reasonable doubt and, due to the severity of the beating, the jury could have concluded that appellant committed acts beyond the killing itself.


OUTCOME: Conviction for first degree murder with an aggravating factor of mutilation and subsequent death sentence was affirmed.

Gonzales v. Department of Human Servs., Div. of Child & Family Servs. (In re Gonzales)


No. 28637


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


113 Nev. 324; 933 P.2d 198; 1997 Nev. LEXIS 33



February 26, 1997, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from an order terminating appellant's parental rights. Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County; Gerald W. Hardcastle, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother sought review of an order from the Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County (Nevada), which terminated her parental rights pursuant to Nev. Rev. Stat. § 128.105 upon the court's finding of child abandonment, failure of parental adjustment, and its determination that the children's best interest were served by termination.


OVERVIEW: On review, the court held that the mother's assignments of error were without merit and accordingly affirmed. The court found that clear and convincing evidence established the requisite jurisdictional and dispositional grounds for the termination of the mother's parental rights. The court noted that the mother's conduct in disappearing from her children's lives for a one-year period of time satisfied the definition of abandonment in Nev. Rev. Stat. § 128.012 and that she did not rebut the presumption of Nev. Rev. Stat. § 128.012(2). The court further noted that the record contained evidence supporting a finding of failure of parental adjustment, as the mother failed to comply with the case plan in that she disappeared from one year, during which time she failed to visit her children, failed to maintain contact with the relevant state agency, and failed to provide support for her children. The court concluded by noting that the dispositional grounds for termination had been established by the finding that under no reasonable circumstances would the children's best interests be served by sustaining the parental tie.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment terminating the parental rights of the mother.

Rehearing denied by, 12/17/1997
Writ denied by, Motion denied by Crump v. First Judicial Dist. Court, 114 Nev. 590, 958 P.2d 1200, 1998 Nev. LEXIS 69 (1998)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from an order of the district court denying petition for writ of habeas corpus. First Judicial District Court, Carson City; Michael R. Griffin, Judge.
Crump v. State, 102 Nev. 158, 716 P.2d 1387, 1986 Nev. LEXIS 1122 (1986)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, petitioner for habeas corpus, sought review of an order from the First Judicial District Court, Carson City (Nevada), which denied appellant's second petition for post-conviction relief.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of first degree murder and robbery with use of a deadly weapon and was sentenced to death. The conviction and sentence was affirmed on direct appeal. Appellant filed a petition for post-conviction relief and was appointed counsel pursuant to Nev. Rev. Stat. 177.345(1). After an evidentiary hearing, the post-conviction petition was dismissed. Appellant then filed a petition for a writ of habeas corpus, which set forth several allegations of ineffective counsel during the post-conviction proceedings. The district court found that the petition was procedurally barred because the issues could have been raised on direct appeal or in the post-conviction petition. Appellant claimed on appeal that ineffectiveness of post-conviction counsel established cause to preclude application of any procedural bar. The court agreed with appellant's claims. OUTCOME: The court reversed the dismissal of appellant's petition for a writ of habeas corpus. The court ruled that appellant was entitled to effective assistance of counsel for his post-conviction petition and that an evidentiary hearing was necessary to determine with post-conviction counsel's failure to raise certain issues constituted ineffective assistance of counsel.

Related proceeding at Greene v. State, 122 Nev. 1680, 178 P.3d 760, 2006 Nev. LEXIS 1047 (2006)
Habeas corpus proceeding at, Motion denied by, Motion granted by, Stay granted by Greene v. McDaniel, 2009 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 13849 (D. Nev., Feb. 6, 2009)
Related proceeding at Greene v. Dist. Court (Warden), 125 Nev. 1040, 281 P.3d 1177, 2009 Nev. LEXIS 406 (2009)
Habeas corpus proceeding at, Decision reached on appeal by Winfrey v. State, 2011 Nev. Unpub. LEXIS 344 (2011)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Greene v. State, 2016 Nev. LEXIS 595 (Nev., June 24, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Consolidated appeal from judgments of conviction for two counts of murder with use of a deadly weapon, conspiracy to commit murder, and possession of a stolen vehicle. Appellant Greene was sentenced to death for each murder and appellant Winfrey was sentenced to life without the possibility of parole for each murder. Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County; Gene T. Porter, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed judgments from the Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County (Nevada), which convicted them of two counts of murder with use of a deadly weapon, conspiracy to commit murder, and possession of a stolen vehicle.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were convicted of two counts of murder with use of a deadly weapon, conspiracy to commit murder, and possession of a stolen vehicle. Defendants appealed their convictions, alleging several points of error. One defendant argued that the prosecutor improperly elicited testimony from a witness which constituted prior bad acts testimony not falling under any exception enumerated in Nev. Rev. Stat. 48.045(2). The court held that the determination of whether to admit evidence of separate or criminal acts was within the sound discretion of the trial court, and the evidence was not required to fit under an exception under 48.045(2). The defendant also asserted that the prosecutor engaged in prejudicial, passionate, and improper argument to the jury under the guise of an opening statement, and that the augment violated defendant's right to a fair trial. The court determined that a criminal conviction was not to be lightly overturned on the basis of a prosecutor's comments standing alone. The court held that the prosecutor's remarks did not rise to the level of improper argument that would have justified overturning the conviction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendants' convictions.

Geary v. State


No. 24277


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


112 Nev. 1434; 930 P.2d 719; 1996 Nev. LEXIS 163



December 20, 1996, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Rehearing granted in part, denied in part; Reported at: 1998 Nev. LEXIS 2.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On rehearing, appeal from a judgment of conviction, entered pursuant to a jury verdict, of one count of first-degree murder with use of a deadly weapon, and from a sentence of death. Second Judicial District Court, Washoe County; Mills Lane, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Rehearing granted; sentence vacated and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The trial court convicted defendant of first-degree murder and sentenced him to death. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgments of conviction and sentence. Defendant petitioned for a rehearing on the bases that errors occurred in both the guilt and sentencing phases. The court granted defendant's petition for rehearing.


OVERVIEW: In reversing, the court rejected defendant's contention that the jury instructions provided during the guilt phase were improper. The court held, however, that the jury instruction regarding the possibility of commuting defendant's sentence from life without, to life with the possibility of parole was misleading, prejudicial, and violated defendant's constitutional rights to due process and a reliable sentence. The court held that aggravating circumstance instruction, that defendant committed the murder at random and without apparent motive, was applied in an unconstitutional manner to the facts of defendant's case. The court held that defendant's right against double jeopardy was not violated by the finding of two aggravating circumstances based on the same prior conviction. The court held that the jury instruction regarding the imposition of the death penalty was in error, because it may not have adequately conveyed to the jury that it was not required to impose the death penalty regardless of the presence or absence of aggravating or mitigating circumstances. Lastly, the court found error in penalty phase instruction as to when sentence would be carried out.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the sentence and remanded the case.

Sonner v. State


No. 26485


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


112 Nev. 1328; 930 P.2d 707; 1996 Nev. LEXIS 173



December 20, 1996, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Granted April 2, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from judgment of conviction pursuant to jury verdict on one count of first-degree murder with use of a deadly weapon and from sentence of death; and judgments of conviction on one count of being an ex-felon in possession of a firearm, one count of possession of a stolen vehicle, and one count of resisting a public officer. Sixth Judicial District Court, Pershing County; Richard A. Wagner, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Sixth Judicial District Court, Pershing County (Nevada) entered a judgment of conviction against defendant for first-degree murder with use of a deadly weapon, being an ex-felon in possession of a firearm, possession of a stolen vehicle, and resisting a public officer in connection with the shooting death of a trooper. He was sentenced to death. Defendant challenged the judgment of conviction and imposition of the death penalty.


OVERVIEW: The driver of a stolen car pumped gas and left without paying. The trooper who halted the car, was found on the ground with a gunshot wound to his head, and his pistol was still in its holster. The stolen car was seen pulling away from the scene. Defendant was found several miles therefrom. He argued that the jury charge on the State Board of Pardons Commissioners' power to modify sentences, the denial of his motions to recuse and disqualify the judge, and the admission of certain statements were erroneous. The court held (1) the jury charge was proper under Nev. Rev. Stat. § 175.161(7) (amended 1995), and defendant was not prejudiced thereby; (2) the denial of the motion to recuse the district judge and to disqualify the prosecutor was proper because there was no indication of extrajudicial bias; (3) the refusal to change venue was proper because defendant did not show actual prejudice from pre-trial publicity or bias by the jury, which assured that it would be fair and impartial in its deliberations; and (4) defendant's incriminating statement in the patrol car and in jail were voluntary because there was no state action tending to exploit his mental state.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of convictions and sentencing.

Flanagan v. State


No. 27320


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


112 Nev. 1409; 930 P.2d 691; 1996 Nev. LEXIS 166



December 20, 1996, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied November 21, 1997.
Certiorari Denied April 20, 1998, Reported at: 1998 U.S. LEXIS 2677 and Reported at: 1998 U.S. LEXIS 2678.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals from a district court order denying habeas corpus relief and appeals from judgments of conviction of first degree murder and sentences of death entered on remand. Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County; Addeliar D. Guy, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants sought review of a decision of the Eighth Judicial Court, Clark County (Nevada), which denied their applications for habeas corpus relief, and their appeals from judgments of conviction of first degree murder and sentences of death entered on remand, due to improper evidence admitted before the jury in the penalty phase.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were convicted of first degree murder and were sentenced to death. Their death sentences were twice vacated and remanded, first due to prosecutorial misconduct, and then due to the admission of evidence before the jury in the penalty phase regarding their occult beliefs and activities. Defendants filed habeas corpus petitions seeking to overturn their convictions based on the same improper evidence and filed motions to strike their sentences, all of which the district court denied. Defendants were sentenced to death a third time, and the court ordered joint review of their appeals of their convictions and the denials of habeas corpus review. The court affirmed and held that although the prosecution violated defendants' First Amendment rights by referring to their occult beliefs in closing argument at the guilt phase, the Dawson violation was harmless because there was other overwhelming evidence of defendants' guilt and the jury could not be influenced by irrelevant character evidence at the guilt phase. The court concluded that substantial evidence supported the jury's finding of aggravating circumstances to sustain a proper sentence of death.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the district court's order denying defendants' habeas corpus relief and affirmed the judgments of conviction of first degree murder. The court again affirmed defendants' death sentences, having previously concluded the sentences were not excessive in light of the crimes and the characteristics of defendants.

Smith v. State


No. 26260


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


112 Nev. 1269; 927 P.2d 14; 1996 Nev. LEXIS 155



November 7, 1996, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a judgment of conviction of abuse or neglect of a child. Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County; Myron E. Leavitt, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed her conviction in the Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County (Nevada) under Nev. Rev. Stat. § 200.508(1)(a), (b) or Nev. Rev. Stat. § 432B.140 for neglect or abuse of a child in connection with the death of her son at her boyfriend's hand.


OVERVIEW: On appeal from defendant's conviction for neglect or abuse of a child, the court affirmed the conviction. Defendant did not satisfy her burden to prove that Nev. Rev. Stat. § 200.508(1)(a), (b) was unconstitutionally vague because all of the terms were adequately defined, including the state of mind requirements of knowledge and reasonableness. It was untenable for defendant to claim that she could not reasonably have known that she criminally allowed her child to suffer physical pain or mental suffering where it was shown that her son's body had bruises predating the fatal beating, she saw the bruises from the fatal beating, she knew that he was listless, vomiting, and feverish following the beating, and she returned the child to her boyfriend's care. The evidence was sufficient to convict defendant solely under § 200.508(1)(a), because she allowed her boyfriend to take care of her son immediately following the fatal beating, of which she had knowledge. Further, given the facts, it was untenable for defendant to argue that she did not know her repeated refusal to obtain medical treatment for her son was criminal under Nev. Rev. Stat. § 432B.140.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for neglect or abuse of a child in connection with the death of her son at her boyfriend's hand.

Evans v. Nev.


No. 26679


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


112 Nev. 1172; 926 P.2d 265; 1996 Nev. LEXIS 152



October 22, 1996, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied December 13, 1996.
Writ of certiorari denied Evans v. Nevada, 520 U.S. 1245, 117 S. Ct. 1854, 137 L. Ed. 2d 1056, 1997 U.S. LEXIS 3339 (May 27, 1997)
Post-conviction relief granted at, in part, Remanded by Evans v. State, 117 Nev. 609, 28 P.3d 498, 2001 Nev. LEXIS 54 (2001)
Writ of habeas corpus denied, Certificate of appealability denied Evans v. McDaniel, 2008 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 34854 (D. Nev., Mar. 17, 2008)
Habeas corpus proceeding at, Decision reached on appeal by Evans v. State, 2011 Nev. Unpub. LEXIS 431 (2011)
Writ of habeas corpus dismissed Evans v. State, 2013 Nev. Unpub. LEXIS 1569 (2013)
Related proceeding at Evans v. State, 2017 Nev. Unpub. LEXIS 71 (Jan. 30, 2017)
Related proceeding at Evans v. State, 2017 Nev. App. Unpub. LEXIS 228 (Nev. Ct. App., Apr. 18, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from judgment of conviction, pursuant to a jury verdict, of one count of burglary, and four counts of first-degree murder with use of a deadly weapon; from four death sentences; and from the denial of a motion for an acquittal notwithstanding the verdict. Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County; Jeffrey D. Sobel, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County (Nevada), which convicted him, pursuant to a jury verdict, of one count of burglary, and four counts of first-degree murder with use of a deadly weapon, entered four death sentences, and denied defendant's motion for an acquittal notwithstanding the verdict.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed from his conviction for burglary and four counts of first-degree murder, and the resulting four death sentences. The court affirmed, finding there was no evidence that, despite witness sequestration, the State's witness was influenced by the testimony given in his presence, and the trial court did not abuse its discretion in determining that the State had shown good cause for its non-compliance with Nev. Rev. Stat. § 174.087. "Weighty affairs" jury instruction language did not create a reasonable likelihood that the jury applied the instruction unconstitutionally where the jury was also instructed regarding the State's burden of proof and the presumption of innocence. The court found sufficient evidence upon which to base defendant's conviction, and the trial judge used the correct standard in denying his motion for an acquittal notwithstanding the verdict. Finally, there was sufficient evidence to justify the jury's finding of aggravating circumstances to support the imposition of the death penalty.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for burglary and four counts of first-degree murder, and the resulting four death sentences, concluding that defendant was fairly tried, convicted and sentenced.

Atkins v. State


No. 27169


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


112 Nev. 1122; 923 P.2d 1119; 1996 Nev. LEXIS 135



August 28, 1996, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected August 28, 1996. Rehearing Denied October 17, 1996. Certiorari Denied March 17, 1997, Reported at: 1997 U.S. LEXIS 1799.
Rehearing denied by, 10/17/1996
Writ of certiorari denied Atkins v. Nevada, 520 U.S. 1126, 117 S. Ct. 1267, 137 L. Ed. 2d 346, 1997 U.S. LEXIS 1799 (Mar. 17, 1997)
Related proceeding at, Sub nomine at Doyle v. State, 116 Nev. 148, 995 P.2d 465, 2000 Nev. LEXIS 16 (Feb. 3, 2000)
Post-conviction proceeding at Atkins v. State, 118 Nev. 1081, 106 P.3d 1203, 2002 Nev. LEXIS 114 (May 14, 2002)
Post-conviction relief denied at Atkins v. State, 2014 Nev. Unpub. LEXIS 650 (Apr. 23, 2014)
Writ of habeas corpus dismissed, in part, Motion denied by, in part, Motion denied by Atkins v. Filson, 2017 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 162528 (D. Nev., Sept. 28, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment of conviction, pursuant to a jury verdict, for murder, conspiracy to commit murder, first degree kidnapping, and sexual assault, and from one sentence of death. Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County; Addeliar D. Guy III, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County (Nevada) that convicted him of murder, conspiracy to commit murder, first-degree kidnapping, and sexual assault, and sentenced him to death for the murder conviction.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, among other claims, that the evidence was insufficient to support the conviction for sexual assault, and that it was error to admit prior inconsistent statements of his co-conspirator and evidence of the death of the victim's infant child. The court reversed the conviction for sexual assault and affirmed the remaining convictions. The court found that sexual assault as defined in Nev. Rev. Stat. § 200.366(1) required penetration, as defined in Nev. Rev. Stat. § 200.364(2), and that the penetration had to occur while the victim was alive. The court found no evidence in this case that the victim was alive at the time of the sexual penetration. The court determined that the inconsistent statements were admissible pursuant to Nev. Rev. Stat. § 51. 035(2)(a) and (b). The court explained that while § 51.035(2)(b) required that the witness be recalled to the stand to explain or deny his prior inconsistent statements, the State's failure to do so was harmless error. The court found that the evidence relating to the previous death of the victim's child was relevant to explain her depressed state of mind and drug use and was admissible pursuant to Nev. Rev. Stat. § 48.015.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of conviction for sexual assault and affirmed the judgment of conviction for first-degree murder, conspiracy to commit murder, and first-degree kidnapping, and the sentence of death.

Lippis v. Peters


No. 26575


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


112 Nev. 1008; 921 P.2d 1248; 1996 Nev. LEXIS 127



August 16, 1996, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from an order of the district court granting a motion for summary judgment, and an order awarding attorney's fees. Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County; Lee A. Gates, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant justices' courts and individual justices of the peace (justices') sought review of the order of the Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County (Nevada), which declared JCRCP 106 and Nev. Rev. Stat. § 40.253 to be unconstitutional, enjoined the justices to hold hearings in all cases in which tenants file an affidavit in opposition to eviction proceedings, and awarded attorneys' fees to the tenants.


OVERVIEW: In an action against the justices' courts and the justices challenging their summary eviction proceedings, the district court granted summary judgment and attorney fees to the tenants. On appeal, the court affirmed in part and reversed in part the order of the district court. JCRCP 106 was unconstitutional because it violated Nev. Const. art VI, § 6 and Nev. Const. art. IV, § 21. Consequently, henceforth, judgments of the justices' courts in summary eviction actions would be appealable to the district court. Nev. Rev. Stat. § 40.253 was constitutional. Insofar as the district court's judgment intimated that the federal and Nevada constitutions required "pre-deprivation" hearings as a condition to every summary eviction order, such judgment was of no effect. Tenants were entitled to a pre-deprivation hearing in summary eviction proceedings only when they properly requested such a hearing by filing an affidavit showing that the tenant had either tendered payment or is not in default in payment of rent. The award of attorneys' fees was reversed because this was not a 42 U.S.C. S. § 1983 claim and there was no other claim that served as a basis for attorneys' fees.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part and reversed in part the order of the district court in favor of the tenants.
