Miller v. Warden, Nevada State Prison


No. 27566


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


112 Nev. 930; 921 P.2d 882; 1996 Nev. LEXIS 117



July 22, 1996, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original petition for writ of habeas corpus.



DISPOSITION: Petition granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner prisoner filed a petition for a writ ordering the pardons board to consider his application for commutation without regard to Nev. Rev. Stat. § 213.085(1) and challenging § 213.085(1), which revoked the pardons board's power to commute a life sentence without the possibility of parole and which applied retroactively, on the ground that it constituted an unconstitutional ex post facto law.


OVERVIEW: In 1983, the prisoner was sentenced to life in prison without the possibility of parol after he pled guilty to first degree murder. In 1995, the state legislature passed § 213.085(1), which revoked the power of the pardons board to commute a sentence of life without the possibility of parol and which applied retroactively to anyone serving a "life without" sentence without the possibility of parol for first degree murder. After the pardons board denied the prisoner's application for commutation of his sentence, the prisoner filed a petition for a writ challenging the statute on the ground that it applied retroactively and thus violated the ex post facto clause of the federal and state constitutions. The court issued a writ declaring § 213.085(1) invalid, holding that § 213.085(1), to the extent that it applied retroactively, violated the ex post facto clause because it increased the measure of punishment for the covered crime of first-degree murder. The court found that the statute denied the prisoners affected by it the right to seek commutation without regard to whether or not their applications may have been futile.


OUTCOME: The court issued a writ declaring the statute, which revoked the power of the pardons board to commute a sentence of life without the possibility of parole to a sentence that would allow parole, invalid to the extent that it applied retroactively. However, the court declined to order the pardons board to reconsider the prisoner's application for commutation because the pardons board was not a party to the action.

 

37 of 423 DOCUMENTS


STATE v. HIATT


No. 24820


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


112 Nev. 868; 920 P.2d 116; 1996 Nev. LEXIS 118



July 22, 1996, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from an order of the district court reversing an administrative decision revoking respondent's driving privileges. Third Judicial District Court, Churchill County; Mario G. Recanzone, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Department of Motor Vehicles sought review of an order of the Third Judicial District Court, Churchill County (Nevada), which reversed an administrative decision revoking respondent driver's license.


OVERVIEW: A police officer stopped the driver after observing his car weaving and crossing over the center line. The driver failed preliminary tests, and he was arrested for driving under the influence. His blood test showed a blood alcohol content in excess of the legal limit. The department revoked his license under Nev. Rev. Stat. § 484.384, and the revocation was affirmed after a hearing. The driver appealed. The district court reversed, holding that § 484.384 was unconstitutional as applied. The department appealed. In reversing and remanding, the court held that (1) the scope of review of a license revocation order was limited to the issues of whether the person failed to submit to an evidentiary test or had 0.10 percent or more by weight of alcohol in his blood at the time of the test; (2) the legislature chose to apply different standards for revoking driving privileges in a civil proceeding under § 484.384 than for a conviction for driving under the influence under Nev. Rev. Stat. § 484.379; (3) the legislative choice was reasonably related to the legitimate, compelling state interest of reducing alcohol-related accidents, and (4) Nev. Rev. Stat. § 484.384 was constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order and remanded the case to the district court with instruction to reinstate the administrative revocation of the driver's license.

Doyle v. State


No. 27146


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


112 Nev. 879; 921 P.2d 901; 1996 Nev. LEXIS 124



July 22, 1996, FILED

Writ of habeas corpus denied Doyle v. State, 2015 Nev. Unpub. LEXIS 1126 (2015)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a judgment of conviction, pursuant to a jury verdict, of one count each of first-degree murder, conspiracy to commit murder, first-degree kidnaping, and sexual assault. Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County; Addeliar D. Guy, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of conviction by the Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County (Nevada), of one count each of first-degree murder, conspiracy to commit murder, first-degree kidnapping, and sexual assault. The jury found several aggravating circumstances and imposed a sentence of death and consecutive life terms for first-degree kidnapping and sexual assault, and a concurrent six-year term for conspiracy to commit murder.


OVERVIEW: The court in part affirmed the lower court's judgment because it found that the State did not improperly use its peremptory challenges to remove black venirepersons from the jury pool. The court found that defendant failed to make the requisite showing under Batson. The court found that although defendant made a prima facie showing of racial discrimination by showing that the State exercised two of its peremptory challenges to strike black venirepersons, the State presented a race neutral explanation in support of its exercise of the of the peremptory challenges. The court further found that defendant failed to show that the State's explanation was pretextual. The court found that the evidence was sufficient to support defendant's conviction for first-degree kidnapping, and conspiracy to commit murder. However the court reversed the judgment of the lower court finding defendant guilty of sexual assault because it determined that defendant's conviction for sexual assault was not supported by substantial evidence because it was not clear whether the victim was alive at the time of the sexual assault.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part and reversed in part the judgment of the lower court.

State v. Justice Court


No. 27476


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


112 Nev. 803; 919 P.2d 401; 1996 Nev. LEXIS 98



June 24, 1996, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original petition for writ of prohibition. Justice Court of the Las Vegas Township, Clark County; William P. Jansen, Justice of the Peace.



DISPOSITION: Petition granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Real party in interest defendant was charged with sexual assault of a minor and with lewdness with a minor. Defendant filed a motion requesting respondent, Justice Court of the Las Vegas Township (Nevada), to order a physical examination of the victim. The justice court granted the motion and petitioner state filed a petition for a writ of prohibition.


OVERVIEW: The state's petition for a writ of prohibition sought an order vacating the justice court's order and prohibiting the justice court from granting discovery requests prior to a preliminary hearing. The state argued the justice court did not have express or inherent authority to order discovery in criminal actions prior to a preliminary hearing. The court agreed and granted the writ of prohibition. The justice courts were courts of limited jurisdiction whose authority was dictated by statute. No statute gave the justice courts the authority to order discovery prior to a preliminary hearing in a criminal action. The court also found that the role of the justice court at a preliminary hearing was limited to finding whether probable cause existed and that the justice court could not order discovery at a preliminary hearing. The justice court could not obtain jurisdiction via a stipulation by the state because waiver or stipulation could not cure a lack of jurisdiction.


OUTCOME: The court granted the state's petition for a writ of prohibition.

Colwell v. State


No. 27570


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


112 Nev. 807; 919 P.2d 403; 1996 Nev. LEXIS 99



June 24, 1996, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied February 27, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a sentence of death following a plea of guilty to one count of murder in the first degree. Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County; Gene T. Porter, Michael R. Griffin, Jerry Carr Whitehead, Judges.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant's counsel sought review of a conviction from the Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County (Nevada), for murder in the first degree and a sentence of death pursuant to Nev. Rev. Stat. 200.010, 200.020, 200.030. Defendant asked to appear pro se and actively sought the death penalty at his trial. On appeal, defendant's counsel brought seven grounds alleging unconstitutionality.


OVERVIEW: In reviewing defendant's trial and sentence, the court concluded that defendant was entitled to represent himself however he wished, whether that was by introducing mitigating evidence, by not introducing such evidence, or even by actively seeking the death penalty, and his actions did not render the resulting sentence unconstitutional. The court concluded that because there was no requirement that defendant present mitigating evidence or put on a defense in a death penalty hearing, there could be no infirmity in the record on review if it did not contain mitigating evidence and, therefore, the court could meaningfully review defendant's death sentence. The court held that the three-judge panel was constitutional because the Nevada Constitution did not prohibit the legislature from providing that district judges must act as a collegial body in the exercise of such judicial functions as sentencing. The court concluded from the record that the aggravating circumstances used by the panel to impose the death sentence sufficiently narrowed defendant's death eligibility determination, and the sentence was not prejudicially imposed, nor was it excessive. The death sentence was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's death sentence for murder in the first degree, holding that defendant, acting pro se at trial, was entitled to actively seek the death penalty, and that did not make the sentence unconstitutional.

Binegar v. Eighth Judicial Dist. Court


No. 27579


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


112 Nev. 544; 915 P.2d 889; 1996 Nev. LEXIS 80



May 1, 1996, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for writ of mandamus or in the alternative writ of prohibition challenging an order of the district court denying respondents' motion for a protective order. Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County; Lee A. Gates, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Statute declared unconstitutional.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner challenged the order from respondent, the Eighth Judicial District Court of the State of Nevada, which denied his motion for a protective order against real party in interest state. He filed an original petition for a writ of mandamus or in the alternative a writ of prohibition and challenged the constitutionality of Nevada's reciprocal discovery statute, codified as amendments to Nev. Rev. Stat. 151 et seq. (1995).


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was charged with one count of first degree murder. The trial judge determined that Nevada's reciprocal discovery statute, codified as amendments to Nev. Rev. Stat. 151 et seq. (1995), was constitutional except for Nev. Rev. Stat. 174.245(2). The trial judge denied petitioner's motion for a protective order and ordered him and his counsel to turn over to the prosecutor the names and addresses of the prospective witnesses they intended to call at trial. The petitioner argued that Nev. Rev. Stat. 151 et seq. was unconstitutional. The court concluded that the petitioner's contentions had merit and held that: 1.) The issue was not moot, because it was capable of repetition, yet evading review; 2.) As written, Nev. Rev. Stat. 174.089(1) and 174.235(2) presented Fifth Amendment violations; and 3.) Nev. Rev. Stat. 174.089(2) and 174.245(2) could not be sustained, because the scope and object of Nev. Rev. Stat. 151 et seq. was defeated with the rejection of Nev. Rev. Stat. 174.089(1) and 174.235(2).


OUTCOME: The court declared the challenged statute unconstitutional and held that issuance of a writ would have provided no effective relief for the petitioner, because by virtue of the court's stay order, the statute was never applied to him. Accordingly, it was unnecessary to issue the requested writ. Nevertheless, the decision constituted the court's final decision respecting the important public policy issue of whether the statute was constitutional.

Blume v. State


No. 24671


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


112 Nev. 472; 915 P.2d 282; 1996 Nev. LEXIS 63



April 30, 1996, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a judgment of conviction pursuant to a guilty plea of felony driving under the influence of alcohol with four prior convictions. Third Judicial District Court, Churchill County; Archie E. Blake, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Criminal appellant sought review of the judgment of the Third Judicial District Court, Churchill County (Nevada), which convicted appellant of felony driving under the influence of alcohol.


OVERVIEW: Appellant entered a guilty plea to one count of felony driving under the influence of alcohol with four prior convictions. The memorandum of plea bargain provided that in exchange for entering a guilty plea, appellant reserved the right to argue the validity of his former convictions. Appellant contended that the trial court erred in admitting his four prior convictions at the sentencing phase of the trial because they took place in another state. Appellant contended that the elements of the crimes were different because Nevada's blood alcohol percentage for the offense was .10, while the other state's legal limit was .08 percent. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment of conviction. The court held that all four previous convictions were properly admitted. Driving under the influence in another state, even though the blood alcohol limit was .02 percent lower than in Nevada constituted "the same or similar conduct" as driving under the influence of intoxicating liquor in Nevada, pursuant to Nev. Rev. Stat. § 484.3792(8).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's judgment of conviction.

Wesley v. State

SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


112 Nev. 503; 916 P.2d 793; 1996 Nev. LEXIS 78

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury convicted defendant of robbery with a deadly weapon and two counts of murder with a deadly weapon. Based upon the jury's recommendation, the Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County (Nevada), sentenced defendant to death. Defendant challenged his conviction and sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant alleged 16 points of error. The court first held that the trial court acted properly by refusing to recuse the deputy district attorney, the trial court was not manifestly wrong in ruling that defendant's prior convictions would have been admissible if defendant had testified, and the trial court did not abuse its discretion when it denied defendant's request for a continuance. The court determined that the district attorney did not imply that defendant had threatened a witness and the State's arguments regarding reasonable doubt were harmless. The court also held that the depravity of mind aggravator was properly submitted to the jury, the death penalty statute was constitutional, the jury instructions given by the trial court were proper, and victim impact evidence was correctly admitted.

Levingston v. Washoe County by & Through the Sheriff of Washoe County


No. 26265


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


112 Nev. 479; 916 P.2d 163; 1996 Nev. LEXIS 67



April 30, 1996, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Granted April 2, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a final judgment in a civil forfeiture action. Second Judicial District Court, Washoe County; Mills Lane, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, individually and as administrator of decedent's estate, sought review of a judgment of the Second Judicial District Court, Washoe County (Nevada), finding for respondent county in its civil forfeiture complaint. The county seized the house without formally notifying the owners.


OVERVIEW: The county seized a house based on illegal drug activity without formally notifying the three owners or the administrator, who had a lien on the property. On appeal, the administrator challenged the district court's order by contending that Nevada's civil forfeiture statutes violated the Due Process, Double Jeopardy, and Excessive Fines Clauses of the United States Constitution. The court reversed in part and remanded. The court that found that seizure of real property without notice or a hearing could only occur in the most exigent of circumstances. These were not present in the case at bar because the county failed to show that the threat to neighborhood safety justified the seizure of real property without notice or a hearing. The seizure pursuant to Nev. Rev. Stat. 179.1165(c) violated the Due Process Clause, yet it was not invalid because the evidence introduced at the forfeiture proceeding of the arrests of two of the owners at house for illegal drug activity was derived independently from the illegal seizure. But it was unconstitutional because it was clearly a separate legal proceeding that subjected these owners to additional punishment for the same unlawful activity.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment in so far as it deprived the owners that had been arrested at the house for illegal drug activities of their property interest. The court directed the district court to consider on remand whether another owner and the administrator were aware of criminal activity on the premises and, if so, whether the present forfeiture order imposed an excessive fine on them.

Del Papa v. Steffen


No. 27847


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


112 Nev. 369; 915 P.2d 245; 1996 Nev. LEXIS 53; 24 Media L. Rep. 1879



April 25, 1996, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Opinion of July 12, 1996, Reported at: 1996 Nev. LEXIS 105.


PRIOR HISTORY: Petition for a writ of prohibition or in the alternative for a writ of mandamus directing Respondents to cease all action in Supreme Court Case No. 24598 and in particular all action in furtherance of the allegedly unlawful and unconstitutional investigation directed at Petitioner and other individuals by Respondent Herbert F. Ahlswede, Special Master.



DISPOSITION: Petition granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent justices appointed respondent special master to investigate alleged leaks of information to the press in violation of two early orders by a panel of the court that directed the proceedings regarding a case were to have been kept confidential. Petitioner state attorney general filed an action for a writ of prohibition or in the alternative a writ of mandamus declaring that the court mandate the justices to cease all action in the case.


OVERVIEW: The court held that the writ of prohibition was proper. The court determined that the confidential orders entered by the justices were done so without jurisdiction. The court held that the public had a right and a need to know of the proceedings and secret judicial proceedings posed a threat to public confidence in the judiciary. Open court proceedings assured that the proceedings were conducted fairly and discouraged misconduct and biased decision making. The court held that the justices' concern with confidentiality did not constitute a compelling state interest that overrode the constitutionally protected rights of freedom of speech and press and access to the courts. Therefore, the court held that the appointment of the special master was not authorized. The court also determined that the justices lacked the authority to initiate and oversee an investigation into the source of the leaked information and the appointment of the special master was not in accordance with standard procedures. Finally, the court held that the situation impermissibly invested both investigatory and adjudicative functions into the hands of the justices.


OUTCOME: The court granted the petition for a writ of prohibition.

McKague v. Warden, Nevada State Prison


No. 25816


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


112 Nev. 159; 912 P.2d 255; 1996 Nev. LEXIS 34



February 29, 1996, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied July 24, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from an order of the district court dismissing a second post-conviction petition for a writ of habeas corpus in a capital case. First Judicial District Court, Carson City; Michael E. Fondi, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision of the First Judicial District Court, Carson City (Nevada), which dismissed with prejudice defendant's second post-conviction petition for writ of habeas corpus in proper person.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of two counts of first-degree murder and other crimes. He was sentenced to death for the murders. Defendant filed a second post-conviction petition for writ of habeas corpus in proper person, alleging prior and additional claims of ineffectiveness of trial counsel and a new claim of ineffectiveness of his first post-conviction counsel for counsel's failure to file a timely appeal. The trial court dismissed the petition with prejudice. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that defendant had no statutory right to counsel in a post-conviction proceeding. Because he had no right to counsel, he could not demonstrate good cause for filing a successive petition based on an ineffectiveness of post-conviction counsel claim. It did not matter if defendant's post-conviction counsel had timely appealed because his claims lacked merit. The claims that the trial court refused to review were not new or different grounds for relief, but rather were claims that the trial court had already determined on the merits in defendant's first petition.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court, which dismissed with prejudice defendant's second post-conviction petition for writ of habeas corpus in proper person.

Erwin v. State


No. 25812


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


111 Nev. 1535; 908 P.2d 1367; 1995 Nev. LEXIS 178; 44 A.L.R.5th 859



December 19, 1995, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a district court order denying appellant's motion for a preliminary injunction and granting respondent's countermotion to dismiss. Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County; Joseph S. Pavlikowski, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant entrepreneur sought review of the decision of the Clark County District Court (Nevada), which denied his motion for a preliminary injunction and granted respondent state's motion to dismiss the entrepreneur's complaint. On appeal, the entrepreneur contended that Nev. Rev. Stat. 599B did not apply to his business and that the trial court's application of the statute violated his constitutional rights.


OVERVIEW: The entrepreneur owned and operated a telephone sports information service to which customers subscribed and then called in for information at their convenience. In 1993, the legislature amended Nev. Rev. Stat. ch. 599B to require telephone solicitors to register their business with the state, pay a $ 6,000 annual fee, and post a $ 50,000 bond. The entrepreneur sought equitable relief and filed a complaint, claiming that chapter 599B did not apply to his business and that its application violated his constitutional rights. The state filed a motion to dismiss. The trial court dismissed the complaint and granted the state's motion to dismiss. The court held that the plain language of Nev. Rev. Stat. 599B.010(8) (c) (2) covered the entrepreneur's business. Chapter 599B satisfied due process, equal protection, and the commercial speech guarantees of the First Amendment. Licensing fees imposed upon expression-related businesses were required to be nominal and imposed only as a regulatory measure to defray the expenses of policing such activities. The record on appeal was inadequate to determine whether the fee and bond requirements of chapter 599B were nominal and reasonable.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order and remanded for determination of whether the statute's fee and bond requirements were nominal and reasonable.

 

49 of 423 DOCUMENTS


Barrett v. Baird


No. 25947


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


111 Nev. 1496; 908 P.2d 689; 1995 Nev. LEXIS 182



December 19, 1995, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a judgment in favor of respondents in a medical malpractice action and from orders awarding attorney fees and costs. Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County; J. Charles Thompson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant widow sought review of the order of the Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County (Nevada), which entered judgment in favor of respondent hospital and physicians in a medical malpractice action, and from orders awarding attorney fees and costs.


OVERVIEW: Appellant widow brought a medical malpractice action against respondent hospital and physicians, following the alleged failure of respondents to correctly diagnose and treat the ailments of appellant's deceased husband. Subsequently, appellant sought review of the trial court's failure to grant a new trial following a judgment in favor of respondents. Appellant additionally contended that implementation of a medical malpractice screening panel was unconstitutional because it violated the right to a jury trial, equal protection, separation of powers, and due process. On appeal, the court concluded that the panel was constitutional, but reversed the trial court's judgment based upon respondents' counsels' misconduct. The court held that the cumulative effect of respondents' misconduct permeated the entire proceeding such that the jury was improperly influenced in reaching its verdict. Finally, the court held that the screening panel statute did not make appellant's right to a jury trial practically unavailable because it did not undermine the guarantee that a jury will find the facts.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the lower court's judgment and award of attorney fees in favor of respondent hospital and physicians on the grounds that the district court abused its discretion in failing to grant appellant widow a new trial due to respondents' counsels' misconduct.

 

50 of 423 DOCUMENTS


Woolsey v. State


No. 26198


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


111 Nev. 1440; 906 P.2d 723; 1995 Nev. LEXIS 169



November 30, 1995, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a judgment of conviction, pursuant to a guilty plea, of one count of felony failure to appear. Seventh Judicial District Court, Eureka County; Dan L. Papez, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the decision from the Seventh Judicial District Court, Eureka County (Nevada), which convicted defendant following a guilty plea of felony failure to appear. Defendant argued that the charge was barred by the statute of limitations and that the state could not prove the underlying offense.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested for driving while intoxicated and other crimes, and he posted bail. Defendant failed to appear at a hearing, and he was later re-arrested and again failed to appear. Bench warrants were issued by times. Approximately seven years later, defendant was arrested again, convicted of some of the underlying crimes, and then convicted of Nev. Rev. Stat. 199.335, the bail jumping statute. Defendant also sought habeas corpus relief, which was denied. The appellate court reversed. Felonies other than murders had a three-year statute of limitations under Nev. Rev. Stat. 171.085(2). The period generally began to run when the crime was completed. However, case law, which held that an escape was a continuing offense, was extended to bail jumping since a person on bail was still technically in the state's custody. Thus, the limitation period did not begin to run until defendant was returned to custody. The failure to appear was a separate offense from the underlying charge. However, the felony driving while intoxicated charge was reduced to a misdemeanor. Thus, defendant could not have been convicted of felony failure to appear.


OUTCOME: The conviction of defendant for felony failure to appear was reversed and remanded. While the limitations period was not violated and while the state did not have to prove the underlying felony, the failure to appear charge was only for a misdemeanor offense.

 

51 of 423 DOCUMENTS


Taylor v. State


No. 25287


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


111 Nev. 1253; 903 P.2d 805; 1995 Nev. LEXIS 141



October 4, 1995, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from an order denying a motion to suppress and a judgment of conviction of one count of possession of a controlled substance. Seventh Judicial District Court, White Pine County; Merlyn H. Hoyt and Dan L. Papez, Judges.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant driver appealed the order from the Seventh Judicial District Court, White Pine County (Nevada), which denied his motion to suppress evidence in favor of the state and convicted him of possession of marijuana with a condition of probation requiring him to reimburse the county for the cost of his defense.


OVERVIEW: Defendant driver was stopped by police officers for driving below the speed limit and arrested for driving without a valid license. The officers found marijuana while taking inventory of the contents of the car in preparation for towing. The district court denied defendant's motion to suppress the evidence taken from his car, and convicted him of possession of a controlled substance, as charged by the state. The district court also required him to reimburse the county for the cost of his defense as a condition of probation. Defendant appealed, claiming that the initial stop and subsequent arrest were performed by the officers as a pretext for searching his car, and that the trial court erred in ordering him to reimburse the county for his defense costs as a condition of probation. On appeal, the court affirmed and applied the "would" test to the stop and search of defendant's car. The court concluded that any reasonable officer would have pulled over defendant's car in similar circumstances, and that the actions of the officers after stopping the car were routine. Nev. Rev. Stat. 178.3975 gave the trial court the discretion to condition probation on the repayment of attorney fees.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order in favor of the state that denied defendant driver's motion to suppress evidence taken from his car. The court concluded that any reasonable officer would have pulled over the car in similar circumstances, and that the actions of the officers after stopping the car were routine. The court affirmed the order requiring the defendant to reimburse the county the cost of his defense because a Nevada statute so provided.

 

52 of 423 DOCUMENTS


Desimone v. State


No. 24971


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


111 Nev. 1221; 904 P.2d 1; 1995 Nev. LEXIS 143



October 4, 1995, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Judgment of Conviction Reversed and Vacated February 23, 2000, Reported at: 2000 Nev. LEXIS 20.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment of conviction of one count of possession of a trafficking quantity of a controlled substance. Second Judicial District Court, Washoe County; Mills B. Lane, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his conviction in the Second Judicial District Court, Washoe County (Nevada) for possession of a trafficking quantity of a controlled substance. Defendant was assessed a tax and penalties for illegal possession of a controlled substance, which was reduced to judgment. Defendant argued that the criminal conviction was a second punishment barred by the Double Jeopardy Clause, U.S. Const. amend. V.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was assessed tax and penalties pursuant to Nev. Rev. Stat. § 372A for illegal possession of a controlled substance, and the amount was reduced to judgment. Defendant was then convicted in a bench trial of one count of possession of a trafficking quantity of a controlled substance. The court reversed his conviction and held that payment of a tax pursuant to § 372A constituted punishment, triggering the protections of the Double Jeopardy Clause. In deciding whether a tax was designed to punish rather than to raise revenue, the court was required to consider: (1) the rate of taxation, (2) the deterrent purpose, based on the use of tax revenues for anti-crime initiatives; (3) the requirement that the tax was imposed solely upon criminal activity; and (4) the imposition of the tax upon goods which were neither owned nor possessed by the debtor. The crucial inquiry in determining whether jeopardy attached to tax statutes probed the state's intentions. The court was required to identify characteristics of the state's enactment and prosecution of the tax statute to test objectively if the state intended punishment. Whether actual punishment occurred was not part of the inquiry.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction for possession of a trafficking quantity of a controlled substance.

Bollinger v. State


No. 26404


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


111 Nev. 1110; 901 P.2d 671; 1995 Nev. LEXIS 129



August 24, 1995, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Habeas corpus proceeding at, Motion denied by, in part, Dismissed by, in part, Summary judgment denied by Bollinger v. Baker, 2013 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 179686 (D. Nev., Dec. 20, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a judgment of conviction, following a jury trial, of two counts of murder in the first degree and a number of related charges. Second Judicial District Court, Washoe County; Jerry Carr Whitehead, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Second Judicial District Court, Washoe County (Nevada), convicting him of two counts of first degree murder, two counts of kidnapping, two counts of robbery, and one count of burglary, and sentencing him to death.


OVERVIEW: On appeal from his criminal convictions and death sentence, defendant contended that the trial court erred in failing to admonish the jury, at every adjournment, to refrain from talking about the trial and to avoid coming into contact with the media. It was also contended that the jury instruction concerning reasonable doubt was erroneous, and that the trial court erred in allowing the jury to view his tattoo which read "pyro." The court affirmed defendant's convictions of two counts of first degree murder, two counts of kidnapping, two counts of robbery, and one count of burglary. Defendant's death sentence was also affirmed. Reversal was not required for any errors of the trial court in failing to admonish the jury before adjourning because defendant failed to show prejudice. The court rejected defendant's constitutional challenge to the reasonable doubt instruction because there was not a reasonable likelihood that the jury applied the instruction in an unconstitutional manner. Also, at the sentencing phase, defendant's tattoo was relevant evidence in illuminating his character.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions of two counts of first degree murder, two counts of kidnapping, two counts of robbery, and one count of burglary. Defendant's death sentence was also affirmed.

Ford v. Warden, Nev. Women's Correctional Ctr.


No. 24961


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


111 Nev. 872; 901 P.2d 123; 1995 Nev. LEXIS 105



July 27, 1995, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Amended August 24, 1995. Rehearing Denied October 19, 1995. Certiorari Denied February 20, 1996, Reported at: 1996 U.S. LEXIS 1212.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from district court order dismissing petition for writ of habeas corpus in capital case. First Judicial District Court, Carson City; Michael E. Fondi, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner sought review of a judgment from the First Judicial District Court, Carson City (Nevada), which dismissed petitioner's application for a writ of habeas corpus and denied her motion to copy the record and to appoint new counsel following petitioner's conviction for murder and attempted murder.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was convicted for 6 counts of murder and 23 counts of attempted murder and was sentenced to death. Following the denial of her appeal and initial habeas corpus petition, petitioner filed a second petition for a writ of habeas corpus on the grounds that she was denied a fair trial, was denied effective assistance of trial and appellate counsel, and that the state and court system had engaged in unconstitutional conduct. The district court dismissed the petition, holding that the claims had previously been raised and rejected on direct appeal and any claims not raised in the previous petition were waived. On appeal, the court held that: (1) Nev. Rev. Stat. § 34.810 placed the burden on petitioner to show good cause and prejudice in order to avoid the effects of an abuse of the writ, which petitioner failed to show; (2) the burden of production was on petitioner for writs of habeas corpus; (3) successive petitions could be dismissed based solely on the face of the petition; (4) and the district court did not err in failing to provide a competency hearing sua sponte where there was no evidence that raised a sufficient doubt as to petitioner's competency to proceed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment from the district court, which denied petitioner's second petition for a writ of habeas corpus and which denied petitioner's motion to copy the record and to appoint new counsel.

McNelton v. State


No. 25127


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


111 Nev. 900; 900 P.2d 934; 1995 Nev. LEXIS 112



July 27, 1995, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of certiorari denied McNelton v. Nevada, 517 U.S. 1212, 116 S. Ct. 1833, 134 L. Ed. 2d 937, 1996 U.S. LEXIS 3337 (1996)
Writ of habeas corpus denied McNelton v. State, 115 Nev. 396, 990 P.2d 1263, 1999 Nev. LEXIS 71 (1999)
Habeas corpus proceeding at, Motion granted by, in part, Motion denied by, in part McNelton v. McDaniel, 2006 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 27223 (D. Nev., May 5, 2006)
Writ of habeas corpus denied McNelton v. State, 2012 Nev. Unpub. LEXIS 778 (2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a judgment of conviction pursuant to a jury verdict and a sentence of death for murder with the use of a deadly weapon. Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County; J. Charles Thompson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County (Nevada), after he was convicted of first degree murder and sentenced to death.


OVERVIEW: Witnesses testified that defendant grabbed the back of the victim's head, pointed a gun at her forehead, pulled the trigger, and walked away as she fell. The court upheld defendant's conviction, finding that the prosecutor's comments about defendant's failure to show remorse in his allocution statement was not prejudicial because the jury would not naturally view the comments as comments on his failure to testify. The trial judge had no duty to advise defendant as to the scope of cross-examination if he testified at the penalty phase. The probative value of evidence that the victim was pregnant outweighed the prejudicial effect and did not render the trial fundamentally unfair. The jury's finding of aggravating circumstances based on prior convictions was proper because defendant did not show that the convictions were constitutionally invalid. The "sentence of imprisonment" aggravator applied even though defendant had been released from physical incarceration, and there was no evidence that the legislature intended for such aggravator to disproportionately affect African-American males. Under the circumstances, the court determined that the sentence of death was not excessive.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for first degree murder and the sentence of death.

DISPOSITION: Writ granted with instructions. 1



1  On September 9, 1994, this court issued an unpublished order that granted in part Petitioner Whitehead's petition for various forms of relief. This opinion is substantially the same as the referenced order, with certain exceptions that both clarify and modify the order and respond to the "Dissenting Addendum To Order Granting Petition" filed by Justice Shearing on November 22, 1994. * * * Therefore, certain aspects of this opinion that are responsive to the addendum dissent may not have application to our colleague's revised dissent. Sheriff, Washoe County v. Vlasak


No. 24893


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


111 Nev. 59; 888 P.2d 441; 1995 Nev. LEXIS 3



January 25, 1995, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from district court order dismissing a criminal information. Second Judicial District Court, Washoe County; Charles McGee, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state sought review of an order from the Second Judicial District Court of Washoe County (Nevada), which dismissed a criminal indictment against defendant for persistent failure to provide support and maintenance for his children under Nev. Rev. Stat. § 201.020.


OVERVIEW: The trial court dismissed an indictment against defendant for "persistent" failure to provide "support and maintenance" for his children on the ground that the § 201.020 was unconstitutionally vague. On appeal, the court reversed and remanded the dismissal of the indictment. The court did not view the word "support" to be vague. The court found that parents of ordinary intelligence would have understood that their willful refusal to pay court-ordered child support violated the clear terms of the criminal statute. The court held that the term "support" and the phrase "persisted for more than a year" were subject to well settled and ordinarily understood meanings when viewed in the context of the entire statutory provision. Section 201.020 was sufficiently clear to provide notice to potential violators of the conduct proscribed.


OUTCOME: An order of the lower court dismissing an indictment against defendant for persistent failure to provide support and maintenance was reversed and remanded.

Willerton v. Bassham by Welfare Div.


No. 23328


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


111 Nev. 10; 889 P.2d 823; 1995 Nev. LEXIS 10



January 24, 1995, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a special order of the district court denying a motion to declare a prior order and judgment non-modifiable. Ninth Judicial District Court, Douglas County; Norman C. Robison, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant father sought review from a judgment of a special order of the Ninth Judicial District Court, Douglas County (Nevada), which denied a motion to declare a prior child support order and judgment non-modifiable in an action against appellees, mother, child, the welfare division, and the Department of Human Resources.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the father contended that the bar and merger principles of res judicata precluded any further litigation on the same claims or causes of action as those interposed in the complaint originally filed. The issue for the court was whether a stipulated compromise agreement in an action to determine paternity and to compel child support precluded a later action by either the mother or child to modify the support provisions of the order. The court concluded that a consideration of the policies and purposes behind the applicable acts required a departure from the otherwise appropriate application of the bar and merger principles of res judicata to preclude an action by the child to determine paternity and to compel support and an action by the child or the state to modify support. Specifically, the principles of res judicata barred the mother from reasserting an action to determine paternity or compel support, but that the child was not so barred. In addition, the child or the state could seek to modify the provisions of a compromise agreement intended to provide the child with support to the extent that the judgment or order was being enforced in the state.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the district court denying the motion to declare the prior order and judgment non-modifiable.

Lay v. State

SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


110 Nev. 1189; 886 P.2d 448; 1994 Nev. LEXIS 146



November 30, 1994, FILED

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by a jury of first degree murder with the use of a deadly weapon. The judgment was entered in the Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark Count (Nevada). The trial judge sentenced him to two consecutive life terms without possibility of parole, one for the murder and as an enhancement for use of a deadly weapon. OVERVIEW: Defendant was a member of a gang. He was identified by a number of witnesses as the driver of the car that approached the victim and as the shooter. The man who was shot died later. Defendant and others were indicted on a number of charges. The charges of first-degree murder and use of a deadly weapon were severed from the other charges and defendants. It held that in the sentencing phase a trial judge could consider evidence not otherwise admissible.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of conviction and the sentences imposed by the trial judge in defendant's first degree murder charge.

Williams v. State


No. 23425


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


110 Nev. 1182; 885 P.2d 536; 1994 Nev. LEXIS 148



November 30, 1994, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a judgment of conviction, pursuant to a jury verdict, of one count of murder in the first degree. Second Judicial District Court, Washoe County; Mills B. Lane III, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed her judgment of conviction for murder in the first degree from the Second Judicial District Court, Washoe County (Nevada). Defendant contended that prejudicial error resulted from the exclusion of expert psychiatric testimony on her defense of not guilty by reason of insanity.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's daughter was pronounced dead on arrival when brought to the hospital for emergency treatment. After defendant pleaded not guilty and not guilty by reason of insanity to murder in violation of Nev. Rev. Stat. §§ 200.010, 200.030, the jury found her guilty of murder in the first degree and she was sentenced to life imprisonment with possible parole. The court reversed this conviction and remanded the matter to proceed further. The district court committed prejudicial error by excluding defendant's proffered evidence of the expert psychiatric testimony that tended to support her theory of defense, despite the expert's lack of an opinion on her sanity under the controlling M'Naughten standard. The district court correctly ruled that § 200.030 was constitutional because it was not impermissibly vague. The court concluded that the word "nonaccidental" in § 200.030(6)(a) was not an imprecise or difficult term to understand. The court found that ordinary persons would know that purposeful, or nonaccidental, injury of a child would constitute child abuse, and that if the abuse resulted in the child's death would subject the perpetrator to a first-degree murder conviction.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of conviction for murder in the first degree challenged by defendant from the district court. The court remanded the matter for further proceedings.

Sheriff v. Encoe


No. 24888


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


110 Nev. 1317; 885 P.2d 596; 1994 Nev. LEXIS 156



November 30, 1994, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from an order of the district court granting a pretrial petition for writ of habeas corpus. Second Judicial District, Washoe County; Steven R. Kosach, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state appealed from the order of the Second Judicial District, Washoe County (Nevada) which granted respondent mother's pre-trial petition for writ of habeas corpus, on the charge of willfully endangering a child pursuant to Nev. Rev. Stat. § 200.508.


OVERVIEW: The mother was charged with willfully endangering a child pursuant to Nev. Rev. Stat. § 200.508. The state contended that the mother violated the statute from the moment her child left the womb to the moment the umbilical cord was severed, based on the transmission of illegal substances from respondent to her newborn baby through the umbilical cord. The mother admitted that she had used illegal substances during her pregnancy and the infant tested positive for them. The district court granted mother's pre-trial petition for writ of habeas corpus. On appeal, the court affirmed. It held that the statute did not apply to a pregnant woman's ingestion of illegal substances and the resulting transmission of the substances to her child through the umbilical cord. To so interpret the statute was contrary to legislative intent. The writ of habeas corpus was properly granted because the mother's conduct was not subject to prosecution under the statute.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the district court granting a pre-trial petition for writ of habeas corpus filed by the mother, who was charged with willfully endangering a child through the transmission of illegal substances to a newborn infant through the umbilical cord, immediately following birth.

Foley v. Kennedy


No. 24284


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


110 Nev. 1295; 885 P.2d 583; 1994 Nev. LEXIS 164



November 30, 1994, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied June 22, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal and cross-appeal from district court orders following a bench trial directing registrar of voters to take no further action on appellants' recall petition and denying the cross-appellant's request for costs. Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County; William P. Beko, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant citizens sought review of the judgment from the Eighth Judicial District Court (Nevada) that found in favor respondent board member holding that a petition filed by the citizens seeking to recall the board member legally insufficient.


OVERVIEW: The citizens organized a petition to recall the board member from her position as a university regent. Because the petition did not have enough signatures, the lower court found the petition legally insufficient. In affirming, the court held that the lower court correctly found the language of Nev. Const. art. II, § 9 unambiguous as it said nothing concerning the filing of the notice of intent to recall. The court noted that according to the constitutional provision, 25 percent of the persons who actually voted in the general election were required to sign the recall petition. Accordingly, the court concluded that the plain and unambiguous language of the constitution was determinative of the issue of which election was relevant in calculating the required number of signatures on a recall petition. The court further found that the principle of equitable estopped did not apply. The court found that the registrar's erroneous advice did not require the registrar to accept the citizens' recall petition and go forward with the recall election. The court reversed the lower court's ruling relating to costs.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part and reversed in part the judgment from the lower court.

Smith v. State


No. 24213


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


110 Nev. 1094; 881 P.2d 649; 1994 Nev. LEXIS 136



September 28, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal after remand at Smith v. State, 114 Nev. 33, 953 P.2d 264, 1998 Nev. LEXIS 9 (1998)
Habeas corpus proceeding at, Motion granted by, Motion denied by, As moot Smith v. McDaniel, 2007 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 83847 (D. Nev., Oct. 25, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a judgment of conviction of three counts of murder with use of a deadly weapon and one count of attempted murder with use of a deadly weapon and from a sentence of death. Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County; Jeffrey D. Sobel, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part and remanded for a new penalty hearing.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision of the Eighth Judicial District Court of Clark County (Nevada), which convicted defendant of three count's of murder with a deadly weapon and one count of attempted murder with a deadly weapon and sentenced defendant to death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted for murdering his wife and his two step children with a hammer and for the attempted murder of a fourth person, also with a hammer. Defendant was sentenced to death for the murders of his step children, life without parole for the murder of his wife, and two consecutive twenty year terms for the attempted murder. On appeal, the court found that the trial court erred in failing to dismiss the deadly weapon sentence enhancement because a hammer, while potentially harmful when misused, was not intended by its nature or design to be used to cause injury and wass therefore not a deadly weapon as a matter of law for purposes of sentence enhancement. The court also vacated the two death sentences because the trial court's failure to instruct the jury that an aggravating circumstance based upon depravity of mind had to include torture, mutilation or other serious and depraved physical abuse beyond the act of killing itself rendered Nev. Rev. Stat. 200.033(8) unconstitutionally vague as applied. Finally, the court found that under Nev. Rev. Stat. 175.552 the trial court properly allowed the victims' family member to give victim impact testimony.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions on three counts of first degree murder and one count of attempted murder, vacated the 20-year sentence enhancement for use of a deadly weapon in the attempted murder, vacated the death sentences for two of the murders, and remanded for a new penalty hearing.

Morgano v. Smith


No. 24958, No. 25215


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


110 Nev. 1025; 879 P.2d 735; 1994 Nev. LEXIS 117



August 10, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Consolidated proper person appeals from district court orders in favor of respondents in actions for legal malpractice against former criminal defense counsel. Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County; Jack Lehman, Judge (docket number 24958); First Judicial District Court, Carson City; Michael E. Fondi, Judge (docket number 25215).



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants brought legal malpractice actions against respondents, former criminal defense counsel. The Eight Judicial District Court, Clark County (Nevada) and the First Judicial District Court, Carson City (Nevada) granted motions disposing of the actions in favor of counsel. The consolidated the actions for review.


OVERVIEW: Appellants filed actions against their privately retained criminal defense counsel for legal malpractice after entering guilty pleas. The trial court granted motions for summary judgment and dismissal to defense counsel. The appellate court determined that in order to avoid the defense counsels' motions for summary judgment and for dismissal, appellants were required to plead that they had obtained appellate or post-conviction relief. The court held that in order to state a claim for legal malpractice against private criminal defense counsel, appellants must assert a basis for claiming that the convictions or sentences were caused by something other than appellants' own conduct. The court found that one appellant had not obtained any appellate or post-conviction relief from his conviction or sentence. The other appellant did not allege that he had obtained such relief in his complaint. The court noted that there was no record of a direct appeal and the court had recently dismissed his petition for post-conviction relief.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgments of the trial courts.

 

65 of 423 DOCUMENTS


Skipper v. State


No. 23843


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


110 Nev. 1031; 879 P.2d 732; 1994 Nev. LEXIS 118



August 10, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from judgment of conviction pursuant to a jury trial of two counts of cheating at gaming. Second Judicial District Court, Washoe County; Mills B. Lane, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction in the Second Judicial District Court, Washoe County (Nevada), of cheating at gaming in violation of Nev. Rev. Stat. §§ 465.070(7), 465.083.


OVERVIEW: While playing craps at two different gaming establishments, defendant was videotaped throwing the dice in a manner referred to as dice sliding. Defendant presented no defense to the charges, but instead challenged the constitutionality of Nev. Rev. Stat. §§ 465.070(7), 465.083. On appeal, the court affirmed the conviction. The court found that a dice slider used a methodology of play that was based upon a purposefully orchestrated combination of factors designed to change the nature of play through affirmative acts of cheating and deception. The court reasoned that persons of average intelligence who play the game of craps would have no difficulty understanding that a surreptitious manipulation of the dice contrary to the rules of the game, in order to alter its outcome, constituted an act of cheating. The court noted that defendant utilized an accomplice to obscure the dealer's vision of the table, while he purposely engaged in sliding the dice. Thus, the court concluded that defendant altered an integral attribute of the game in affecting the otherwise established probabilities of its various outcomes.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction of cheating at gaming.

 

66 of 423 DOCUMENTS


Williams v. Williams


No. 24291


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


110 Nev. 830; 877 P.2d 1081; 1994 Nev. LEXIS 110



July 26, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from an order of the district court denying appellants' motion for a trial de novo following an arbitration decision. Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County; Joseph S. Pavlikowski, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, owner and driver, challenged an order of the Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County (Nevada), which held in favor of appellee injured party and denied their motion for a trial de novo following an arbitration decision.


OVERVIEW: The owner and driver argued that the district court erred in its denial of its motion for a trial de novo. The court reversed the judgment and held that former Nev. Rev. Stat. 38.215, which incorporated Nev. Rev. Stat. 38.145, was an unconstitutional infringement on the right to trial by jury. Nev. Rev. Stat. 38.235(1) required that the party requesting a trial de novo, or the party's attorney, make an oath or affirmation that it was not for the purpose of delay that the trial was requested, but for the purpose of alleviating an injustice that was done by the arbitrators in making the award. The court held that 38.235(1) was plain and unambiguous. It required only that an oath be made, and the court would not lend the statute a construction contrary to its clear meaning.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the judgment that denied the owner and driver's motion for a trial de novo following an arbitration decision in an action by the injured party. The court held that the attorney for the owner and driver swore under oath that the request was not for purposes of delay and that it was error to require a showing of injustice.

Didomenico v. State


No. 25830


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


110 Nev. 861; 877 P.2d 1069; 1994 Nev. LEXIS 111



July 26, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Proper person appeal from a judgment of conviction pursuant to a no contest plea. Second Judicial District Court, Washoe County; Mills Lane, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Order denying motion for appointment of counsel vacated.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order of the Second Judicial District Court, Washoe County (Nevada), which denied his motion for appointment of counsel following his conviction for two counts of possession of stolen property and one count of burglary in three different cases pursuant to a no contest plea.


OVERVIEW: Defendant sought the appointment of appellate counsel. The court found that Nev. Rev. Stat. § 178.397 did not grant the district court any discretion in appointing counsel to represent an indigent defendant on appeal. The court found that an indigent defendant had a Fourteenth Amendment right to appointed counsel on defendant's first appeal of right from a judgment of conviction. The court also found that Nev. Rev. Stat. § 177.015 granted a criminal defendant the right to an appeal from a judgment of conviction. The court noted that trial counsel had an obligation to inform a defendant of the right to appeal and to perfect that appeal if the defendant wished to challenge the judgment of conviction. The court concluded that defendant enjoyed a right to direct appeal even if the judgment of conviction was based upon a guilty plea.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the order and remanded the case to the district court for the limited purpose of appointing counsel.

In re A WRIT OF PROHIBITION OR IN THE ALTERNATIVE FOR A WRIT OF MANDAMUS


No. 24598


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


878 P.2d 913; 1994 Nev. LEXIS 113



July 26, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Opinion of July 12, 1996, Reported at: 1996 Nev. LEXIS 105.


PRIOR HISTORY: Original proceeding; motion to preclude further involvement of Attorney General; motion for an order to show cause, an investigation, and a protective order; motion for appointment of a master to conduct factual investigation.



DISPOSITION: Motions granted in part; judgment reserved in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner judge sought a writ of prohibition to preclude further involvement of the Attorney General on behalf of respondent Commission on Judicial Discipline (Commission). The judge also filed a motion for an order to show cause, an investigation, and a protective order; and a motion for appointment of a master to conduct factual investigation.


OVERVIEW: An attorney from the state's Attorney General's office engaged in a very extensive investigation of the allegations against judge on behalf of the Commission. The court found that such an investigation could only be carried out properly and constitutionally by the Commission itself, pursuant to Nev. Const. art. 6, § 21(7). The court reasoned that the Attorney General must be removed as counsel and prosecutor for the Commission not only because of the stated constitutional grounds, but due to the conflict of interest created by the Attorney General's office when it acted as both legal advisor to the Commission and as a prosecutor who has been prosecuting a matter before the Commission. Such a situation caused a member of the executive branch to act in a judicial capacity, which was simply not constitutionally permitted. Nev. Rev. Stat. § 1.450(2) was constitutional insofar as it permitted the Commission to request official legal opinions of the Attorney General in matters unrelated to judicial discipline, but could not be constitutionally read to authorize the Attorney General to act as counsel or as prosecutor to the Commission.


OUTCOME: The court ordered that the Attorney General be removed as counsel for the Commission in all disciplinary proceedings pending against the judge.

Paine v. State


No. 24304


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


110 Nev. 609; 877 P.2d 1025; 1994 Nev. LEXIS 91



July 7, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied August 12, 1994.
Writ of certiorari denied Paine v. Nevada, 514 U.S. 1038, 115 S. Ct. 1405, 131 L. Ed. 2d 291, 1995 U.S. LEXIS 2305 (1995)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from sentence of death imposed by a three-judge panel, subsequent to a guilty plea to one count of first-degree murder with use of a deadly weapon. Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County; Carl J. Christensen, Judge; Sixth Judicial District Court, Humboldt, Lander, and Pershing Counties; Jerry V. Sullivan, Judge; Second Judicial District Court, Washoe County; Charles N. McGee, Judge.
Paine v. State, 107 Nev. 998, 823 P.2d 281, 1991 Nev. LEXIS 206 (1991)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a death sentence imposed on remand by a three-judge panel from Clark, Humboldt, Lander, Pershing, and Washoe Counties (Nevada), subsequent to a guilty plea to one count of first-degree murder with use of a deadly weapon and a prior appeal of the same sentence imposed earlier by a different three-judge panel. In the previous appeal, the court vacated the sentence, and the second panel then reimposed it.


OVERVIEW: Defendant had murdered a taxi driver in the course of a robbery. The second sentencing panel found beyond a reasonable doubt that two aggravating circumstances under Nev. Rev. Stat. § 200.033 existed: the murder was committed during the commission of a robbery, and it was committed upon a person at random and without apparent motive. The second panel found that the aggravating circumstances outweighed the mitigating circumstances, and again sentenced defendant to death. The court affirmed, finding that defendant's rights had been duly and justly considered and that he was sentenced fairly and in accordance with the constitutionally valid law of Nevada. Inter alia, the court rejected defendant's challenge to the district court's finding that the murder was aggravated because it was committed at random and without apparent motive. That finding had already been affirmed in the first appeal and had become the law of the case. Further, defendant's confession was voluntary because he had been properly Mirandized, the ineffective assistance of counsel in the first sentencing hearing had not prejudiced his case, and photographs of the crime scene were properly admitted.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the imposition of a death sentence on defendant for first-degree murder with use of a deadly weapon.

Pertgen v. State


No. 21141


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


110 Nev. 554; 875 P.2d 361; 1994 Nev. LEXIS 70



May 31, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied July 22, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from an order of the district court denying appellant's petition for post-conviction relief in a death penalty case. Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County; Myron E. Leavitt, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County (Nevada), denying his petition for post-conviction relief in a death penalty case.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted on charges including murder, kidnapping, and rape. Defendant's challenges to the guilt phase of his trial included the improper admission of his confession and ineffective assistance of counsel. On the penalty phase, defendant primarily challenged the trial court's failure to instruct the jury on the definitions of "torture" and "depravity of mind," the two aggravating circumstances found by the jury. The court found no error in the guilt phase, holding that the court's previous rejection of the confession issue on direct appeal was the law of the case and that defendant failed to show ineffective assistance under Strickland. However, the court reversed defendant's death sentence because the aggravating circumstances were unconstitutionally vague. Because the invalid aggravating circumstances were the only ones found by the jury, the court held that a new penalty hearing was required. The state's inclusion of three aggravating circumstances on special verdict forms that were not contained in the notice of intent to seek the death penalty, and on which the jury was not instructed, was additional support for reversal under the doctrine of cumulative error.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment in part, finding no error in the guilt phase of defendant's trial. The court reversed the trial court's judgment with regard to the penalty phase, finding serious constitutional errors, and remanded for a new penalty hearing.

Castillo v. State


No. 24559


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


110 Nev. 535; 874 P.2d 1252; 1994 Nev. LEXIS 67



May 23, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied September 6, 1994.
Writ of habeas corpus denied Castillo v. McDaniel, 2005 U.S. App. LEXIS 365 (9th Cir. Nev., Jan. 10, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a judgment of conviction entered upon a plea of guilty of one count each of sexual assault and battery with intent to commit sexual assault. Ninth Judicial District Court, Douglas County; David R. Gamble, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the judgment of the Ninth Judicial District Court of Douglas County (Nevada), entered upon defendant's guilty plea, convicting defendant of sexual assault and battery with intention to commit sexual assault. Among other arguments, defendant argued that Nev. Rev. Stat. § 62.080, preventing a juvenile from being certified as an adult unless he committed the crime after age 16, should be retroactively applied to defendant.


OVERVIEW: Defendant sought review of the trial court's judgment which, pursuant to a plea agreement, convicted defendant of sexual assault. The court held that Nev. Rev. Stat. § 62.080, preventing juveniles under the age of 16 from being tried as adults, should not be given retroactive effect because there was no clear legislative intent to the contrary. The court held that defendant's life sentence did not constitute cruel and unusual punishment in contravention of U.S. Const. amend. VIII. Defendant's sentence fell within the statutory limits and was not so disproportionate to the crime that it shocked the conscience or offended fundamental notions of human dignity. The court held that it was error to permit victim impact statement in violation of Nev. Rev. Stat. § 213.005 because the statement was not provided by a statutorily defined "victim." However, the lower court's consideration of the statement was harmless error. The court held that Nev. Rev. Stat. § 62.080, under which defendant was certified as an adult, did not violate U.S. Const. amend. XIV Due Process Clause. Accordingly, the trial court's judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's conviction of sexual assault and consequent life sentence. Absent evidence of legislative intent to the contrary, amended statute, preventing juveniles under the age of 16 from being tried as adults, was not entitled to retroactive effect. Defendant's life sentence did not constitute cruel and unusual punishment because it fell with the statutory guidelines and was not disproportionate to defendant's crimes.

Stroup v. State


No. 24302


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


110 Nev. 525; 874 P.2d 769; 1994 Nev. LEXIS 55



May 19, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a judgment of conviction, pursuant to a jury verdict, of one count of second degree murder. Fifth Judicial District Court, Nye County; John P. Davis, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from the Fifth Judicial District Court, Nye County (Nevada), which convicted him of second-degree murder.


OVERVIEW: A jury found defendant guilty of second-degree murder but made no finding as to the use of a deadly weapon. The trial court sentenced defendant to 11 years for second degree murder with an enhancement pursuant to Nev. Rev. Stat. § 193.165 of 11 more years for the use of a deadly weapon. Defendant sought review. On appeal, the court affirmed the trial court's conviction of defendant. However, the court held that the trial court erred in enhancing defendant's conviction for the use of a deadly weapon when the jury made no finding as to that fact. The court held that § 193.165 required the jury to find the use of a deadly weapon in the commission of the crime before defendant's sentence could be enhanced. The court affirmed the decision of the trial court in refusing defendant's proffered jury instruction as to justifiable homicide. The court held that it was not error to refuse to give an instruction when the law encompassed therein was substantially covered by another instruction given to the jury.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's conviction of defendant for second degree murder but reversed the trial court's enhancement of defendant's sentence for the use of a deadly weapon.

Mello v. Woodhouse


No. 24028


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


110 Nev. 366; 872 P.2d 337; 1994 Nev. LEXIS 46



April 6, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a judgment of the district court dismissing appellant's breach of contract claim and denying appellant's request for declaratory and injunctive relief. Second Judicial District Court, Washoe County; William N. Forman, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant member of the legislature sought review of the decision of the Second Judicial District Court of Washoe County (Nevada), which found in favor of respondents, retirement board members and associated individuals, in appellant's action for breach of contract, injunctive and declaratory relief, constitutional violations, and incidental damages. Appellant's action was dismissed with prejudice.


OVERVIEW: Appellant member of the legislature was a member for nearly 27 years. During the 1989 session, he was instrumental in the passage of a law that quadrupled the pension benefit for legislators. He then resigned about three months later with his retirement benefits based upon the newly enacted legislation. Subsequently, the governor convened a special session of the legislature that repealed the increased pension benefits. Appellant then brought claims against respondents, retirement board members and associated individuals, for breach of contract, injunctive and declaratory relief, constitutional violations, and incidental damages. The district court concluded that the Nevada Constitution prohibited the vesting of appellant's rights and dismissed the action with prejudice. The court affirmed and held that because the legislature repealed the increased benefit before the natural expiration of appellant's term of office, his increased pension benefits did not vest. Consequently, there was no impairment of vested contract rights. The court concluded that appellant concocted his reliance on the increased benefits in an effort to save the increases.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision in favor of respondents, retirement board members and associated individuals, because the increased pension benefits were repealed before the natural expiration of appellant member of the legislature's term of office; therefore his increased pension benefits did not vest. His was not entitled to equitable relief based on promissory estoppel because he concocted his reliance in an effort to save the increases.

Boulder City v. Cinnamon Hills Assocs.


No. 23951


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


110 Nev. 238; 871 P.2d 320; 1994 Nev. LEXIS 25



March 30, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied June 16, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from findings of fact, conclusions of law, and judgment against appellants in a dispute over the denial of a building permit. Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County; Jack Lehman, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, the city, its mayor and its councilmen, sought review of the decision of the Eight Judicial District Court, Clark County (Nevada) that awarded respondents, developer and affiliated individuals, damages for appellants' alleged violations of Nev. Rev. Stat. § 278.0233 and 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983. The violations allegedly occurred when appellants refused respondent's request for a building permit.


OVERVIEW: Respondents, developer and affiliated individuals, were denied a building permit by appellants, the city, its mayor, and its councilmen for a retirement complex. Respondents filed an action alleging, among other things, that the denial of the permit violated Nev. Rev. Stat. § 278.0233 and 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983. The parties initially agreed to enter written transcripts into the record in lieu of calling live witnesses at trial. The trial court then denied appellants' request to call live witnesses. Based only on a review of the records, the trial court found in favor of respondents on the liability issues, and in a separate trial for damages, awarded over $ 500,000 in damages and attorney's fees. The court reversed and remanded the action for a new trial. The court held that the trial court abused its discretion by constricting the liability trial to a paper record. Appellants were not afforded an opportunity to fend off claims in which they acted arbitrarily and capriciously, and their actions were unconstitutional. The court disposed of respondents' claims under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983, finding that respondents' claims were legally deficient and should have never proceeded to trial.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed respondents', developer and affiliated individual, action alleging constitutional violations, having determined that appellants', the city, its mayor, and its councilmen, conduct could not have violated any of respondents' constitutional rights. The court reversed the district court's decision and remanded the action for a new trial because the trial court erred when it conducted the trial on the written record only.
