Dep't Taxation v. Kelly-Ryan, Inc.


No. 24421


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


110 Nev. 276; 871 P.2d 331; 1994 Nev. LEXIS 39



March 30, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a district court order granting summary judgment in favor of a taxpayer in a use tax refund case. First Judicial District Court, Carson City; Michael R. Griffin, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, the State of Nevada, the Nevada Department of Taxation, and the Nevada Tax Commission (cumulatively, the state), sought review of an order entered by the First Judicial District Court, Carson City (Nevada), which granted summary judgment in favor of respondent taxpayer in its action for a use tax refund.


OVERVIEW: The United States engaged a private contractor to solicit bids for the construction of a modular housing complex. The taxpayer was awarded the bid, and pursuant to its performance thereunder, the taxpayer entered a subcontract with a modular housing manufacturer. The taxpayer purchased the modular housing units in Washington and transported them to Nevada for installation. In connection with these transactions, the taxpayer submitted quarterly use tax payments to the state. When its request for a refund was denied, the taxpayer filed this action and alleged that the tax at issue was an unconstitutionally collected sales tax because the tax burden fell directly on the United States in violation of the Supremacy Clause of the United States Constitution. On appeal, the court disagreed and reversed the judgment in favor of the taxpayer. The court held that the taxable events were not the transactions between the taxpayer and the United State's contractor, but rather the transactions between the taxpayer and the housing manufacturer. Therefore, the taxpayer was a "construction contractor" subject to a use tax under Nev. Rev. Stat. § 372.185 when it purchased the housing units.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the summary judgment entered in favor of the taxpayer by the trial court and remanded the case with instructions that judgment be entered in favor of the state.

WHITEHEAD v. NEVADA COMMN. ON JUDICIAL DISCIPLINE


No. 24598


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


110 Nev. 128; 906 P.2d 230; 1994 Nev. LEXIS 18



February 18, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Opinion of July 12, 1996, Reported at: 1996 Nev. LEXIS 105.



DISPOSITION: Original proceeding; motion for reconsideration of orders requiring "in camera" production of documents. Motion denied; basis of jurisdiction for orders for production of documents stated.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In petitioner state judge's action for a writ of mandamus, respondent Commission on Judicial Discipline sought reconsideration of the court's requirement of an in camera production of documents. The judge contended that the Commission exceeded its jurisdiction as established by rules the court promulgated in 1988.


OVERVIEW: After allegations that the state Commission on Judicial Discipline had exceeded it authority when it promulgated a new set of rules, a state judge sought a writ of mandamus and requested an in camera inspection of documents held by the Commission. The court granted the request for the in camera inspection, and the Commission filed a motion for reconsideration. The court denied the motion and further explained its original order. It found that, under Nev. Const. art. 6, § 4, it had the power to issue extraordinary writs to compel the actions of persons that held offices created by the Nevada Constitution. Because the Commission was created by Nev. Const. art. 6, § 21, the court had the authority to order the production of documents. Furthermore, an in camera inspection was required so that the proceedings could remain confidential, as required by the state constitution, and so the court could determine whether it, in fact, had jurisdiction.


OUTCOME: The court denied the motion for reconsideration and further explained its original decision to order the in camera inspection of documents.

 

79 of 423 DOCUMENTS


State v. Parent


No. 24365


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


110 Nev. 114; 867 P.2d 1143; 1994 Nev. LEXIS 13



February 4, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from an order of the district court granting a pretrial motion to suppress evidence. Second Judicial District Court, Washoe County; James A. Stone, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state sought review of a decision of the Second Judicial District Court (Nevada), which granted a pretrial motion to suppress evidence brought by defendant, who was charged with one count of possession of a controlled substance.


OVERVIEW: After an anonymous informant told the police that defendant was travelling by air with cocaine. Defendant was caught and charged with one count of possession of a controlled substance. The trial court granted a pretrial motion to suppress evidence brought by defendant. On appeal, the court reversed and remanded. The court held that the issuance of the anticipatory search warrant and subsequent search in the case were authorized by state statute and did not violate the Fourth Amendment to the United States Constitution. The purposes of the Fourth Amendment were best served by permitting government agents to obtain warrants in advance if they could show probable cause to believe the contraband was to be located on the premises at the time that the search was to take place. The district court erred in suppressing the evidence obtained as a result of the search. The magistrate protected against premature execution by listing in the warrant conditions governing the execution which were explicit, clear, and narrowly drawn, so as to avoid misunderstandings or manipulation by government agents.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the decision of the trial court, which granted a pretrial motion to suppress evidence of defendant, who was charged with one count of possession of a controlled substance.

Anderson v. State

Bradley v. State


No. 23324


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


109 Nev. 1090; 864 P.2d 1272; 1993 Nev. LEXIS 170



November 29, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a judgment of conviction of multiple counts of attempted sexual assault, sexual assault, and lewdness. Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County; Jack Lehman, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed and vacated in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision by the Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County (Nevada), which rendered a judgment of conviction for multiple counts of attempted sexual assault on a minor, sexual assault on a minor, and lewdness with a minor.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of several counts of sexual assault on, attempted sexual assault on, and lewdness with his minor stepdaughter. On appeal, the court affirmed the district court's judgment in part and reversed and vacated in part, holding that there was insufficient evidence to sustain defendant's conviction on one count because the minor victim's testimony was not sufficiently particular as to an element of the offense. The court concluded that the district court properly allowed testimony that defendant used a belt to discipline the victim because its purpose was to demonstrate the victim's state of mind, rather than to show that defendant acted in conformity with a particular trait, and because it did not likely affect the jury's perception of defendant, due to the egregious nature of the crimes committed. The court held that the district court's subsequent written modification of the orally pronounced sentence was effective because the judge's pronouncement of judgment and sentence from the bench was not a final judgment, and because a judgment of conviction was not final until it was signed by the judge and entered by the clerk.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions for sexual assault on a minor, attempted sexual assault on a minor, and lewdness with a minor in part, and reversed and vacated defendant's conviction on one count.

 

82 of 423 DOCUMENTS


Mazzan v. State


No. 23589


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


109 Nev. 1067; 863 P.2d 1035; 1993 Nev. LEXIS 162



November 24, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from an order of the district court denying a motion to change venue in a post-conviction habeas proceeding. First Judicial District Court, Carson City; Michael E. Fondi, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Appeal dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate filed a petition for post conviction relief. The Second Judicial District Court (Nevada) denied the inmate's petition. The inmate challenged the district court's decision.


OVERVIEW: The inmate was found guilty of first degree murder and sentenced to death. After his subsequent appeals failed, the inmate filed his petition for post conviction relief. The inmate relied on Nev. R. App. P. 3A(b)(2) and Nev. Rev. Stat. § 2.090 to support his contention that the challenged order was the "functional equivalent" of an order refusing to change the place of trial of a civil action. The court found the inmate's argument unpersuasive, holding that a habeas corpus was a proceeding that was neither civil nor criminal for all purposes. It was a special statutory remedy, which was essentially unique. The court then held that it was the uniquely statutory quality of habeas corpus that made the inmate's argument unconvincing. Additionally, the court held that no court rule or statute provided for an appeal from an order of the district court denying a motion to change venue in a post-conviction habeas proceeding. The right to appeal was statutory. Moreover, the court held that since no court rule or statute provided for an appeal, no right to appeal existed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the district court's denial of inmate's request for post conviction relief.

Childs v. State

SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


109 Nev. 1050; 864 P.2d 277; 1993 Nev. LEXIS 164

PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from judgment of conviction after a bench trial of one count each of attempted fraudulent slot machine manipulation and fraudulent slot machine manipulation. Ninth Judicial District Court, Douglas County; Norman C. Robison, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment of the Ninth Judicial District Court (Nevada), which convicted him of one count of attempted fraudulent slot machine manipulation and one count of fraudulent slot machine manipulation under Nev. Rev. Stat. § 465.070(7) and Nev. Rev. Stat. § 193.330.


OVERVIEW: The court found that its prior decision, which declared Nev. Rev. Stat. § 465.070(7) invalid, was dispositive of the appeal. The court found that there had been no transfusion of clarity in the statute since it held that it was an invalid attempt to regulate conduct that was identical to the conduct that defendant was convicted of.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the lower court's judgment that convicted defendant of attempted fraudulent slot machine manipulation and fraudulent slot machine manipulation.

 

84 of 423 DOCUMENTS


Hogan v. Warden, Ely State Prison


No. 23193


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


109 Nev. 952; 860 P.2d 710; 1993 Nev. LEXIS 143



September 29, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by, Motion denied by Hogan v. Warden, Ely State Prison, 112 Nev. 553, 916 P.2d 805, 1996 Nev. LEXIS 71 (1996)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from order dismissing post-conviction petition for Writ of Habeas Corpus. Seventh Judicial District Court, White Pine County; Jack B. Ames, Judge.
Hogan v. State, 104 Nev. 860, 809 P.2d 607, 1988 Nev. LEXIS 590 (1988)
Hogan v. Iowa, 952 F.2d 224, 1991 U.S. App. LEXIS 30646 (8th Cir. Iowa, 1991)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of first degree murder and sentenced to death. Defendant appealed the order of the Seventh Judicial District Court, White Pine County (Nevada), which dismissed his petition for a writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: Defendant killed his female companion and shot her daughter five times. Defendant filed a habeas corpus petition after his direct appeals failed, arguing that he was actually innocent of aggravating circumstances. The court affirmed the dismissal of defendant's habeas petition. Defendant's prior manslaughter conviction was constitutional and proof existed that defendant had resorted to violence in the commission of that crime. The manslaughter conviction was thus a proper ground for the imposition of the aggravating circumstance relating to the commission of a prior felony involving the use or threat of violence, Nev. Rev. Stat. § 200.033(2). Further, as there was proof that defendant committed the murder while knowingly and deliberately creating a great risk of death to more than one person, the imposition of the aggravating circumstance under Nev. Rev. Stat. § 200.033(3) was proper. Regardless, the imposition of the aggravating circumstances had previously been upheld on appeal and constituted the law of the case. There were no grounds for habeas relief as defendant failed to prove he sustained actual prejudice and failed to prove a fundamental miscarriage of justice occurred.


OUTCOME: The order dismissing defendant's petition for a writ of habeas corpus was affirmed.

 

85 of 423 DOCUMENTS


Libby v. State


No. 21271


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


109 Nev. 905; 859 P.2d 1050; 1993 Nev. LEXIS 137



September 9, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied June 27, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment of conviction of two counts of murder with use of a deadly weapon, five counts of grand larceny, and a sentence of death. Sixth Judicial District Court, Humboldt County; Jerry V. Sullivan, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the Sixth Judicial District Court, Humboldt County (Nevada), which convicted him of murder with use of a deadly weapon and grand larceny and imposed a death sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that it was improper for the trial court to admit photographs of the victims' bodies, to grant the prosecutor's motion in limine to prohibit questioning regarding the victims' drug use, to deny a change of venue, and to deny supplemental voir dire. Defendant also raised a host of other procedural errors. On appeal, the court affirmed both the conviction and the resulting sentence. Defendant committed the murders during the commission of a robbery, which was an aggravating circumstance to be weighed against the mitigating factor of defendant's family background. The aggravating circumstance far outweighed the mitigating circumstance. Thus, an invalid aggravating circumstance was not a significant factor in sentencing defendant to death, and it did not warrant reversal in this case. The evidence of guilt was overwhelming. While the trial court did commit some errors, none of the errors individually or cumulatively warranted reversal of either the conviction or the sentence. Considering the heinous nature of the killings, the sentence was not excessive or disproportionate to the penalty imposed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction and sentence.

Canape v. State

SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


109 Nev. 864; 859 P.2d 1023; 1993 Nev. LEXIS 136



September 9, 1993, Filed

Post-conviction relief granted at, in part, Post-conviction relief denied at, in part, Remanded by Canape v. State, 2016 Nev. LEXIS 458 (Nev., May 19, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from judgments of conviction for robbery and murder in the first degree and from sentence of death. Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County; Thomas A. Foley, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury convicted defendant of murder in the first degree and armed robbery of the murder victim and sentenced defendant to death. Defendant appealed the judgments of conviction and sentence entered by the Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County (Nevada).


OVERVIEW: On appeal from his murder conviction and death sentence, defendant argued that the trial court erred by instructing the jury on the depravity of mind aggravating circumstance. The court affirmed the sentence and held that the arguably invalid instruction was not a significant factor in the sentencing process because three other aggravating circumstances existed with no mitigating circumstances. The court's weighing whether the evidence allowed the sentencer to arrive at the death sentence did not violate Nevada's Constitution or statutes. In affirming the convictions, the court also found: (1) that the circumstantial evidence was sufficient for a reasonable jury to conclude that defendant robbed the victim prior to his death; (2) that defendant was estopped from objecting to the form of the record because he was given full opportunity to cure any defects in the record; (3) that defendant's failure to object to improper statements by the prosecution precluded consideration of the alleged misconduct on appeal; and (4) defendant's constitutional rights were not violated when he appeared before the jury in shackles at the penalty hearing.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the death sentence and the convictions for murder in the first degree and armed robbery of the murder victim.

 

87 of 423 DOCUMENTS


Crowley v. Duffrin


No. 23489


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


109 Nev. 597; 855 P.2d 536; 1993 Nev. LEXIS 100



June 22, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from summary judgment. Second Judicial District Court, Washoe County; Joseph O. McDaniel, Senior Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant attorney sought review of the decision from the Second Judicial District Court, Washoe County (Nevada) that granted summary judgment in favor of respondent court officials in an action whereby attorney sought a declaration of contractual invalidity because his contract with the county compensated court-appointed attorneys at a rate less than that specified in Nev. Rev. Stat. § 7.125.


OVERVIEW: Appellant attorney, who represented indigent criminal defendants, ceased receiving indigent appointments after invoking his right to compensation under Nev. Rev. Stat. § 7.125 rather than a contract he entered into with the district court, which provided for a lesser rate of pay. Attorney filed a complaint for declaratory relief against respondent court officials and sought a declaration of contractual invalidity because his contract with the county compensated court-appointed attorneys at a rate less than that specified in § 7.125. The district court granted summary judgment to officials. On appeal, the court reversed. The misjoinder or nonjoinder of parties did not justify the entry of summary judgment. The district court should have allowed attorney to amend his complaint to join or delete a party or parties, or the district court should have effectuated the amendment sua sponte. The court noted that where the legislature had adopted a comprehensive scheme for the regulation of a particular subject, any conflicting local regulation on the subject was preempted. The court held that § 7.125 governed the compensation of individual court-appointed attorneys in Nevada.


OUTCOME: The court concluded that summary judgment for officials was inappropriately granted and reversed and remanded to the district court for joinder of the necessary parties and the issuance of declaratory relief to attorney.

Bell v. Anderson


No. 23130


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


109 Nev. 363; 849 P.2d 350; 1993 Nev. LEXIS 42



March 25, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from findings of fact, conclusions of law and judgment of the trial court upholding the validity of a tax sale of real property. Third Judicial District Court, Churchill County; Archie E. Blake, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded with instructions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owners sought review of an order from the Third Judicial District Court, Churchill County (Nevada), which upheld the validity of a tax sale of real property assessed by the county in an action against respondents, county trustee and property purchasers.


OVERVIEW: The property owners, each with an interest in the subject real property, brought an action to set aside a tax sale of the property, alleging that the tax sale was void because the county failed give them proper notice under Nev. Rev. Stat. § 361.565. The trial court entered judgment in favor of respondents. On appeal, the court reversed the trial court's decision and held that the county did not comply with the strict requirements of § 361.565 because they attempted to notify only one of the property owners of the tax assessment and sale of property. The court found that under § 361.565, the county was required to name all property owners in its published delinquency notice, attempt locate addresses for all property owners in order to send personal notice by first class mail, and serve notice upon all the property owners. The court concluded that because the county did not follow the requirement of § 361.565, it did not have the authority to conduct a tax sale of the property. The court remanded the case to the trial court with instructions to enter judgment quieting title to the land in the property owners.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment in favor of respondents and remanded the matter to the trial court with instructions to enter judgment quieting title to the land in the property owners.

Mishler v. State Bd. of Medical Examiners


No. 22397


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


109 Nev. 287; 849 P.2d 291; 1993 Nev. LEXIS 49



March 24, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied July 7, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from an order dismissing a petition for judicial review with respect to a decision by the State of Nevada Board of Medical Examiners to issue a public reprimand and to impose restrictions on appellant's reapplication for a medical license in Nevada. Second Judicial District Court, Washoe County; Brent T. Adams, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant physician sought review of a decision of respondent, the State of Nevada Board of Medical Examiners (board), to issue a public reprimand and to impose restrictions on the physician's reapplication for a medical license in Nevada. The Second Judicial District Court, Washoe County (Nevada), dismissed the physician's petition for judicial review, and the physician appealed.


OVERVIEW: Three years after the physician spoke out about another physician's incompetence and his colleagues retaliated by searching hospital records for anything negative about him, the board filed its complaint against the physician. The board refused the physician's request that it provide him with various documents and X-rays, stating that it was the physician's responsibility to secure the same. On appeal, the court held that the testimony of the board's expert, who practiced in California, was properly admitted because it was based on a national standard of care. However, the court held that the hearing officer erred in admitting hospital records without X-rays and other radiographs and in ruling that their absence was the physician's fault because the physician did not have access to them and the board obstructed his access. The court further held that the board's actions warranted dismissal of the charges against the physician. Finally, the court held that, due to the absence of important records, the evidence did not support the board's findings with respect to certain cases and that the discipline was unwarranted in light of the true nature of the facts.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the disciplinary order of the board in its entirety and dismissed all proceedings against the physician with prejudice.

Nevada Dep't of Taxation v. Scotsman Mfg. Co.

SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state appealed from a summary judgment order of the First Judicial District Court, Carson City (Nevada) that, upon remand, entered judgment in favor respondent taxpayer and ordered the state to refund an unlawfully exacted tax to the taxpayer. The state challenged the district court's jurisdiction to order the refund.


OVERVIEW: On a previous occasion, the court determined that a sales tax levied by the state against the taxpayer was unconstitutional. As a result of that ruling, the court remanded the matter to the district court and directed the entry of summary judgment in favor of the taxpayer. On remand, the district court entered summary judgment in the taxpayer's favor and ordered the state to refund the unlawfully exacted tax. The state appealed, challenging the district court's jurisdiction to order the refund. The court concluded that the district court had jurisdiction to order a refund of the tax payments and therefore affirmed the judgment of the district court. The court found that the district court's order requiring the refund logically followed from the court's conclusion in the prior appeal that the tax was illegally imposed and that the taxpayer was entitled to summary judgment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a summary judgment order of the district court that, upon remand, entered judgment in favor of the taxpayer and ordered the state to refund an unlawfully exacted tax to the taxpayer.

SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA

March 18, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals from judgments of conviction of four counts of child sexual abuse. First Judicial District Court, Carson City; Michael R. Griffin, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed from their judgments of conviction of four counts of child sexual abuse by the First Judicial District Court, Carson City (Nevada).


OVERVIEW: Defendants were convicted of child sexual abuse primarily on the statements of two six year old girls who had not been in the care of the defendants for over a year at the time of their accusations. The court reversed the convictions, finding that one of the girls could not differentiate between fact and fantasy, and the lower court had failed to examine the other girl to determine her competency, thus both girls were incompetent to testify. Further, the court's failure to determine the necessity of having one of the girls shielded while testifying at the preliminary hearing was improper. Additionally, the court found that the hearsay testimony of the other girls was improperly admitted because the court did not make a determination that the statements were reliable and that the girl was unavailable to testify under Nev. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 51.385.


OUTCOME: Judgment of conviction for each defendant was reversed because the testimony of the two six year old girls upon which the convictions were based was improperly admitted.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant electrical subcontractor (subcontractor) sought review of a decision by the Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County (Nevada), which refused the subcontractor's requests to enjoin application of Nev. Rev. Stat. § 338.160(5) and for the immediate release of payments withheld on order of respondent labor commissioner (commissioner).


OVERVIEW: The subcontractor was retained for work on two public works projects. The commissioner received a letter from the subcontractor's electricians that the subcontractor was not paying them the correct prevailing wage. Thereafter, pursuant to Nev. Rev. The court noted that the commissioner should have set a date for hearing upon his determination to withhold the monies, but that his failure to do so did not render Nev. Rev. Stat. § 338.160(5) unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment refusing the subcontractor's requests was affirmed.

OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested for driving under the influence of alcohol, and defendant was charged by criminal information with driving under the influence of alcohol and driving with a blood alcohol level of 0.10 percent or more. Stumpf v. Lau


No. 23517


Supreme Court of Nevada


108 Nev. 826; 839 P.2d 120; 1992 Nev. LEXIS 154



September 18, 1992  
September 18, 1992, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original proceedings in mandamus.



DISPOSITION: Writ made permanent.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner voters brought an original proceeding in mandamus against respondent Secretary of State to remove a Congressional term limit initiative from the ballot. The court earlier issued an alternate writ of mandamus that ordered the secretary of state to either remove the initiative from the ballot or show cause why the initiative proposal should not be rejected.


OVERVIEW: The court issued the earlier alternative writ on three grounds: (1) the act violated the United States Constitution, which set the terms and qualifications of Congressional members; (2) there was a lack of sufficient valid signatures on the initiative petition; and (3) the initiative proposal was so poorly drafted that it was unclear if it was intended to enact a law or amend the state constitution. In the mandamus hearing, the proponents did not contest that the act would be legally ineffective but rather urged the court to allow the voters to express themselves in a de facto straw poll. The proponents argued that the act could be challenged later if it passed. The court found that the act clearly and palpably violated the qualifications clause of U.S. Const. art. I and that there was no possible constitutional manner to implement it, that the affidavits on petition documents from two counties were attested by non-voters and, thus, were invalid under Nev. Const. art. 19, § 3(1) because the persons were not "signers," and, that the failure to specify the nature and purpose of the initiative was not merely an obscurity of language but was a fatal omission.


OUTCOME: The court held that it would be irresponsible of the court to allow a clearly defective act to stay on the ballot and to treat the initiative as a straw poll. The court made the writ of mandamus permanent and ordered the secretary of state to remove the matter from the ballot.

Eberle v. State ex rel. Redfield Trust


No. 21492


Supreme Court of Nevada


108 Nev. 587; 836 P.2d 67; 1992 Nev. LEXIS 122



August 10, 1992  
August 10, 1992, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from post-judgment order granting a motion for expert witness fees. Second Judicial District Court, Washoe County; Deborah A. Agosti, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant individuals who sought incorporation of a city (individuals) challenged the decision of the Second Judicial District Court, Washoe County (Nevada), which granted the motion of respondent owners of large pieces of property within the proposed new city (owners) for expert witness fees and costs after the district court entered a final judgment in the action.


OVERVIEW: The individuals tried to incorporate a new city pursuant to Nev. Rev. Stat. ch. 266. The district court held that chapter 266 was unconstitutional. While an appeal of the district court's decision was pending, the legislature amended chapter 266. The court dismissed the appeal as moot. The district court permanently enjoined the individuals from attempting to incorporate under chapter 266 as it existed prior to amendment and dismissed the action. The district court awarded the owners expert witness fees and costs. On appeal, the court held that although the district court did not grant further time for filing the motion, by granting the motion, the district court either considered the motion to be timely, or impliedly granted the owners additional time within which to file the motion. The statutory period of Nev. Rev. Stat. 18.110(1) was not a jurisdictional requirement. The court held that because the court had found the issues on appeal to be moot, there was no party in whose favor judgment was rendered. Neither party prevailed in the action. The action was terminated by the legislature. Thus, the district court erred in awarding expert witness fees and costs to the owners.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the district court's order, which had granted expert witness fees and costs to the owners.

State Envtl. Comm'n v. John Lawrence Nev.


No. 22121


Supreme Court of Nevada


108 Nev. 431; 834 P.2d 408; 1992 Nev. LEXIS 92



July 6, 1992  
July 6, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied August 31, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from an order of the district court granting respondent's petition for judicial review, and reversing orders of appellant State Environmental Commission. First Judicial District Court, Carson City; Michael E. Fondi, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded with instructions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants state environmental commission sought review of the judgment of the district court (Nevada), which reversed its order that affirmed notices sent by the Nevada Department of Conservation & Natural Resources, Division of Environmental Protection (DEP) to respondent corporation regarding violations of regulations involving dust disturbances.


OVERVIEW: The corporation was issued an air quality permit by the DEP. The permit allowed the corporation to construct a subdivision and golf course. The corporation was required to control fugitive dust from disturbed areas by using the best practical methods. Despite the corporation's efforts to control the dust, the DEP served 12 notices of violations. The commission affirmed seven of the notices. The trial court reversed and vacated the notices and fines. On a challenge by the DEP and commission the court reversed. The court found that the requirement that the corporation control the dust was not unconstitutional vague. The corporation had clear notice that it was in violation of the regulation. The requirements were not arbitrarily enforced as notices were issued only when the dust was out of control. The court found that the trial court erred in rejecting the DEP's interpretation of the regulation.


OUTCOME: The court reversed with instructions to reinstate the notices.

 

100 of 423 DOCUMENTS


Gaming Comm'n v. Southwest Sec.


No. 22264


Supreme Court of Nevada


108 Nev. 379; 832 P.2d 387; 1992 Nev. LEXIS 80



May 18, 1992  
May 18, 1992, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from summary judgment reversing the decision of the Nevada Gaming Commission. Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County; Gerard Bongiovanni, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded with instructions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Nevada Gaming Commission challenged a decision from the Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County (Nevada), which reversed the Commission's decision and granted respondent casino's motion for summary judgment. The district court held that the annual slot machine tax imposed by Nev. Rev. Stat. § 463.385 was not an excise tax and therefore was subject to the prohibition against double taxation.


OVERVIEW: The property owner leased its land to a company that operated a hotel and casino. When the company filed for bankruptcy, the bankruptcy trustees conducted the gaming and paid the annual slot machine taxes. The Gaming Commission licensed the property owner to take over the gaming operations and required the owner to pay a prorated annual slot machine tax. It sought a refund from the Gaming Commission, alleging that an overpayment resulted because the bankruptcy trustees had already paid the tax on the same machines for the same time period. The owner argued that the annual slot machine tax imposed by Nev. Rev. Stat. § 463.385 was a personal property tax. The Gaming Commission contended the tax was a privilege tax incident to the operation of slot machines. The district court granted the owner's motion for summary judgment, and the Gaming Commission appealed. The court held the annual slot machine tax was an excise tax because the tax was based upon the privilege of using property, rather than the value and ownership of the property. The Gaming Commission properly collected the prorated tax in advance from the property owner who began operation during the fiscal year.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the district court's summary judgment in favor of the property owner and remanded with instructions to enter summary judgment in favor of the Gaming Commission. The annual slot machine tax was an excise tax based upon the privilege of using property that could be imposed more than once during the same tax period if the ownership of the slot machines changed.

 

101 of 423 DOCUMENTS


Redmen v. State


No. 21729


Supreme Court of Nevada


108 Nev. 227; 828 P.2d 395; 1992 Nev. LEXIS 62



March 13, 1992  
March 13, 1992, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a judgment of conviction for robbery with the use of a deadly weapon and first degree murder with the use of a deadly weapon and a sentence of death imposed by a three-judge panel. Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County; Jack Lehman, Judge; Second Judicial District Court, Washoe County; Robin Anne Wright, Judge; Fifth Judicial District Court, Esmeralda, Mineral and Nye Counties; Paul C. Parraguirre, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction and death sentence from the trial court (Nevada), for robbery with the use of a deadly weapon and first-degree murder with the use of a deadly weapon on the basis of a denial of his right to a speedy trial, various claimed evidentiary errors, the claimed unconstitutionality of Nev. Rev. Stat. § 175.556, and equal protection challenges.


OVERVIEW: Defendant shot a stranger he had met and mutilated his body to make identification harder. The jury convicted him and a three-judge panel was convened to determine his sentence of death. On appeal, the court affirmed his conviction. Nev. Rev. Stat. § 178.556 provided that defendant was to be brought to trial within 60 days of the filing of the indictment or information. The prosecutor's trying of another death penalty case was good cause to continue and reset the trial date. It was not error to admit photos of the victim's mutilated body at the penalty phase because it proved the aggravating circumstance of mutilation. It was not error to instruct the jury on the felony murder rule even if it was not alleged in the indictment. The jury instruction that murder committed in preparation of felony carried a conclusive presumption of malice aforethought was not erroneous. The state did not err in calling witnesses during the penalty phase that were not endorsed as witnesses on the information. The record did not establish a lack of due diligence in discovering witnesses prior to trial. Nev. Rev. Stat. § 175.556, which authorized the use of a three-judge panel, was not unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for robbery with the use of a deadly weapon and first-degree murder with the use of a deadly weapon. The court affirmed his death sentences.

 

102 of 423 DOCUMENTS


Kazalyn v. State


No. 21429


Supreme Court of Nevada


108 Nev. 67; 825 P.2d 578; 1992 Nev. LEXIS 13



January 24, 1992  
January 24, 1992, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a judgment of conviction of murder with the use of a deadly weapon. Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County; Earle W. White, Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, vacated in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of conviction of murder with the use of a deadly weapon, an automobile, which was entered by the Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County (Nevada). He also challenged his sentence of life imprisonment, which was enhanced by a consecutive term of life imprisonment without the possibility of parole for the use of automobile as a deadly weapon.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's conviction was based upon the jury's finding in favor of the state that defendant incapacitated his wife with his car and left her lying in the roadway to be hit by another vehicle. He argued that there was insufficient evidence to convict him of first degree murder, that statements made to the police regarding his willingness to take a polygraph examination should not have been admitted into evidence, and that the enhanced penalty for use of the car as a deadly weapon was improper. The court affirmed the conviction but vacated the consecutive life sentence for the use of the car as a deadly weapon. The court held that (1) there was more than sufficient evidence upon which a reasonable jury could have found defendant guilty beyond a reasonable doubt, (2) admission of defendant's offers to take a polygraph examination was harmless error, and (3) defendant's sentence was erroneously enhanced with an additional, consecutive, life term for the use of the car as a deadly weapon because an automobile was not a deadly weapon.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for murder and his life sentence. However, the court vacated the consecutive life sentence that was imposed on defendant for use of his car as a deadly weapon.

Dawson v. State


No. 21799


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


108 Nev. 112; 825 P.2d 593; 1992 Nev. LEXIS 25



January 24, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Rehearing Denied May 18, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from an order of the district court denying appellant's petition for post-conviction relief. Eighth Judicial District, Clark County; Earle W. White, Jr. Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant inmate, who had been convicted of first degree murder, sought review of the judgment of the Eighth Judicial District, Clark County (Nevada), which denied his petition for post-conviction relief because none of his claims of ineffective counsel warranted relief.


OVERVIEW: The inmate had been convicted of first degree murder and sentenced to death. On appeal, the court affirmed the district court's denial of his petition for post-conviction relief because none of his claims of ineffective assistance of counsel warranted relief because: (1) The failure to impeach the victim's husband was not deficient; (2) Counsel conducted a reasonable investigation into an incident and thereafter reasonably pursued another line of defense; (3) Counsel did not have adequate grounds to object to jury instructions; and (4) The failure to move to exclude a witness's testimony was not prejudicial, as the district court excised her reference to the inmate's prior criminal act.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the district court denying the inmate's petition for post-conviction relief.

 

104 of 423 DOCUMENTS


State Employees Ass'n v. Daines


No. 22590


Supreme Court of Nevada


108 Nev. 15; 824 P.2d 276; 1992 Nev. LEXIS 8



January 2, 1992  
January 2, 1992, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original petition for a writ of mandamus.



DISPOSITION: Petition granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, state employees and employee association, sought a writ of mandamus compelling respondent state controller to issue warrants for the employees' salaries, including a four percent pay raise.


OVERVIEW: The state legislature passed and the governor signed a bill appropriating funds for a four percent salary increase for classified state employees. The board of examiners deferred allocation and disbursement of the funds appropriated for the salary adjustments because of a projected budget shortfall. Consequently, the controller refused to issue warrants sufficient to pay the salary increases on the date specified in the bill. The employees filed this action to compel issuance of the warrants. The court concluded that pursuant to Nev. Rev. Stat. § 227.160 the controller had a non-discretionary duty resulting from his office to pay the salary increases enacted by the legislature. The executive branch, represented by the board of examiners whose membership included the governor, was not empowered to disregard the mandate of the legislature that certain salaries be paid. There was no constitutional or statutory authority for the actions of the board of examiners. A writ of mandamus was issued to compel the controller to issue the warrants.


OUTCOME: The court granted a writ of mandamus as requested by the employees and the employee association.

Beenstock v. Villa Borega Mobile Home Parks


No. 21202


Supreme Court of Nevada


107 Nev. 979; 823 P.2d 270; 1991 Nev. LEXIS 201



December 26, 1991  
December 26, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a district court judgment denying appellants relief from a lease in respondents' mobile home park. Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County; Thomas A. Foley, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff tenants filed an action against defendant landlords seeking relief from a lease in defendants' mobile home park. The Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County (Nevada) granted judgment in favor of the landlords. The tenants appealed.


OVERVIEW: The landlords offered promotional long-term leases, featuring predetermined rental increases and rents below those in comparable spaces in other mobile home parks. The tenants holding long-term leases would become month-to-month tenants when their leases expired. The tenants opposed a rent increase to monthly tenants as violative of Nev. Rev. Stat. § 118B.150(1)(a), because the increases were not the same amount for each month-to-month tenant. The landlords proposed a new long term lease with increases that kept the rents below market rate. The tenants opposed that lease asserting that the rent adjustment under the long-term leases violated Nev. Rev. Stat. § 118B.150(1)(a) because it did not afford the same rent increases to all residents of the park. The landlords filed a motion for summary judgment. The trial court ruled that although § 118B.150(1)(a) applied to long-term leases, the statute unconstitutionally violates the due process clause, as it applied to the facts of the case. The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment in favor of the landlords, but on the basis that it concluded that the statute did not apply to long-term leases.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment in favor of the landlords in the tenants' action challenging the constitutionality of certain rent increases in long term leases was affirmed.

Ikie v. State


No. 21170


Supreme Court of Nevada


107 Nev. 916; 823 P.2d 258; 1991 Nev. LEXIS 196



December 20, 1991  
December 20, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from judgment of conviction of one count of larceny from the person. Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County; J. Charles Thompson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County (Nevada), which convicted him of one count of larceny from the person, in violation of Nev. Rev. Stat. § 205.270, and sentenced him to 10 years in prison.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of one count of larceny from the person, in violation of Nev. Rev. Stat. § 205.270, and was sentenced to 10 years in prison. Defendant sought review of the judgment. Pursuant to § 205.270, every person who, under circumstances not amounting to robbery, with intent to steal or appropriate his own use, took from another, without his consent, any money or thing of value, was to be punished by imprisonment for not less than 1 year nor more than 10 years. The court determined that the state was required to set forth in the information the specific acts constituting the means of aiding and abetting so as to provide defendant notice to prepare his defense. The court held that the state failed to set forth the aiding and abetting acts in the indictment. The court reversed the judgment of the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court reversed a judgment of the trial court, which convicted defendant of one count of larceny from the person and sentenced him to 10 years in prison.

Beets v. Nev.


No. 20694


Supreme Court of Nevada


107 Nev. 957; 821 P.2d 1044; 1991 Nev. LEXIS 197



December 20, 1991  
December 20, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied March 3, 1992.
Writ of certiorari denied Beets v. Nevada, 506 U.S. 838, 113 S. Ct. 116, 121 L. Ed. 2d 73, 1992 U.S. LEXIS 5875 (1992)
Habeas corpus proceeding at, Motion granted by, Appeal dismissed by Beets v. State, 110 Nev. 339, 871 P.2d 357, 1994 Nev. LEXIS 38 (1994)
Habeas corpus proceeding at, Motion granted by, in part, Motion denied by, in part, Motion denied by Beets v. McDaniel, 2007 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 12317 (D. Nev., Feb. 12, 2007)
Writ of mandamus denied Beets v. Eighth Judicial Dist. Court of Nev., 2011 Nev. Unpub. LEXIS 11 (2011)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from convictions pursuant to jury verdict of first degree murder with use of a deadly weapon, attempted murder with use of a deadly weapon, mayhem with use of a deadly weapon, first degree kidnaping with use of a deadly weapon, sexual assault with use of a deadly weapon, two counts of sexual assault with a minor, burglary, and a sentence of death pronounced by a three-judge panel. Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County; J. Charles Thompson, Judge; Third Judicial District Court, Lyon County; Archie E. Blake, Judge; First Judicial District Court, Carson City; Michael E. Fondi, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a trial court (Nevada), defendant was found guilty of first degree murder with use of a deadly weapon, attempted murder with use of a deadly weapon, mayhem with use of a deadly weapon, first degree kidnapping with use of a deadly weapon, sexual assault with use of a deadly weapon, two counts of sexual assault with a minor, and burglary. He was sentenced to death by a three-judge panel. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant broke into the victim's home and assaulted her with a hammer, both physically and sexually. He hit the victim's mother with the hammer and killed her. He also sexually assaulted the victim's minor daughter. After being convicted, a three-judge panel found no mitigating circumstances, found four aggravating circumstances, and sentenced defendant to death. On appeal, the court affirmed the convictions and sentence. The court found that the jury could have, based on the evidence, been reasonably convinced beyond a reasonable doubt that he killed the victim's mother with premeditation. While the trial court did give an erroneous jury instruction, it was harmless because the court did not believe that the jury would have returned an acquittal but for the instructional error. The court held that the aggravating circumstance based on depravity of mind failed because there was no predicate for a finding of torture beyond killing the mother with a hammer. However, the court allowed the death sentence to stand because of the weight properly according to the remaining valid aggravating circumstances.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions and death sentence.

State v. Rosenthal


No. 21216


Supreme Court of Nevada


107 Nev. 772; 819 P.2d 1296; 1991 Nev. LEXIS 167



October 30, 1991  
October 30, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from an order of the district court granting respondent's petition for judicial review and expunging respondent from appellants' List of Excluded Persons. Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County; Joseph S. Pavlikowski, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, state and state gaming commission, sought review of an order of the Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County (Nevada), which granted respondent gambler's petition for judicial review and expunged respondent from appellants' list of excluded persons who could not be employed with gambling institutions due to previous convictions, as provided for in Nev. Rev. Stat. § 463.151(3).


OVERVIEW: Respondent gambler was placed on a list of persons excluded from employment at gambling institutions, by appellants, state and state gaming commission. Respondent filed a petition for judicial review, and the trial court expunged defendant from the list of excluded persons, ruling that appellant commission's decision to include respondent on the list was arbitrary and capricious, that the exclusion order deprived respondent of due process of law because substantial prejudice resulted from appellant commission's delay in following through with the proceedings, and that respondent's prior gambling conviction was improperly considered. The court reversed, holding that the decision by appellants was not arbitrary and capricious because the decision to exclude respondent was based on criteria set forth in Nev. Rev. Stat. § 463.151(3). A finding of any one of the criteria was sufficient for inclusion on the list. The decision by appellants to include respondent on the list due to a prior conviction was proper, as proceedings to revoke a license were not included among disabilities that were released by an honorable discharge from probation.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the trial court granting respondent gambler's petition for judicial review and expunging him from the list of excluded persons of appellants, state and state gaming commission. Appellants' decision to include respondent on the list was not arbitrary or capricious as the decision was based on statutory criteria. Respondent was convicted of a gambling offense and was associated with organized crime.

Dressler v. State


No. 21088


Supreme Court of Nevada


107 Nev. 686; 819 P.2d 1288; 1991 Nev. LEXIS 164



October 24, 1991  
October 24, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a judgment of conviction of one count of driving under the influence of alcohol, third offense. Ninth Judicial District Court, Douglas County; David R. Gamble, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following a bench trial, the Ninth Judicial District Court, Douglas County (Nevada) convicted defendant of one count of driving under the influence of alcohol with two or more prior convictions, in violation of Nev. Rev. Stat. §§ 484.379, 484.3792(1)(c), and sentenced defendant to serve a term of two years in state prison. Defendant appealed his conviction.


OVERVIEW: Subsequent to his conviction, defendant contended that the district court erred in permitting the state to amend the information of one prior conviction after the verdict to reflect that the conviction had occurred in a county other than the one stated on the conviction and in considering evidence of another prior conviction. The court affirmed. The court stated the inaccuracy in describing the prior conviction had not prejudiced defendant and thus the information, even without amendment, was sufficient to allow the state to use the conviction for enhancement purposes. The court found that in regard to the evidence of the other prior conviction: (1) the record demonstrated that defendant was represented by counsel throughout the proceedings; and (2) because defendant made no attempt in the district court to show that his prior conviction had not been constitutionally obtained -- thus failing to rebut the presumption that the prior conviction was constitutionally obtained -- the district court properly relied on the record of that conviction in enhancing defendant's sentence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction in district court.

Childs v. State


No. 21373


Supreme Court of Nevada


107 Nev. 584; 816 P.2d 1079; 1991 Nev. LEXIS 145



September 6, 1991  
September 6, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a judgment of conviction, pursuant to a jury verdict, of one count of cheating at gambling and one count of burglary. Second Judicial District Court, Washoe County; Roy L. Torvinen, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the Second Judicial District Court, Washoe County (Nevada) that convicted him, pursuant to a jury verdict, of the crimes of burglary and cheating at gambling.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's convictions stemmed from his activities in a casino. A manager for the casino in question testified that she observed defendant engage in handle popping by his act of jerking on the handle of a slot machine in such a way that one of three reels would stop spinning prematurely. On appeal, defendant asked for a reversal on the ground that Nev. Rev. Stat. § 465.070(7) was unconstitutionally vague. The court reversed defendant's judgment of conviction, holding that handle manipulation did not alter the physical characteristics and potential pay offs of slot machines and therefore did not constitute cheating under Nev. Rev. Stat. § 465.015. The court stated that there were no rules directing slot machine patrons to pull the handles in a specific manner. The court further noted that if the State and the gaming industry desired to make handle popping or handle manipulation of slot machines a crime, it was necessary to do so in clearly expressed, specific statutory terms.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment that convicted defendant of the crimes of burglary and cheating at gambling.

 

111 of 423 DOCUMENTS


W. Heritage Thrift & Loan v. Cloutier


No. 21299


Supreme Court of Nevada


107 Nev. 471; 813 P.2d 999; 1991 Nev. LEXIS 116



June 28, 1991  
June 28, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from an order of the district court granting respondents' motion to set aside a foreign judgment. Second Judicial District Court, Washoe County; Roy L. Torvinen, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant creditor sought review of an order of the Second Judicial District Court, Washoe County (Nevada), which granted respondent debtors' motion to set aside the foreign judgment filed by the creditor with the district court under the Uniform Foreign Judgments Act, Nev. Rev. Stat. §§ 17.330-17.400.


OVERVIEW: The creditor obtained a Utah deficiency judgment against the debtors and filed it with the district court under the Uniform Foreign Judgments Act. The district court granted the debtors' motion for dismissal of the foreign judgment, and the creditor appealed. The court affirmed the district court's judgment, holding that while the district court erred in declaring the Utah long-arm statute under Utah Code Ann. § 78-27-41(1) unconstitutional, the district court's refusal to apply the Utah statute was correct as an "as applied" due process violation. The court held that because the cause of action did not arise out of the debtors' acts in the forum, the assertion of specific jurisdiction was unreasonable. The creditor failed to establish that the debtors "reached out" to Utah when they leased their backhoe and trailer, and the debtors' contacts with Utah were insufficient to support the exercise of specific jurisdiction by the Utah court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the district court's judgment, which granted the debtors' motion to set aside the foreign judgment filed by the creditor with the district court.

Huebner v. State


No. 21728


Supreme Court of Nevada


107 Nev. 328; 810 P.2d 1209; 1991 Nev. LEXIS 52



May 6, 1991  
May 6, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Proper person petition for rehearing. Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County; John F. Mendoza and Jeffrey D. Sobel, District Judges.



DISPOSITION: Rehearing granted; appeal reinstated; instructions to district court clerks issued.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant prisoner filed a petition for rehearing, appealing from the order of the Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County (Nevada) that denied his petition for post-conviction relief.


OVERVIEW: Following the district court's denial of the prisoner's petition for post-conviction relief, the prisoner's appeal from the order was dismissed on the ground that the appeal was untimely. In his petition for rehearing, the prisoner alleged that the court incorrectly concluded that it lacked jurisdiction to entertain his appeal because the record on appeal indicated that he mailed his notice of appeal to the clerk of the district court prior to the required deadline. The court remanded the matter to the district court with instructions that it determine the date on which the prisoner's notice of appeal was received into the custody of the district court clerk. The district court thereafter entered formal written findings, which stated that an incoming notice of appeal could remain in the officer of the district court clerk for an undetermined period of time before it was actually filed. The court granted the motion for rehearing and reinstated the appeal, holding that because it could not be determined whether the prisoner's notice of appeal was received into the custody of the district court clerk in a timely fashion, the ambiguity had to be resolved in favor of the prisoner.


OUTCOME: The court granted the prisoner's motion for rehearing and reinstated his appeal from the district court's order denying his motion for post-conviction relief.

 

113 of 423 DOCUMENTS


Riley v. State


No. 21240


Supreme Court of Nevada


107 Nev. 205; 808 P.2d 551; 1991 Nev. LEXIS 34



March 28, 1991  
March 28, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied May 9, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment of conviction and from a sentence of death. Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County; Joseph Pavlikowski, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County (Nevada), which convicted him of first degree murder with the use of a deadly weapon and robbery with the use of a deadly weapon and sentenced him to two consecutive life terms, the sentence of death, and no possibility of parole.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of first degree murder with use of a deadly weapon and robbery with use of a deadly weapon after killing a man with a saw-off shot gun. He was sentenced to two consecutive terms of life, the death sentence, and no possibility of parole. Defendant appealed, claiming that the evidence was insufficient to support the convictions, the trial court erred by rejecting his request fore a bench trial, and the prosecutor committed prejudicial misconduct during the trial. On appeal, the court affirmed, ruling that there was ample evidence to support the jury's finding of guilt and the subsequent convictions, including the fact that the murder weapon belonged to defendant, his discussion with the victim that he intended to kill him and his control over the murder weapon at all times during the commission of the crime. The trial court did not err in refusing defendant's request for a bench trial because there was no constitutional right to compel a bench trial. Finally, the court found that the prosecutor's conduct of misstating facts and maligning defendant's counsel did not warrant a reversal in light of the strength of the evidence of defendant's guilt.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, which convicted defendant of first degree murder with the use of a deadly weapon and robbery with the use of a deadly weapon sentencing him to two consecutive terms of life, including the death sentence, with no possibility of parole.

 

114 of 423 DOCUMENTS


Lord v. State


No. 20660


Supreme Court of Nevada


107 Nev. 28; 806 P.2d 548; 1991 Nev. LEXIS 6



February 7, 1991  
February 7, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Habeas corpus proceeding at, Remanded by Lord v. McDaniel, 2004 U.S. App. LEXIS 17031 (9th Cir. Nev., Aug. 16, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from judgment of conviction and from sentence of death. Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County; Earle W. White, Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part; remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County (Nevada), which convicted him of first-degree murder, robbery with a deadly weapon, and conspiracy to commit robbery and/or murder, and sentenced him to death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of first-degree murder, robbery with a deadly weapon, and conspiracy to commit robbery and/or murder, and was sentenced to death. The court held that any error due to the prosecutor's misstatement of evidence during opening argument was harmless. The court held that the evidence did not warrant an instruction on possession of stolen property. The court also held that the district court abused its discretion in denying the defense request for a half-day continuance to permit six out-of-state witnesses to testify during the penalty phase. The court further held that it was prejudicial error for the district court to have allowed a detective to read to the jury a transcript of a co-defendant's confession during the penalty phase. The convictions were affirmed, and the sentences were affirmed in part and reversed and remanded in part.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's three convictions because the errors assigned by defendant did not require reversal of the guilt phase. The court reversed the sentence of death and remanded, holding that the penalty phase had to be reversed because the district court abused its discretion in denying the reasonable defense request for a half-day continuance to allow out-of-state witnesses to testify and because the rule of Bruton applied.

 

115 of 423 DOCUMENTS


State v. American Bankers Ins. Co.


No. 20791


Supreme Court of Nevada


106 Nev. 880; 802 P.2d 1276; 1990 Nev. LEXIS 168



December 20, 1990 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from district court order exonerating bail bonds. Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County; J. Charles Thompson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state challenged an order of the Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County (Nevada), which exonerated respondent surety's bail bond. The state issued the notices of intent to forfeit the bonds, pursuant to Nev. Rev. Stat. § 178.508 (1987), on the day the accused failed to appear, but the notices were not mailed to the surety until 20 days later.


OVERVIEW: The surety posted bail bonds for a criminal who failed to appear before the court. Notices of intent to forfeit the bonds were issue and dated on the same day, but were not mailed for 20 days. The bonds were forfeited, 90 days later, pursuant to Nev. Rev. Stat. § 178.508 (1987). The lower court exonerated the bonds. On appeal, the court affirmed the lower court's decision. The forfeiture was improper because the 15 day notice deadline of § 178.508 was mandatory and notice was sent to respondents five days beyond the statutory period. Adherence to the specified notice period was essential to effectuating the legislature's enactment of a "bright line" rule. The 15-day notice requirement to a surety constituted a basically nonjudicial action of a ministerial nature, occurring after a judicial function had taken place and before a final resolution of the dispute. The 1987 amendments to § 178.508 facilitated the fair and orderly administration of the bail bond business and did not infringe upon judicial functions and prerogatives.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the lower court exonerating the bail bonds.

 

116 of 423 DOCUMENTS


Buschauer v. State


No. 20820


Supreme Court of Nevada


106 Nev. 890; 804 P.2d 1046; 1990 Nev. LEXIS 171; 59 U.S.L.W. 2446



December 20, 1990 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from judgment of conviction of one count of involuntary manslaughter with a deadly weapon pursuant to plea. Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County; Miriam Shearing, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part; vacated in part; remanded with instructions. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County (Nevada), convicting him of involuntary manslaughter with a deadly weapon in the accidental shooting of his wife and sentencing him to the maximum sentence of six years for involuntary manslaughter plus a consecutive six years for use of a deadly weapon pursuant to Nev. Rev. Stat. § 193.165.


OVERVIEW: On review, the court reversed defendant's six-year base sentence for involuntary manslaughter because inclusion of the reference to the polygraph results in the presentence report was error. Polygraph results that were inadmissible at trial absent written stipulation of the parties also were inadmissible at the sentencing stage of criminal proceedings. Further, the court held that due process required notice, oath, and cross-examination in connection with the victim's oral impact statement given pursuant to Nev. Rev. Stat. § 176.015(3) because the statement included several accusations of specific prior acts by defendant. The court vacated the enhancement of defendant's sentence for use of a deadly weapon under Nev. Rev. Stat. § 193.165, because, by definition, the crime of involuntary manslaughter did not involve use of weapon in conscious furtherance of a crime. The deadly weapon enhancement of § 193.165 thus did not apply to the unintentional crime of involuntary manslaughter.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's six-year base sentence for involuntary manslaughter, vacated the six-year enhancement for use of a deadly weapon, and remanded with instructions for resentencing.

Starlets Int'l v. Christensen


No. 19802


Supreme Court of Nevada


106 Nev. 732; 801 P.2d 1343; 1990 Nev. LEXIS 145; 15 A.L.R.5th 1118



November 28, 1990 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from order dismissing complaint for injunctive relief and confirming constitutionality of Clark County Code § 6.140. Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County; Michael J. Wendell, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, an outcall promoter and an entertainer, sought review of the decision from the Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County (Nevada), which granted summary judgment in favor of respondents, county commissioners, the sheriff, and the director of business licenses (county officials), on a complaint to enjoin a county ordinance and have the ordinance declared unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The county adopted an ordinance, Clark County, Nev. Code § 6.140.010, in response to the transformation of prohibited illegal prostitution businesses from escort services to outcall entertainment. The outcall promoter and the entertainer filed a complaint to enjoin the ordinance and have it declared unconstitutional. The trial court granted summary judgment to the county government officials. The outcall promoter and the entertainer sought review. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment of the trial court. The court held that the ordinance was reasonably and rationally related to a legitimate government interest as a weapon to combat prostitution. The court found that the right to engage in prostitution or other illegal activity was not encompassed in the right of association and the ordinance properly required information, such as the name of the entertainer and the name of the patron. The court determined the ordinance met the due process standard of being clear and was not violative of due process requirements in its licensing requirements.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court that granted summary judgment to the county officials on the complaint of the outcall promoter and the entertainer.

 

118 of 423 DOCUMENTS


Choose Life Campaign '90' v. Del Papa


No. 21325


Supreme Court of Nevada


106 Nev. 802; 801 P.2d 1384; 1990 Nev. LEXIS 155



November 28, 1990 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from order dismissing petition for injunctive and other extraordinary relief. First Judicial District Court, Carson City; Michael R. Griffin, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Writ of mandamus issued; appeal dismissed. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff abortion opponents appealed from an order of the First Judicial District Court, Carson City (Nevada) that granted intervenor abortion proponents' motion to dismiss their petition for injunctive and other extraordinary relief. The trial court held that the secretary of state's pro and con arguments placed on a sample ballot, pursuant to Nev. Rev. Stat. § 293.250(5), did not violate the abortion opponents' due process rights.


OVERVIEW: The abortion opponents claimed that two sentences in each of the pro and con arguments placed on a sample ballot pursuant to Nev. Rev. Stat. § 293.250(5) did not accurately represent the positions of any abortion opponent. The two sentences in essence informed the registered voters that they were determining whether the voters or the legislature should have the power to regulate abortions. The court issued a writ of mandamus that required the secretary of state to remove those sentences. While every referendum was essentially a vote to determine whether a certain power was to have been reserved to the voters, the court held that in this case that was not a fair representation of the abortion opponents' position on abortions. Therefore it was inappropriate for the secretary of state to have included those statements in the proposed language on the sample ballots. Furthermore, the abortion opponents did not have an adequate remedy at law due to the impending election, and the issue was of great importance, therefore, issuance of a writ of mandamus compelling the secretary of state to correct the injustice was appropriate.


OUTCOME: The court issued a writ of mandamus to compel the secretary of state to remove parts of the pro and con arguments from a sample ballot that led voters to believe they were determining whether the voters or the legislature was to regulate abortions, as sought by the abortion opponents.

Robins v. State


No. 20064


Supreme Court of Nevada


106 Nev. 611; 798 P.2d 558; 1990 Nev. LEXIS 113



September 19, 1990 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing denied December 18, 1990.
Writ of certiorari denied Robins v. Nevada, 499 U.S. 970, 111 S. Ct. 1608, 113 L. Ed. 2d 670, 1991 U.S. LEXIS 2096, 59 U.S.L.W. 3702 (1991)
Habeas corpus proceeding at, Motion granted by, in part, Motion denied by, in part, Motion denied by Robins v. Skolnik, 2010 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 83082 (D. Nev., Aug. 11, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from convictions of first degree murder and child abuse with substantial bodily harm and the sentence of death for the murder conviction and twenty years in prison for the child abuse conviction. Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County; Earle W. White, Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Eighth Judicial District Court of Clark County (Nevada), which convicted him of first degree murder and felony child abuse with substantial bodily harm. Defendant also challenged the validity of his death sentence.


OVERVIEW: The evidence adduced at trial demonstrated a pattern of abusive treatment of an eleven-month old child that ultimately resulted in the child's violent death. Defendant first contended that the trial court erred in failing to grant his motion for mistrial. At trial, an officer referenced defendant's possible drug involvement. The court held that the error, if any, was harmless because of the overwhelming evidence of guilt. Defendant also argued that he was unfairly prejudiced by the joinder of the child abuse charge and the first degree murder charge. The court found no abuse of the trial court's discretion in the joinder decision. Most, if not all, of the evidence relating to the child abuse was cross-admissible on the murder charge. Defendant also contended that he was unfairly prejudiced by objectionable expert testimony, but the court held that the child's physician was qualified to testify on the autopsy results and on battered children. Finally, the court affirmed defendant's death sentence, holding that derogatory character evidence was properly admitted in the penalty hearing as aggravating circumstances relative to the offense, pursuant to Nev. Rev. Stat. § 175.552.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence for first degree murder and felony child abuse with substantial bodily harm after finding that defendant was fairly tried and sentenced.
