Hayes v. State


No. 20036


Supreme Court of Nevada


106 Nev. 543; 797 P.2d 962; 1990 Nev. LEXIS 98



August 21, 1990 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing denied September 14, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from appellants' identical judgments of conviction, following a bench trial, of one count each of: trafficking in a controlled substance (methamphetamine), possession of a controlled substance (marijuana), possession of a controlled substance for the purpose of sale (methamphetamine), and conspiracy to sell a controlled substance (methamphetamine and/or marijuana). First Judicial District Court, Carson City; Michael R. Griffin, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed from a judgment of the First Judicial District Court, Carson City (Nevada), which convicted defendants of trafficking in a controlled substance, possession of a controlled substance, possession of a controlled substance for the purpose of sale, and conspiracy to sell a controlled substance.


OVERVIEW: Subsequent to their convictions on drug-related charges, defendants argued that the trial court erred in admitting evidence seized from the premises during a protective sweep search. On review, the court reversed the convictions on the drug charges. In reaching its conclusion, the court held that officers lacked sufficient reason to fear for their safety; thus, the protective sweep search was not justified. In support of its holding, the court found that the officers in prior cases in which protective sweep searches were justifiable were placed in more dangerous situations than the officers in the case at issue. Additionally, the court held a separate statutory reason for reversing the convictions of possession for purposes of sale existed because defendants were subject to a greater sentence based on charges of trafficking of the same controlled substance.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendants' convictions on each of the drug-related charges.

 

121 of 423 DOCUMENTS


Department of Motor Vehicles & Pub. Safety v. Hutchings


Nos. 20130, 20158


Supreme Court of Nevada


106 Nev. 453; 795 P.2d 497; 1990 Nev. LEXIS 87



July 18, 1990 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Consolidated appeals from a judgment in Case No. 20130; and from a denial of a petition for a writ of mandamus in Case No. 20158. Second Judicial District Court, Washoe County; Jerry C. Whitehead, Judge (No. 20130); James J. Guinan, Judge (No. 20158).



DISPOSITION: Case No. 20130 reversed; Case No. 20158 affirmed. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In consolidated suits pertaining to Nev. Rev. Stat. § 284.175(5), appellants, the State and others, challenged a judgment from the Second Judicial District Court, Washoe County (Nevada), which ordered a retroactive increase in respondent highway patrol officers' salaries. Appellants, state employees and others, challenged the denial of their petition for a writ of mandamus to compel respondents, the State and others, to increase their salaries.


OVERVIEW: Both the officers and the employees claimed that the State and their immediate employers violated § 284.175(5) by failing to set their salaries at prevailing rates as determined by surveys conducted by the Nevada Department of Personnel. The trial court found in favor of the officers, ordered their salaries to be adjusted immediately to the prevailing rates as determined by the most recent survey, and ruled that its decision was to apply retroactively to the date the legislature last convened. On appeal, the court ruled that § 284.175(5) did not mandate that the officers' or the employees' salaries be set at the prevailing rates as determined by the Department. Section 284.175(5) required that the salaries of Nevada's classified service employees, such as the officers and the employees, be "set based upon" prevailing rates. Had the legislature intended to require that such salaries be set "at" prevailing rates, it would have expressly so stated. In addition, by including the words "where appropriate" in § 284.175(5), the legislature indicated that it did not intend that prevailing rates would, in all cases, be determinative.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment that ordered an increase in the officers' salaries and affirmed the judgment that denied the employees' petition for a writ of mandamus.

 

122 of 423 DOCUMENTS


Slinkard v. State


No. 20499


Supreme Court of Nevada


106 Nev. 393; 793 P.2d 1330; 1990 Nev. LEXIS 71



June 28, 1990 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a judgment of conviction. Fourth Judicial District Court, Elko County; Joseph O. McDaniel, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment of the Fourth Judicial District Court, Elko County (Nevada), which convicted him, after a jury verdict, of driving with a blood alcohol level in excess of 0.10 percent, third offense, a felony under Nev. Rev. Stat. §§ 484.379(1), 484.3792(1)(c) and sentenced him to serve three years in prison and to pay a fine.


OVERVIEW: After an accident, blood samples were taken from which defendant's blood alcohol level was determined. The trial court refused to allow defendant to testify regarding what he believed that his blood alcohol level was at the time. Defendant argued that such refusal was prejudicial error. Further, he argued that Nevada driving under the influence (DUI) statutes were premised on the assumption that a person could know his blood alcohol level following consumption of liquor and that a person charged with DUI must have the ability to know his or her blood alcohol level, otherwise the DUI statutes would fail to meet constitutional requirements regarding notice of prohibited conduct. The court determined that a person who consumed a substantial amount of liquor and then drove was on sufficient notice that he could be in violation of the DUI statutes. Defendant was not competent to testify to his blood alcohol level, and he was not prejudiced because he could not have overcome the presumption that his level was at least as high as the test showed. Because knowledge of one's intoxication was not an element of the crime of DUI, the absence of such knowledge was not a defense.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Clark County Social Serv. Dep't v. Newkirk


No. 18903


Supreme Court of Nevada


106 Nev. 177; 789 P.2d 227; 1990 Nev. LEXIS 29



March 27, 1990 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing denied August 21, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal and cross-appeal from summary judgment and order permanently enjoining Clark County Social Services Department from denying single employable individuals and employable childless couples county welfare benefits. Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County; Myron E. Leavitt, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed; cross-appeal dismissed. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Clark County Social Services Department (social services) sought review of an order from the Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County (Nevada), which entered summary judgment permanently joining the social services from denying single employable individuals and employable childless couples county welfare benefits in respondent indigent citizen's action for relief under Nev. Rev. Stat. § 428.010(1).


OVERVIEW: The indigent citizen filed an application for benefits with social services. Social services denied the application based on an internal regulation categorizing the indigent citizen as employable. The indigent citizen brought suit against social services seeking injunctive relief. The district court granted summary judgment in favor of the indigent citizen on the ground that social services was required to provide him with care, support and relief under Nev. Rev. Stat. § 428.010(1). On appeal, the court affirmed the order. The court held that although social services was permitted to enact regulations setting standards for assistance eligibility, it was still required under § 428.010(1) to provide care and support for the indigent citizen. The court reasoned that the analysis as to whether or not social services was required to provide the indigent citizen with relief was simple because it was undisputed that the he was poor. The court held that the district court did not err in denying retroactive benefits to the indigent citizen. The court noted that the regulation was clearly in conflict with the state's mandate that counties care for their poor.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order granting summary judgment in favor of the indigent citizen and permanently enjoining social services from denying single employable individuals and employable childless couples county welfare benefits.

McKay v. Las Vegas


No. 19491


Supreme Court of Nevada


106 Nev. 203; 789 P.2d 584; 1990 Nev. LEXIS 33



March 27, 1990 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the district court's decision in a declaratory relief action and from the district court's denial of injunctive relief. Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County; Stephen L. Huffaker, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant attorney general sought review of an order from the Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County (Nevada), which entered a judgment for respondents, a city and its municipal judges. The trial court declared that the municipal judges had the power to declare state statutes unconstitutional and that Nev. Rev. Stat. § 176.059 was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The municipal judges issued an order announcing that they would not enforce the amendments to § 176.059 because the amendments provided a sliding scale assessment on court fines. But the attorney general filed a suit seeking a preliminary injunction preventing the judges from implementing their order. The trial court entered a judgment for respondents declaring that the municipal judges had the power to declare state statutes unconstitutional and that the amendments were unconstitutional. But on appeal, the court held that the trial court erred in declaring the judges' authority because the municipal judges' position was created by a statute that had not given them the authority to declare state statutes unconstitutional. The court also held that § 176.059 was a reasonable assessment as opposed to a tax. The court also held that the statute was not unconstitutional simply because a portion of the assessment was allotted for law enforcement purposes. Finally, the court held that the assessment was to be primarily used for court improvement and judicial capital acquisition.


OUTCOME: The court reversed an order from the trial court, which declared that the municipal judges had the power to declare state statutes unconstitutional and that an assessment statute was unconstitutional.

Bennett v. State


No. 19706


Supreme Court of Nevada


106 Nev. 135; 787 P.2d 797; 1990 Nev. LEXIS 21



February 23, 1990 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing denied April 17, 1990.
Writ of certiorari denied Bennett v. Nevada, 498 U.S. 925, 112 L. Ed. 2d 260, 111 S. Ct. 307, 1990 U.S. LEXIS 5320, 59 U.S.L.W. 3293 (1990)
Subsequent appeal at State v. Bennett, 2003 Nev. LEXIS 83 (2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: This is an appeal from a judgment of conviction and sentence of death following a jury trial. Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County; Miriam Shearing, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment from the Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County (Nevada), which convicted defendant upon a jury verdict of attempted robbery with use of a deadly weapon, murder with use of a deadly weapon, and attempted murder with the use of a deadly weapon and which sentenced him to death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant shot and killed a clerk during the robbery of a convenience store. At defendant's instruction, his accomplice shot a witness. When executing a search warrant for clothing at defendant's home, police officers seized incriminating poetry and arrested him. Defendant was convicted of robbery with use of a deadly weapon, murder with use of a deadly weapon, and attempted murder with the use of a deadly weapon. The aggravating circumstances were found to outweigh the mitigating circumstances and defendant was sentenced to death. On appeal, the court affirmed. The search of defendant's home and defendant's subsequent arrest were lawful. The trial court did not err by admitting the seized poetry pursuant to the plain view doctrine. Substantial evidence supported the jury's finding that defendant killed the victim without an apparent motive and the finding that he committed attempted robbery. Both the burglary and attempted robbery made the crime more heinous and could be stated as two separate aggravating factors. The sentence of death was not imposed under the influence of passion, prejudice, or any arbitrary factor, nor was it excessive considering both the crime and defendant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for robbery, murder, and attempted murder, all committed with a deadly weapon, and the death sentence imposed because of the aggravating circumstances involved in the crimes.

 

126 of 423 DOCUMENTS


Lucky v. State


No. 20048


Supreme Court of Nevada


105 Nev. 807; 783 P.2d 457; 1989 Nev. LEXIS 301



December 6, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from order denying a petition for a writ of habeas corpus. Second Judicial District Court, Washoe County; Robin A. Wright, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, who were each charged with bribery, were held in contempt of court after invoking their rights against self-incrimination under the Fifth Amendment at a preliminary hearing where they were called to testify pursuant to Nev. Rev. Stat. § 199.090. Defendants challenged the decision of the Second Judicial District Court, Washoe County (Nevada), which denied their petitions for a writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were charged in criminal complaints. One was charged with four counts of asking for or receiving a bribe by a public officer in violation of Nev. Rev. Stat. § 197.040. Another was charged with four counts of bribing a public officer in violation of Nev. Rev. Stat. § 197.020. The third was charged with one count of bribing a public officer in violation of Nev. Rev. Stat. § 197.020. They invoked their Fifth Amendment privilege at a preliminary hearing and were held in contempt. The court affirmed the lower court's decision denying their petitions for a writ of habeas corpus. The lower court correctly interpreted Nev. Rev. Stat. § 199.090 as providing defendants with derivative use immunity. Because crimes involving bribery and corruption of public officials were usually committed in secret, they were difficult to prosecute. Section 199.090, which mandated that those committing a crime of bribery could not be excused from giving testimony tending to incriminate himself, was clearly intended by the legislature to ease the burden of prosecuting offenses that involved the corruption of public officials.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the lower court, which denied the petitions for a writ of habeas corpus filed by defendants, who were held in contempt of court after refusing to testify at a preliminary hearing.

Shannon v. State


No. 18316


Supreme Court of Nevada


105 Nev. 782; 783 P.2d 942; 1989 Nev. LEXIS 306



December 6, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from judgment of conviction in case C74463 of lewdness with a minor, two counts of sexual assault, and two counts of solicitation of minor to engage in the infamous crime against nature and from judgment of conviction in case C76901 of one count of lewdness with a minor. Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County; Thomas A. Foley, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment from the Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County (Nevada) that convicted him of seven counts of lewdness with a minor, two counts of sexual assault, and two counts of solicitation of a minor to engage in an infamous crime against nature.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of seven counts of lewdness with a minor, two counts of sexual assault, and two counts of solicitation of a minor to engage in an infamous crime against nature. On appeal, defendant claimed it was error for the trial court to grant plaintiff state's motion to amend the information because the amended information had the effect of charging a different offense. The court found that defendant's substantial rights were not prejudiced by the amendment. The original complaint alleged that defendant committed sexual assault by inserting his penis into the mouth of a minor. The amended information transposed the sequence by stating that the minor's penis was inserted into the mouth of defendant. The original information alleged that the act of sexual penetration was accomplished by fellatio. After the amendment, defendant's charged offense remained sexual assault accomplished by fellatio. Defendant also argued that his solicitation convictions were mutually exclusive. The court agreed and vacated the felony convictions of the solicitation because the facts underlying the sexual assault charges were indistinguishable from the solicitation charges.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part defendant's convictions for lewdness with a minor and sexual assault, but reversed and vacated the felony convictions of the solicitation.

Naovarath v. State

Supreme Court of Nevada


105 Nev. 525; 779 P.2d 944; 1989 Nev. LEXIS 262



September 7, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from judgment of conviction for first degree murder and imposition of the sentence of life without possibility of parole. Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County; Miriam Shearing, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Sentence reduced from life imprisonment without the possibility of parole to life imprisonment with the possibility of parole. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A juvenile defendant appealed his sentence of life imprisonment without possibility of parole imposed by the Clark County District Court (Nevada) after his conviction for murder.


OVERVIEW: A 13-year old defendant challenged his sentence of life imprisonment without possibility of parole. Defendant killed a man who had been molesting him sexually and then stole the man's belongings. On appeal, the court reduced the sentence to life imprisonment with the possibility of parole and held that the sentence was cruel and unusual punishment for the mentally and emotionally disordered 13-year old defendant. The court found that adjudication of a 13-year old to be forever irredeemable and to subject a child of this age to hopeless, lifelong punishment and segregation was not a usual or acceptable response to childhood criminality, even when the criminality amounted to murder. The court also found that it was questionable as to whether a 13-year old could even imagine or comprehend what it meant to be imprisoned for 60 years or more. The court further found that the trial judge did not have enough information to make the predictive judgment that this particular 13-year old defendant should never again see the light of freedom.


OUTCOME: The court reduced defendant's sentence to life imprisonment with the possibility of parole.

 

129 of 423 DOCUMENTS


Snow v. State


No. 18634


Supreme Court of Nevada


105 Nev. 521; 779 P.2d 96; 1989 Nev. LEXIS 258



September 6, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from denial of motion for new trial in death penalty case; Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County; Donald M. Mosley, Judge.
Snow v. State, 101 Nev. 439, 705 P.2d 632, 1985 Nev. LEXIS 433 (1985)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from an order of the Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County (Nevada), which under Nev. Rev. Stat. § 176.515(3) denied his motion for a new trial based on newly discovered evidence as untimely filed. Defendant was convicted of conspiracy to commit murder and of murder in the first degree and received a death sentence for the murder charge.


OVERVIEW: More than two years after his conviction for murder in the first degree, defendant filed a motion for a new trial based only newly discovered evidence. The court denied the motion on the ground that it lacked jurisdiction to hear the same because it was filed after the two year statute of limitations in Nev. Rev. Stat. § 176.515(3). On appeal, defendant claimed that the limitations period was unconstitutional and violated his equal protection, due process, and Eight Amendment rights. The court disagreed and affirmed the judgment denying the motion for a new trial. Although § 176.515(3) precluded defendant from seeking a new trial more than two years after his conviction, it did not violate his constitutional rights because defendant could have sought collateral review of his alleged newly discovered evidence by petitioning for a writ of habeas corpus. In addition, the court also noted that the state's interest in the finality of judgments, based on the difficulty of meeting the burden of proof due to difficulty locating witnesses and evidence for retrying a case years, was substantial.


OUTCOME: In a death penalty case based on a murder conviction, the court affirmed the trial court's judgment denying defendant's motion for a new trial based on newly discovered evidence.

Techtow v. City Council of North Las Vegas


No. 16498


Supreme Court of Nevada


105 Nev. 330; 775 P.2d 227; 1989 Nev. LEXIS 67



June 2, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from declaratory judgment sustaining the constitutional validity of a city ordinance regulating massage parlors. Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County; Miriam Shearing, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner massage parlor operator appealed from the decision of the Eighth Judicial District Court (Nevada), which granted a declaratory judgment sustaining the constitutional validity of a city ordinance regulating massage parlors that was approved by respondent city officials.


OVERVIEW: A licensed operator of a massage parlor challenged North Las Vegas, Nev. Code 811, ch. 3.60 (ordinance), which officials enacted to regulate massage parlors. The district court held that the ordinance was constitutional. On appeal, the court reversed as to two provisions, but affirmed the other rulings. The court held that § 3.60.080(11), which required a window in a door of any room used for a massage or bath, violated the right to privacy. The court held that § 3.60.090, which required that massage parlors keep records of names and services rendered available for inspection, invaded privacy rights and freedom of association. However, the court held that the ordinance was not a bill of attainder because it did not single out the operator or punish him without judicial process, the definitions were not vague or overbroad, the advertising restrictions were a reasonable use of police power, the limited hours of operation set forth by § 3.60.110 did not violate equal protection, and §§ 3.60.230(b), 3.60.294(2), and 3.60.224(A), (B), which set forth same sex restrictions for massages and sponsorship of apprentices, were not a denial of equal protection.


OUTCOME: The court held that all but two of the provisions in the ordinance were constitutional. The court affirmed in part and reversed in part the district court's ruling.

Lyons v. State


No. 18503


Supreme Court of Nevada


105 Nev. 317; 775 P.2d 219; 1989 Nev. LEXIS 61



June 1, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from judgment of conviction pursuant to a guilty plea of one count of attempting to obtain money by false pretenses. Ninth Judicial District Court, Douglas County; David R. Gamble, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the judgment of the Ninth Judicial District Court of Douglas County (Nevada), which convicted him pursuant to a guilty plea of one count of attempting to obtain money by false pretenses. Defendant assented to a plea bargain that allowed him to enter an Alford plea to the non-committed crime of attempting to obtain money by false pretenses. The original charges were dropped in exchange for entry of the plea.


OVERVIEW: On appeal defendant argued that Nev. Rev. Stat. § 465.015, which defines cheating at gambling, was unconstitutionally vague as applied to slot machine handle manipulation. The court agreed because § 465.015 as applied to "handle popping," failed to address such conduct in terms that would alert persons of ordinary intelligence that they were committing a crime. The court did not perceive a description of handle popping within the statutory language. Defendant's conviction was reversed because the activities he engaged in did not constitute criminal activity. Because there was no constitutional basis for prosecuting defendant as a result of his handle popping activities, he received no consideration whatsoever in exchange for his Alford plea to a crime he did not commit. Therefore, defendant did not waive his right to complain of the acceptance of an unconstitutional plea.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction for attempting to obtain money by false pretenses was reversed.

 

133 of 423 DOCUMENTS


Pahrump v. Nye


No. 18951


Supreme Court of Nevada


105 Nev. 227; 773 P.2d 1224; 1989 Nev. LEXIS 53



May 18, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a district court order granting summary judgment and declaring certain sections of a statute unconstitutional. Fifth Judicial District Court, Nye County; William P. Beko, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant town sought review of a judgment of the Fifth Judicial District Court, Nye County (Nevada) that granted respondent county's motion for summary judgment in the town's declaratory judgment action. The trial court ruled that 1985 Nev. Stat. ch. 682, §§ 3, 4, which transferred the powers of planning, zoning, and building inspection from the county to the town, were unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: In the town's declaratory judgment action, the trial court found that 1985 Nev. Stat. ch. 682, §§ 3, 4, were unconstitutional because they violated Nev. Const. art. 4, §§ 20, 25, which respectively prohibited the legislature from passing local or special laws regulating county business and required that the establishment of a uniform system of county government. On appeal, the court rejected the town's contention that planning, zoning and building were not "integral components" of a uniform system of government. The court concluded that zoning and planning fell within the powers, duties and obligations placed upon a political organization, and were precisely the type of activities that Ariz. Const. art. 4, § 25 was intended to regulate. Because 1985 Nev. Stat. ch. 682 delegated those powers away from the county to the town in a unique manner, ch. 682 destroyed the uniformity of the system of government among the counties. The court also rejected the town's argument that ch. 682 merely "affected" county business. Finally, the court rejected the town's assertion that its location in relation to the county seat presented a compelling reason for allowing a special law.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

134 of 423 DOCUMENTS


Las Vegas v. Nevada Indus.


No. 18491


Supreme Court of Nevada


105 Nev. 174; 772 P.2d 1275; 1989 Nev. LEXIS 39



April 25, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a decision of the district court holding portions of the Las Vegas Municipal Code unconstitutional as applied to respondent, granting preliminary and permanent injunctions against enforcement of those ordinances against respondent, and making permanent a previously issued writ of mandamus. Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County; Joseph S. Pavlikowski, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff city appealed the issuance of a writ of mandamus by the district court (Nevada) and the conclusion that defendant licensee's activities enjoyed protection under U.S. Const. amend. I because the city sought to regulate the licensee's nude show. The district court then held Las Vegas, Nev., Municipal Code §§ 19.74.020(I), 6.88.120 were unconstitutional and enjoined their enforcement.


OVERVIEW: The licensee stated on its application for a business license that it was not going to operate a sexually oriented business. However, police observed sexual activity in the licensee's business establishment. The city then held a hearing and revoked the licensee's business license on the basis of its misrepresentation, and fined the licensee. The court reversed the judgment that enjoined the city's use of the municipal code to revoke the licensee's business licenses. The court held that whether the licensee enjoyed protection under U.S. Const. amend. I for its nude show was not the issue, because the city revoked the license for the clear misrepresentation by the licensee on its application. Accordingly, the city properly exercised its discretion under Las Vegas, Nev., Municipal Code § 19.74.020(I) in finding the licensee operated a nude show. The court affirmed the enjoinment of the fine pursuant to Las Vegas, Nev., Municipal Code § 6.88.120, however. The court held that § 6.88.120 invited abusive application because it established no limit for a fine. Therefore, it could not stand pursuant to Nev. Const. art. 1, § 6.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed that part of the judgment that enjoined the imposition of a municipal code provision that permitted the city to fine the licensee without limitation. However, the court reversed the judgment on its permanently enjoining the city from using the municipal code provisions to revoke the licensee's business licenses based upon the licensee's misrepresentation on an application for a business license.

Wolzinger v. Eighth Judicial Dist. Court

Supreme Court of Nevada


105 Nev. 160; 773 P.2d 335; 1989 Nev. LEXIS 34

PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original petition for writs of certiorari, prohibition and mandamus (18715); original petition for writ of mandamus or prohibition (18912); appeal from order denying petition for appointment as successor executrix and for letters testamentary (18972); appeal from order denying petition for appointment as successor executor and for letters testamentary (19223); appeal from order denying petition for appointment as administrator and letters of administration (19269). Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County; Thomas A. Foley, Judge; Myron E. Leavitt, Judge (18912).

Passanisi v. Director, Nev. Dep't of Prisons


No. 19035


Supreme Court of Nevada


105 Nev. 63; 769 P.2d 72; 1989 Nev. LEXIS 15



February 24, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from an order of the district court dismissing without prejudice appellant's petition for a writ of habeas corpus. First Judicial District, Carson City, Michael R. Griffin, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant prisoner sought review of an order of the First Judicial District Court, Carson City (Nevada), which dismissed without prejudice the petition for a writ of habeas corpus based its decision on the prisoner's failure to comply with Nev. Rev. Stat. § 34.725.


OVERVIEW: The prisoner plead guilty to driving under the influence of intoxicating liquor causing substantial bodily harm or death to another person and one count of leaving the scene of an accident involving personal injury or death. Following judgment of conviction, the prisoner sought a writ of habeas corpus, alleging that his guilty plea was involuntary, that he was denied effective assistance of counsel, and that the consecutive sentences were illegal and improper. The trial court denied the petition. The court affirmed the order and held that the petition was properly denied, as was an evidentiary hearing, because the prisoner did not meet the statutory requirement of Nev. Rev. Stat. § 34.725 that he previously file a petition for post-conviction relief in the court that convicted him or that he show good cause for not having done so before having sought a petition for a writ of habeas corpus. The requirement that the prisoner had to have first sought relief in the court of conviction within a year of conviction was constitutional as a reasonable regulation of the writ of habeas corpus.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the district court's order denying the prisoner's petition for habeas corpus relief.

 

137 of 423 DOCUMENTS


Private Investigator's Licensing Bd. v. Taketa


No. 19176


Supreme Court of Nevada


105 Nev. 4; 767 P.2d 875; 1989 Nev. LEXIS 2



January 31, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from district court's judgment that NRS 648.1405(4) is unconstitutional and granting permanent injunctive relief. Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County; Donald M. Mosley, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee private investigators were convicted on felony charges. Appellant Private Investigator's Licensing Board (board) sought termination of the private investigators' employment pursuant to Nev. Rev. Stat. § 648.1405(4). The Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County (Nevada), granted permanent injunctive relief from enforcement of § 648.1405(4) and held that the statute was unconstitutional. The board appealed.


OVERVIEW: The trial judge ruled that § 648.1405(4) was unconstitutional under the equal protection clause and that the statute was overbroad. The court reversed. First, the trial judge erred in finding that there was no rational relationship between the statute's prohibition against entrusting to ex-felons duties, the execution of which required the utmost respect for the law, and the state's legitimate interest in maintaining the integrity and lawfulness of private investigations. The court found that this to be especially true in the private investigators' cases because their felony conviction stemmed from misconduct associated with the duties related to activities in which a private investigator might be expected to be engaged. Second, the trial judge also erred by applying an overbreadth analysis to find the statute unconstitutional. An overbreadth analysis was not applicable to the statute at issue, which pertained to social welfare and which did not disrupt first amendment rights. The court concluded that the provisions of § 648.1405(4) were rationally related to the state's legitimate interest in assuring that private investigations were conducted in a lawful manner.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment declaring the subject statute unconstitutional and ruled in favor of the board, in its action against the private investigators to terminate their employment.

Allstate Ins. Co. v. Furgerson

104 Nev. 772; 766 P.2d 904; 1988 Nev. LEXIS 129

OUTCOME: The district court's order granting summary judgment was reversed.

 

139 of 423 DOCUMENTS


Wise v. Bechtel Corp.


No. 18603


Supreme Court of Nevada


104 Nev. 750; 766 P.2d 1317; 1988 Nev. LEXIS 133; CCH Prod. Liab. Rep. P12,022



December 30, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certified questions pursuant to NRAP 5. The United States District Court, District of Nevada; Lloyd D. George, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Questions answered. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: On defendant pipe manufacturer's motion, the United States District Court, District of Nevada certified issues to the court regarding whether Nev. Rev. Stat. § 11.204 violated the equal protection clause of the Nevada Constitution or Nev. Const. art. 4, § 17. Plaintiffs, injured parties and spouses, had filed a personal injury suit against defendants, pipe manufacturer, pipe installer, maintenance company, and plant owners.


OVERVIEW: The injured parties sustained injuries when a pipe carrying superheated steam failed along a seam. The injured parties and spouses sued the plant owners, the maintenance company, the pipe manufacturer, and the pipe installer. The maintenance company moved for partial summary judgment, contending that the suit for injuries caused by latent construction defects was barred under Nev. Rev. Stat. § 11.204 because more than eight years had passed since the plant's completion. The injured parties and spouses, the pipe manufacturer, and the pipe installer opposed the motion. The trial court certified the questions of whether § 11.204 violated the equal protection clause of the Nevada Constitution or Nev. Const. art. 4, § 17. The court held that Nev. Rev. Stat. § 11.204 did not violate the equal protection clause. There existed a rational basis for distinguishing between owners, occupiers, architects, and builders of improvements to real property, as opposed to manufacturers and material suppliers. Nev. Rev. Stat. § 11.204 only concerned one subject and the language of the title was not misleading. Therefore, § 11.204 did not violate Nev. Const. art. 4, § 17.


OUTCOME: The court held that the statute of repose, which barred actions against property owners, occupiers, architects, and builders of improvements to real property, but exempted suits against manufacturers and material suppliers, did not violate the Nevada Constitution's equal protection clause. The statute also did not violate the Nevada constitutional provision requiring that each law enacted embrace one subject briefly expressed in the title.

Nevada Power Co. v. Metropolitan Dev. Co.

104 Nev. 684; 765 P.2d 1162; 1988 Nev. LEXIS 109

DISPOSITION: Reversed. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant power company sought review of an order of the Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County (Nevada), which dismissed the power company's third-party complaint against respondent installer in a personal injury action.


OVERVIEW: In a plaintiff's action for injuries she received from a fall that was caused by a pull-box, the power company sought to recover from the installer of the pull-box. On the installer's motion to dismiss, the district court held that the power company's complaint was time-barred because it had not been filed within eight years of the substantial completion of the installation, as required by Nev. Maecon, Inc. v. State Dep't of Taxation


No. 18427


Supreme Court of Nevada


104 Nev. 487; 761 P.2d 411; 1988 Nev. LEXIS 69; 35 Cont. Cas. Fed. (CCH) P75,560



September 21, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from judgment affirming a use tax assessment by the Nevada Department of Taxation. First Judicial District Court, Carson City; Michael R. Griffin, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant corporation challenged the judgment of the First Judicial District Court, Carson City (Nevada), which affirmed a use tax assessment by respondent, the State of Nevada Department of Taxation (department).


OVERVIEW: The corporation contended that the transactions taxed by the department were in fact sales to government entities exempted from taxation under Nev. Rev. Stat. § 372.325, the Nevada Tax Commission lacked specific statutory authority to enact Nev. Rev. Rul. 67, and Nev. Rev. Rul. 67 did not apply to the case because the corporation lacked sufficient incidents of ownership over the property transferred to the navy. The court affirmed the district court's judgment. The court determined that whereas the sales were not to the government, and the tax on sales did not fall on the government itself, the sales were not tax exempt under § 372.325. The court explained that the corporation purchased the materials with the intent that they be used in performance of its construction contracts. The court concluded that statutory authority for Nev. Rev. Rul. 67 was found in Nev. Rev. Stat. § 372.185. The court noted that the corporation's incidents of ownership were sufficient to subject it to taxation under Nev. Rev. Rul. 67 because the corporation had the absolute right to divert the materials to another unrelated project or to use them otherwise as it pleased.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the district court, which affirmed a use tax assessment by the department against the corporation.

Bradvica v. State


No. 18112


Supreme Court of Nevada


104 Nev. 475; 760 P.2d 139; 1988 Nev. LEXIS 65



August 31, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from judgment of conviction for carrying a concealed dangerous knife and possession of an illegal weapon. Ninth Judicial District Court, Douglas County; Norman C. Robison, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the order of the Ninth Judicial District Court, Douglas County (Nevada), which convicted defendant of carrying a concealed dangerous knife and possession of an illegal weapon.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested for driving without a license and for a traffic violation. The pocket knife at issue was found in a search of his person at the jail. The court reversed the judgment of the trial court, accepting defendant's argument that Nev. Rev. Stat. § 202.350(1)(b)(2), which prohibited the concealed possession of a dirk, dagger, or dangerous knife was unconstitutionally vague and ambiguous. The court noted that the California Supreme Court had held that an ordinary pocket knife was not a dirk or dagger as a matter of law, and the court concluded that defendant's knife no more resembled a dagger or stabbing weapon than a Boy Scout penknife. The court concluded that the conviction could not stand upon the term "dangerous knife," either, as the term was so vague that individuals could only guess as to its meaning without any objective guiding factors. Neither could defendant be convicted under Nev. Rev. Stat. § 202.350(5)(b), which prohibited spring-activated blades longer than two inches. Because "blade" was not defined, the court held that it meant the portion that was customarily sharpened. Under such definition, defendant's blade measured less than two inches.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction for carrying a concealed dangerous knife and possession of an illegal weapon.

Lane v. Second Judicial Dist. Court


No. 18768


Supreme Court of Nevada

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner district attorney sought reconsideration or rehearing of the court's order denying his request for a writ of prohibition. Petitioner sought a writ of prohibition, which was denied. Petitioner then sought rehearing or reconsideration. The court granted the writ of prohibition so that the trial court could provide petitioner with notice and opportunity for hearing to determine whether petitioner was involved in or ratified the assistant DA's dereliction. The court directed the trial court to determine whether resubmission was necessary and, if so, whether petitioner would go forward with resubmission.


OUTCOME: The court granted a writ of prohibition enjoining respondent district court judges from continuing the inquiry into a rape case previously submitted to the grand jury. The court directed the trial court to conduct a hearing to determine whether petitioner district attorney had participated in or ratified the assistant district attorney's dereliction of duty in presenting hearsay evidence of complainants' sexual history to the grand jury.

Elley v. Stephens


No. 18086


Supreme Court of Nevada


104 Nev. 413; 760 P.2d 768; 1988 Nev. LEXIS 56; CCH Prod. Liab. Rep. P11,902



August 25, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from summary judgment. Second Judicial District Court, Washoe County; William N. Forman, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant homeowners brought an action against defendants, original sellers and county, alleging strict products liability, negligence, and willful misconduct against the sellers, and alleging negligence, negligent inspection, and willful misconduct against the county. The Second Judicial District Court, Washoe County (Nevada), granted summary judgment in favor of the sellers and the county. The homeowners appealed.


OVERVIEW: The original sellers contracted for the erection of a prefab house. Without having lived in the house, they sold it to another couple. The homeowners purchased the house 12 years later and shortly thereafter, one of them fell through the railing of the house's deck, suffering injury. The county argued that the negligence claims were barred by the Nev. Rev. Stat. 11.203 10-year statute of repose, and that the homeowners did not have standing to challenge its constitutionality. The court held that (1) the homeowners lacked standing to challenge the constitutionality of the statute because their injuries were not a result of its alleged unconstitutionality and the invalidation of the statute would not redress their injuries; (2) Nev. Rev. Stat. 11.203 barred the homeowners' negligence claims against the county because the statute was intended to cover county officials conducting inspections; (3) the trial court properly dismissed the strict liability claim against the sellers because they did not qualify as retail sellers of a product; and (4) the trial court properly dismissed the willful misconduct claims because there was no evidence supporting the homeowners' allegations.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision granting summary judgment in favor of the original sellers and the county.

Lavery v. Wolden


No. 18267


Supreme Court of Nevada


104 Nev. 392; 760 P.2d 120; 1988 Nev. LEXIS 60



August 25, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal and cross-appeal from judgment. Second Judicial District Court, Washoe County; Peter I. Breen, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a husband and wife, sued respondents, a home builder and his employee, to recover damages for the faulty construction of their house. The Second Judicial District Court, Washoe County (Nevada) awarded the couple damages plus attorney's fees against the builder. It dismissed the employee from the action. The couple appealed the amount of attorney's fees awarded. The builder cross-appealed.


OVERVIEW: The couple moved into the house in 1977 but did not discover that the builder had not followed the plan's specifications until 1983. They commenced their action in 1984. The trial court found that the latent defects tolled the statute of limitations until they were discovered and applied the eight-year statute of limitations under Nev. Rev. Stat. § 11.204. The builder argued that the couple's action was barred by the six-year statute of limitations in effect in 1977, Nev. Rev. Stat. § 11.205. The court declared § 11.205 unconstitutional in 1983. That same year the Nevada legislature enacted Nev. Rev. Stat. § 11.204, which specifically applied to construction. The builder alternatively argued that since Nev. Rev. Stat. § 11.205 was declared unconstitutional before the couple brought their suit, they only available statute applicable was that for written contracts, Nev. Rev. Stat. § 11.190, which provided a six-year limitation. The court agreed, stating that the couple's action alleged breach of the construction contract. Consequently, the six-year limit under § 11.190 had run before they filed their complaint, which barred their action.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment against the builder.

 

147 of 423 DOCUMENTS


DePasquale v. State


No. 18169


Supreme Court of Nevada


104 Nev. 338; 757 P.2d 367; 1988 Nev. LEXIS 44



July 14, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from judgment of conviction of one count of larceny from the person. Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County; Miriam Shearing, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment from the Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County (Nevada), which convicted defendant of one count of larceny from the person and imposed a sentence of the maximum term.


OVERVIEW: In a decoy operation, an officer, who was the decoy, dressed in plain clothes and carried a shoulder bag. Within one of the side, zippered pockets of the bag was money, which was exposed so as to be visible to persons nearby. Co-defendant twice approached the decoy officer, asking for a pen and then for a piece of paper. When the officer stated "no," he retreated, motioned to defendant and to a third party, and conversed with them. The officer crossed the street, and defendant and co-defendant followed her. Defendant then called out to the officer, and co-defendant took the money as the officer turned around. On appeal from defendant's conviction, the court held that: (1) the defense of entrapment included two elements, an opportunity to commit a crime was presented by the State to a person not predisposed to commit the act; (2) the facts, that the exposed money was presented in a realistic situation and simply presented a generally identified social predator with a logical target, suggested that defendant was predisposed to commit the crime charged; and (3) the maximum sentence imposed was not unconstitutional because it was not disproportionate to the crime charged.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

State Bar v. Claiborne


No. 17294


Supreme Court of Nevada


104 Nev. 115; 756 P.2d 464; 1988 Nev. LEXIS 22



May 18, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original proceedings relating to attorney discipline.



DISPOSITION: Proceedings dismissed. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner state bar brought respondent judge before bar disciplinary proceedings.


OVERVIEW: Subsequent to his conviction on tax evasion charges and his impeachment from the federal bench, the judge faced state bar proceedings. However, the court, after reviewing the record, concluded that the judge had been sufficiently punished and refused to sanction him. In reaching its conclusion, the court reasoned that it had serious questions concerning the propriety of the criminal investigation and proceedings against him. The court noted evidence that tended to show that the judge had been unfairly targeted by federal investigators and that evidence supporting his conviction was not overwhelming. The court also noted questions concerning the judge's impeachment proceedings and the manner in which evidence was presented. Additionally, the court relied on the fact that the judge's record prior to the incidents in question was exemplary. The court then noted that the judge's age and financial considerations mitigated against imposing state bar sanctions.


OUTCOME: The court declined to sanction the judge in state bar disciplinary proceedings.

Roberts v. State


No. 18314


Supreme Court of Nevada


104 Nev. 33; 752 P.2d 221; 1988 Nev. LEXIS 1



March 30, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from an order of the district court granting respondents' motion for summary judgment and from an order of the district court denying appellants' motion to alter or amend the judgment and motion to file a first amended complaint. First Judicial District Court, Carson City; Michael E. Fondi, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, professional employees of the University of Nevada, sought review of an order of the First Judicial District Court (Nevada) granting the summary judgment motion of respondents, the State of Nevada, the University of Nevada, and the regents of the University of Nevada, and denying the professional employees' motions to alter or amend the judgment and to file a first amended complaint in their action to collect longevity pay.


OVERVIEW: The professional employees claimed that they were entitled to retroactive longevity pay pursuant to Nev. Rev. Stat. § 284.177. Respondents denied the professional employees the longevity pay, claiming that subsequent administrative regulations and Nev. Rev. Stat. § 284.179 excluded professional employees from the group entitled to longevity pay. The professional employees brought an action to collect it. The trial court entered summary judgment in favor of respondents and denied the professional employees' motions to alter or amend the judgment and to file an amended complaint. The professional employees' appealed, and the court affirmed. The court, applying the traditional rules of statutory construction, held that the original intent behind Nev. Rev. Stat. § 284.177 was that professional employees of the University of Nevada would not be entitled to longevity pay. The court held that the legislature's subsequent enactment of Nev. Rev. Stat. § 284.179, which specifically provided that, to declare and clarify existing law, the professional employees were not entitled to receive longevity pay, was persuasive evidence of what the legislature intended by Nev. Rev. Stat. § 284.177.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the district court granting summary judgment in favor of the State of Nevada, the University of Nevada System, and the regents of the University of Nevada. The court affirmed the district court's order denying the motions of the professional employees of the University of Nevada System to alter or amend the judgment and to file an amended complaint.

 

150 of 423 DOCUMENTS


Blanton v. North Las Vegas Municipal Court


Nos. 17940, 17976, 17997, 17998, 17999, 18000, 18032, 18065, 18073, 18092, 18140


Supreme Court of Nevada


103 Nev. 623; 748 P.2d 494; 1987 Nev. LEXIS 1884



December 31, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals from orders denying petitions for writs of mandamus, Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County; Hon. Michael J. Wendell, District Judge (17940); Hon. Donald M. Mosley, District Judge (17976); Hon. John F. Mendoza, District Judge (17997, 17998, 18000); Hon. Carl J. Christensen, District Judge (17999); Hon. Earle W. White, Jr., District Judge (18140).

Appeals from orders granting petitions for writs of mandamus, Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County; Hon. Addeliar D. Guy, District Judge (18032); Hon. Joseph S. Pavlikowski, District Judge (18073).

Original petitions for writ of certiorari (18065), and writ of prohibition (18092).



DISPOSITION: Affirm Docket Nos. 17940, 17976, 17997, 17998, 17999, 18000 and 18140; reverse and remand to the Eighth Judicial District Court Docket Nos. 18032 and 18073; grant petition No. 18065; deny petition No. 18092. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants and prosecutors sought review of orders issued by the Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County (Nevada), which granted or denied petitions for writs of mandamus that were based upon defendants' challenge to Nev. Rev. Stat. § 266.550, which denied them a right to a jury trial in the municipal court when they were charged with the misdemeanor offense of driving under the influence (DUI).


OVERVIEW: Defendants contended that § 266.550, which precluded jury trials in municipal courts, was unconstitutional because it violated their constitutional right to a jury trial in misdemeanor criminal prosecutions. The court held that under the statutory penalties for DUI in Nevada, the United States Constitution did not guarantee the right to jury trials in misdemeanor DUI cases. The court stated that the U.S. Const. amend. VI right of trial by jury did not extend to every criminal proceeding. A jury trial was not required in that class or grade of offenses called petty offenses, which, according to the common law, could be proceeded against summarily in any tribunal legally constituted for that purpose. The court recognized that in considering whether a jury trial was required in a criminal case, the United States Supreme Court specifically drew a line of demarcation between "serious" and "petty" offenses; if the maximum authorized punishment was less than six months the offense was "petty." Because the maximum term of imprisonment possible in Nevada for a misdemeanor DUI offense was six months, the offense was "petty," and constitutionally did not mandate a jury trial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the district court's orders that denied the writs of mandamus, and reversed those orders that granted the writs.

 

151 of 423 DOCUMENTS


Barnes v. Eighth Judicial Dist. Court


Nos. 17633, 17872, 18044, 18362


Supreme Court of Nevada


103 Nev. 679; 748 P.2d 483; 1987 Nev. LEXIS 1899



December 31, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Consolidated petitions for writs of mandamus.



DISPOSITION: Petitions granted. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner prisoners filed petitions for writ of mandamus after respondent district judge denied the prisoners' motions to proceed in forma pauperis and refused to allow the prisoners to file in the Eight Judicial District Court of the State of Nevada pleadings seeking relief on various grounds related to their underlying criminal convictions or incarceration.


OVERVIEW: The prisoners filed motions to proceed in forma pauperis on their respective complaints for legal malpractice by their criminal attorneys and for habeas corpus relief. The district judge denied the motions because the prisoners failed to file supporting affidavits of attorneys stating that the complaints had merit. The prisoners filed petitions for writ of mandamus. The court granted the petitions, holding that, by conditioning the waiver of filing fees on an indigent's ability to obtain a certificate of an attorney that the cause of action or defense had merit, Nev. Rev. Stat. 12.015 violated the equal protection guarantees in the Nevada and United States Constitutions. The court reasoned that § 12.015 potentially operated to screen out meritorious actions that would otherwise be filed by persons who could not afford, or could not obtain for other reasons, the required attorney certificate. The court also ruled that the district judge erred in denying the motion of the prisoner who sought habeas corpus relief, because Nev. Rev. Stat. 19.013(4) prohibited the clerk of court from charging a fee for any services rendered to a defendant in habeas corpus proceedings.


OUTCOME: The court granted the prisoners' petitions for writ of mandamus and issued a writ directing the district judge to file the prisoners' pleadings and to refrain from enforcing the statute insofar as it required indigent persons to obtain, as a condition to obtaining a waiver of filing fees, the certificate of an attorney that the indigent had a meritorious cause of action or defense.

 

152 of 423 DOCUMENTS


Yohey v. Department of Motor Vehicles & Pub. Safety


No. 18109


Supreme Court of Nevada


103 Nev. 584; 747 P.2d 238; 1987 Nev. LEXIS 1879



December 22, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from an order of the district court affirming the revocation of appellant's driver's license. Third Judicial District Court, Churchill County; Mario G. Recanzone, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant licensee challenged an order of the Third Judicial District Court, Churchill County (Nevada), which affirmed the revocation by respondent Department of Motor Vehicles and Safety (department) of the licensee's driver's license under Nev. Rev. Stat. § 483.460.


OVERVIEW: The licensee was convicted of a DUI, and within seven years was convicted of a second DUI. The district attorney at the second trial did not produce evidence of the first conviction because of his belief that the first conviction was unconstitutional. Thus, the trial court treated the second conviction as a first offense. The department was notified of the licensee's two convictions and revoked the licensee's driver's license for one year. The licensee petitioned the district court for judicial review, and the district court affirmed the department's decision. The licensee appealed, and the court affirmed. The court found that Nev. Rev. Stat. § 483.460 imposed upon the department a mandatory duty to revoke the licensee's driver's license for one year because of the existence of three factors: (1) the department had received valid records of conviction; (2) those records showed that the licensee was convicted twice within seven years for violating Nev. Rev. Stat. § 484.379; and (3) the convictions were final. The department performed a purely ministerial function in revoking the driver's license, and it was not authorized to assess the validity of the first conviction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment, which affirmed the revocation of the licensee's driver's license because of the licensee's second DUI conviction within seven years.

Sheriff, Clark County v. Anderson


No. 16961


Supreme Court of Nevada


103 Nev. 560; 746 P.2d 643; 1987 Nev. LEXIS 1909



December 10, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from an order granting a petition for a writ of habeas corpus. Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County; Earle W. White, Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant county sheriff challenged the judgment of the Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County (Nevada), which granted petitioner inmate's pre-trial petition for a writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: The inmate was arrested when he was observed using a hidden microcomputer to assist him while playing blackjack at a casino. He was charged with possession of a cheating device and entering a building with intent to use a cheating device in violation of Nev. Rev. Stat. § 465.075. The trial court found § 465.075 to be unconstitutionally vague and overbroad in its application, thereby denying the inmate his rights under the First, Fifth, and Fourteenth Amendments. The court said that § 465.075 prohibited the use of a "device" for various gaming purposes. Whatever else the term "device" included, it certainly included computers. Because no person of ordinary intelligence could believe otherwise, § 465.075 was not unconstitutionally vague. The inmate would know that it clearly proscribed the use of a computer to assist him in playing blackjack.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's issuance of a writ of habeas corpus and remanded the matter to the trial court.

 

154 of 423 DOCUMENTS


Edwards v. Reno


No. 16763


Supreme Court of Nevada


103 Nev. 347; 742 P.2d 486; 1987 Nev. LEXIS 1648



August 27, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from judgment declaring a city ordinance constitutional and awarding respondent $ 6,690.60 on its counterclaim. Second Judicial District Court, Washoe County; Robert J. Schouweiler, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant vendor challenged an order of the Second Judicial District Court, Washoe County (Nevada), which determined that Reno, Nev., Municipal Ordinance § 4.40.010 was constitutional and awarded respondent city damages on its counterclaim for license fees.


OVERVIEW: The vendor challenged the constitutionality of a city law that distinguished between peddlers and solicitors as to licensing fees. The city counterclaimed, seeking reimbursement of license fees for the vendor and his employees. The vendor appealed the lower court's judgment, which held that § 4.40.010 and awarded license fees to the city. The vendor contended that § 440.010 was vague, and violated the state and federal constitutions, and that he was not responsible for his employees' fees. The court affirmed the lower court's judgment insofar as it held that § 440.010 was constitutional. The vendor lacked standing to claim vagueness. Moreover, the law did not violate equal protection or due process. The city distinguished between peddlers and solicitors based on the future delivery of goods by the latter. That type of delivery suggested the solicitors worked for solvent sellers. Accordingly, the classification rationally related to a government objective of preventing fraudulent sales. The classification was also reasonable as to state taxation. Nevertheless, the vendor was responsible to the city only for his license fees, not for those of his employees.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's judgment, which determined the city's ordinance that required licenses for door-to-door salespeople like the vendor. The court reversed the lower court's judgment in favor of the city on its counterclaim for license fees and ordered the vendor to reimburse the city for his license, but not the licenses of his employees.

Hogan v. State


No. 16778


Supreme Court of Nevada


103 Nev. 21; 732 P.2d 422; 1987 Nev. LEXIS 1577



February 6, 1987, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of certiorari denied Hogan v. Nevada, 484 U.S. 872, 108 S. Ct. 201, 98 L. Ed. 2d 153, 1987 U.S. LEXIS 3857, 56 U.S.L.W. 3248 (1987)
Appeal dismissed by Hogan v. State, 104 Nev. 860, 809 P.2d 607, 1988 Nev. LEXIS 590 (1988)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from judgment of conviction for first-degree murder and attempted murder, each involving the use of a deadly weapon, and from sentence of death. Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County; John F. Mendoza, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by a jury in the Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County (Nevada) of murder and attempted murder involving the use of a deadly weapon. He was sentenced to death. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant killed his girlfriend and attempted to shoot and kill her daughter. The court held that hearsay testimony that the victim told the witness defendant threatened to kill the victim was admissible as an excited utterance, Nev. Rev. Stat. § 51.095. The victim was frightened and crying when she made the statements no more than an hour after the threat. Defendant's prior conviction in Iowa for manslaughter was properly admitted in the penalty phase as an aggravating circumstance. The Iowa court was not required to inform defendant of the elements of the offense as long as defendant knew the nature of the offense. The state's allegation that defendant knowingly created a great risk of death to more than one person, Nev. Rev. Stat. § 200.033(3), was a proper aggravating circumstance. Defendant committed two intentional shootings close in time. The second shooting was intended to prevent his detection. The penalty of death was not excessive or disproportionate, Nev. Rev. Stat. § 177.055(2)(d)(amended 1985). The shootings were premeditated with a brutal attempt to kill the only witness. Defendant had previously killed a woman with whom he was involved.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction and sentence.

 

156 of 423 DOCUMENTS


Doe v. Bryan


No. 16978


Supreme Court of Nevada


102 Nev. 523; 728 P.2d 443; 1986 Nev. LEXIS 1620



December 4, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from judgment dismissing action for declaratory relief. First Judicial District Court, Carson City; Michael E. Fondi, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant homosexual couples sought review of an order by the First Judicial District Court, Carson City (Nevada), which granted appellee governor's motion to dismiss the couples' declaratory judgment action seeking a declaration that Nev. Rev. Stat. § 201.190 (1986), the statute that proscribed homosexual conduct, was unconstitutional under the state and federal constitutions. The action was dismissed for appellants' lack of standing.


OVERVIEW: Appellants filed a declaratory judgment action against the governor seeking a declaration that Nev. Rev. Stat. § 201.190 (1986), the statute that criminalized homosexual conduct, was unconstitutional. The governor filed a motion to dismiss, arguing that appellants lacked standing because they had not been arrested or prosecuted for violating Nev. Rev. Stat. § 201.190. The trial court granted the motion to dismiss because appellants had never been arrested, prosecuted, or threatened with prosecution for violation of Nev. Rev. Stat. § 201.190. Appellants sought review, and the court affirmed, holding that an actual justiciable controversy was a preliminary hurdle to an award of declaratory relief. The party seeking declaratory relief must have had a legal interest in the controversy, and the issue involved in the controversy must have been ripe for judicial determination. A declaration was unavailable when the damage was merely apprehended or feared. Thus, because there was no indication that appellants were facing an immediate threat of arrest for violation of Nev. Rev. Stat. § 201.190, or that the risk of prosecution was more than speculative, appellants lacked standing.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court granting the governor's motion to dismiss appellant's declaratory judgment suit seeking a declaration that a statute prohibiting homosexual acts was unconstitutional.

State Employees Ass'n v. State


No. 16415


Supreme Court of Nevada


102 Nev. 356; 724 P.2d 732; 1986 Nev. LEXIS 1570



September 4, 1986, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied March 24, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal and cross-appeal from judgment awarding damages; First Judicial District Court, Carson City; Michael E. Fondi, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed and remanded in part. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant association of employees sued respondent officials on behalf of employees of the Nevada Department of Prisons who were denied travel and uniform allowances, which they had been promised, because of budget cuts effectuated under the terms of Nev. Rev. Stat. § 353.225. The First Judicial District Court, Carson City (Nevada) awarded the uniform allowances but denied the travel allowances. Both parties appealed.


OVERVIEW: The employees claimed that they had a contractual right to receive travel and uniform allowances. The availability of the travel allowance was advertised in job announcements to recruit employees to two southern Nevada facilities. The employees of both facilities who did not have housing at the location of the facilities had continued to incur travel expenses every day they worked at the facilities. Uniform allowance and remote area differential expenditure (travel allowance) reductions were two of the budget saving actions which were taken by the Department of Prisons in order to reach the targeted figure mandated by the governor and his budget chief. The court explained that the record was clear that both the uniform and travel pay were part of the total compensation package offered to workers at these two facilities. Under U.S. Const. art. I, § 10 and Nev. Const. art. 1, § 15, the court held that they constituted integral portions of the contractual consideration given by the State in exchange for the labor of the prison employees. The court explained that the State was no less bound to pay these forms of compensation than it was the employees' regular salary.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment awarding uniform allowances. The court reversed the judgment denying the travel allowances. The court remanded the case with instructions to enter a judgment awarding both allowances.

Gallego v. State


No. 15932


Supreme Court of Nevada


101 Nev. 782; 711 P.2d 856; 1985 Nev. LEXIS 507



December 20, 1985, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from judgment of conviction and sentences of death entered upon jury verdicts for two counts of murder in the first degree and from consecutive sentences of life without possibility of parole for two counts of kidnapping in the first degree with substantial bodily harm. Sixth Judicial District Court, Pershing County; Llewellyn A. Young, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment of conviction from the Sixth Judicial District Court, Pershing County (Nevada), which imposed sentences of death upon jury verdicts of guilty for two counts of murder in the first degree and consecutive sentences of life without possibility of parole for two counts of kidnapping in the first degree with substantial bodily harm.


OVERVIEW: Having determined that no prejudicial error occurred either in the guilt or penalty phases of appellant's trial, the court affirmed the convictions and sentences without exception. The court noted that the trial as a whole produced fairness to appellant both in the guilt and penalty phases. Upon its review of the context of the pretrial publicity in the case, the court concluded that the confluence of news coverage and the rural setting of the trial did not deprive appellant of a fair trial. It was sufficient that the jurors could lay aside their impressions or opinions and render a verdict based on the evidence presented in court. Although it was impossible to divine the true mind-set of any prospective jurors, the court was convinced from the record that the process of jury selection in the instant case yielded a jury panel committed to constitutional behavior. The court further found no error in the admission of accomplice testimony or of evidence of prior killings. The court concluded by finding no prejudicial error resulting from any of the procedures used or evidence offered in connection with the sentencing phase.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's convictions and corresponding sentences.

State v. Eighth Judicial Dist. Court


No. 16259


Supreme Court of Nevada


101 Nev. 658; 708 P.2d 1022; 1985 Nev. LEXIS 485



November 5, 1985, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for writ of certiorari.



DISPOSITION: Petition granted. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state challenged an order from respondent Eight Judicial District Court (Nevada), which declared Nev. Rev. Stat. § 486.231 unconstitutional and dismissed a criminal charge under it against the real party in interest, a motorcyclist, of willfully and unlawfully driving a motorcycle on a public highway without protective headgear. The motorcyclist had pled nolo contendere and then successfully challenged the constitutionality of § 486.231.


OVERVIEW: Section 486.231 required that motorcyclists wear protective headgear and goggles when on a highway. The district court granted the motorcyclist's motion to dismiss the criminal charges and held § 486.231 unconstitutional, finding that it violated his right to privacy and equal protection and that it was an enactment in excess of the state's police powers. The court reversed. First, the motorcyclist's right to privacy was not violated because his "right to be left alone" as guaranteed by U.S. Const. amend. IX and Nev. Const. art. 1, § 20 did not include the right to do whatever he wanted on an expressway. Second, equal protection was not violated because § 486.231 bore a rational relationship to a legitimate state purpose. Further, the differences between cars and motorcycles justified the classification and disparate treatment of motorcyclists. The state had legitimate interests in promoting highway safety, reducing the severity of injuries to motorcyclists, and reducing the public costs of accidents. Last, § 486.231 did not exceed the scope of the state's police powers because those powers could legitimately be exercised for the purpose of promoting public health and safety.


OUTCOME: The court granted the state's petition for a writ of certiorari and declared the mandatory helmet law constitutional. The district court's order and judgment were vacated, and the case was remanded to the district court with instructions to reinstate the judgment of conviction of willfully and unlawfully driving a motorcycle on a public highway without wearing protective headgear, pursuant to the motorcyclist's plea of nolo contendere.

Sheriff, Washoe County v. Wu


No. 16156


Supreme Court of Nevada


101 Nev. 687; 708 P.2d 305; 1985 Nev. LEXIS 490



November 5, 1985, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Sheriff's appeal from a district court order granting a pre-trial writ of habeas corpus; Second Judicial District Court, Washoe County; Richard C. Minor, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, a county sheriff, sought review of the judgment of the Second Judicial District Court, Washoe County (Nevada) granting a pre-trial writ of habeas corpus to respondent, a driver charged with driving under the influence of intoxicants. The sheriff contended that the justice's court of the township where the driver was arrested had jurisdiction, along with the municipal court, to hear the case.


OVERVIEW: The driver was arrested within the city limits and charged with violating Washoe County, Nev., Code § 70.3865. He was cited to appear in the justice's court of the township. At the conclusion of the state's case, the driver's attorney moved to dismiss for lack of jurisdiction. The driver asserted that under Nev. Rev. Stat. § 484.803(1) exclusive jurisdiction was vested in the municipal court. In quashing the writ, the court noted that Nev. Const. art. 6, § 9 did not permit legislative fixing of municipal court jurisdiction to have been in conflict with that of the several courts of record. The mere passage of an ordinance by a municipality, which prohibited an act already prohibited, did not prevent other governmental agencies from enforcing its laws. The court concluded that when a traffic violation occurred within municipal boundaries a violator might have been prosecuted in either a municipal court or justice's court having jurisdiction of the offense. In either event the violator must have been taken without unnecessary delay before that court in which the charge was brought.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order granting habeas corpus and quashed the writ.
