Westinghouse Beverage Group v. Department of Taxation


No. 15582


Supreme Court of Nevada


101 Nev. 184; 698 P.2d 866; 1985 Nev. LEXIS 393



April 25, 1985, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied August 27, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from judgment declaring NRS Chapter 369A to be constitutional and denying injunctive relief; Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County; Carl J. Christensen, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant beverage group challenged a judgment from the Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County (Nevada), which had found constitutional Nev. Rev. Stat. § 369A. The statute imposed a tax upon the sale at retail or the purchase at wholesale of soft drinks.


OVERVIEW: Nev. Rev. Stat. § 369A imposed a tax on the privilege of importing for sale at retail or selling at wholesale soft drinks or syrups and powders used to make soft drinks. The beverage group, corporations that sold soft drinks or soft drink syrups at wholesale in Nevada, challenged the constitutionality of the statute in a declaratory judgment action. The trial court found the statute constitutional. The beverage group contended that the statute was too vague because it failed to identify what was being taxed or who was required to pay the tax. The court affirmed and held that the statute neither forbid nor required the doing of any act in terms so vague that men of common intelligence must necessarily have had to guess at its meaning and differ as to its application. The beverage group expressed no difficulty in understanding what a soft drink was or what syrups and powders used to make soft drinks were, and neither did the court. The statute involved economic considerations and not U.S. Const. amend. I freedoms, thus the statute could only be stricken as unconstitutionally vague if it was found to have been so in all of its applications. Such could not be said of the statute.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment from the trial court, which had found constitutional the statute that imposed a tax upon the sale at retail or the purchase at wholesale of soft drinks.

 

165 of 423 DOCUMENTS


Sheriff, Clark County v. Luqman


Nos. 14566, 14858


Supreme Court of Nevada


101 Nev. 149; 697 P.2d 107; 1985 Nev. LEXIS 382



March 22, 1985, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals from orders granting pretrial petitions for habeas corpus; Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County; Joseph S. Pavlikowski, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sheriff sought review of the decision of the Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County (Nevada), which granted pretrial habeas corpus relief to respondents who were arrested for violating various provisions of the Uniform Controlled Substances Act.


OVERVIEW: The Nevada legislature amended the statutory schedules of the Uniform Controlled Substances Act (UCSA). During the period between the amendatory repeal of the statutory schedules and the publication of the new schedules, respondents were arrested for crimes involving controlled substances. Respondents filed writs of habeas corpus which were granted by the trial court. The court held that the delegation of legislative power to promulgate schedules of controlled substances to the pharmacy board was not unconstitutional. The court found that the UCSA was not unconstitutionally vague because it was clear in the statute that the drugs defined as controlled substances were listed in the pharmacy board regulations. The court held that respondents should have been held accountable for violation of the UCSA although the pharmacy board had not promulgated new schedules as of the date of the infractions because the controlled substances specified in the former schedules notwithstanding use of the word "repeal," continued in effect and were automatically incorporated into the new corresponding schedules. The court reversed the orders granting the writs of habeas corpus.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the orders of the trial court granting the writs of habeas corpus to respondents who were arrested for violating provisions of the UCSA.

 

166 of 423 DOCUMENTS


Jordon v. Housewright


No. 15987


Supreme Court of Nevada


101 Nev. 146; 696 P.2d 998; 1985 Nev. LEXIS 383



March 19, 1985, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from denial of a petition for writ of habeas corpus, First Judicial District Court, Carson City; Michael E. Fondi, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Appeal dismissed. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner appealed from the judgment of the First Judicial District Court, Carson City (Nevada) denying his petition for a writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner, a prisoner in a state prison, filed a post-conviction petition for a writ of habeas corpus. A hearing was held, and the trial court denied the petition. Three days after the written order denying the petition was entered, the prison director's attorney mailed written notice of the entry to petitioner's attorney. Petitioner filed his notice of appeal 21 days after the entry of the written order denying the habeas petition. On appeal, the court determined that it lacked jurisdiction and dismissed the appeal. The court stated that under Nev. Rev. Stat. § 34.380(3), an appeal from an order denying a petition for a writ of habeas corpus had to be made within 15 days after the day of entry of the order. The court noted that habeas corpus was a special statutory remedy that could not be classified as either civil or criminal for all purposes. The court also noted that § 34.380(3) did not provide for additional time in which to file an appeal based upon service of notice by mail. Therefore, the court ruled that Nev. R. App. P. 26(c) did not apply to enlarge the time for perfecting an appeal.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed petitioner's appeal from the trial court's judgment denying his petition for a writ of habeas corpus.

K-Mart Corp. v. State Indus. Ins. Sys.


No. 14888


Supreme Court of Nevada


101 Nev. 12; 693 P.2d 562; 1985 Nev. LEXIS 358



January 3, 1985, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from order of district court on petition for judicial review affirming decision of the Nevada Industrial Commissioners. First Judicial District Court, Carson City; Michael E. Fondi, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Nevada Industrial Commissioners (commissioners) determined that special assessments against appellant employer by appellee State Industrial Insurance System (agency) were proper. The First Judicial District Court (Nevada) affirmed the commissioners' decision. The employer sought review.


OVERVIEW: The employer, contesting certain agency imposed assessments against it, intervened in a hearing pending before the commissioners. When the commissioners affirmed the assessment, the matter was appealed to the trial court, which affirmed the actions of the commissioners. The employer again sought review. The court determined that: (1) 1981 Nev. Stat. ch. 573 § 10 did not cause an impairment of contract because the rights and duties under the workers' compensation statute were not contractual but based in the employer-employee status; (2) the retroactive effect of the statute was a valid exercise of the legislature's police power and therefore constitutional; (3) the use by the agency of the statute's formula did not constitute a regulation and therefore did not have to conform to certain statutory requisites; and (4) the rules created by the agency concerning the date of payments and the permitting of offsets against experience dividends were regulations and therefore invalid.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part but reversed the lower court's ruling on the validity of the date and manner of payment and the offset against the experience dividend.

 

168 of 423 DOCUMENTS


Moore v. State


No. 15230


Supreme Court of Nevada


100 Nev. 698; 692 P.2d 1278; 1984 Nev. LEXIS 461



December 17, 1984 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from judgment of conviction upon a jury verdict of one count of cheating at gambling and one count of altering the result of a gambling game, Ninth Judicial District Court, Douglas County; Norman C. Robison, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part; affirmed in part. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his jury convictions for cheating at gambling (CAG) in violation of Nev. Rev. Stat. § 465.083 and altering the outcome of a gambling game (AOGG) in violation of Nev. Rev. Stat. § 465.070(1), entered in the Ninth Judicial District Court, Douglas County (Nevada).


OVERVIEW: While gambling at a casino, defendant removed a card from a blackjack game and substituted another in order to obtain a better hand and beat the dealer. He was charged with CAG in violation of Nev. Rev. Stat. § 465.083 and AOGG in violation of Nev. Rev. Stat. § 465.070(1). Defendant was convicted of CAG and AOGG. On appeal, he argued that his convictions were double punishment because CAG was a lesser included offense of AOGG. The court reviewed a prior court case, which provided that the test for determining the existence of a lesser included offense was whether the offense at issue could not be committed without committing the lesser offense. The court found that Nev. Rev. Stat. §§ 465.083, 465.070(1) each required that the outcome of a gambling game be altered; the only distinction was the time at which the alteration occurred. Nev. Rev. Stat. § 465.070(1) was the more specific statute in prohibiting altering conduct only after the result was made sure. The court found that a person could not commit AOGG without also violating CAG. Thus, CAG was a lesser included offense of AOGG. Because defendant could only be convicted of one offense, the CAG conviction was reversed.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction for CAG but affirmed his conviction for AOGG.

 

169 of 423 DOCUMENTS


State v. Burbank


No. 14830


Supreme Court of Nevada


100 Nev. 598; 691 P.2d 845; 1984 Nev. LEXIS 444



December 6, 1984 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal and cross-appeal from judgment declaring tax statutes, as applied, violated the Commerce Clause and federal statute, and ordering reimbursement of taxes paid under protest. First Judicial District Court, Carson City; Michael E. Fondi, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed as modified. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, the State of Nevada, its taxing authorities, and a county, and respondent California cities challenged a judgment from the First Judicial District Court, Carson City (Nevada), which declared that Nev. Rev. Stat. §§ 361.157(2), .159(2) (1977), as applied, violated the Commerce Clause and 15 U.S.C.S. § 391, ordered reimbursement of taxes paid, and prohibited future tax collection until the statutes were uniformly applied.


OVERVIEW: The county taxed the cities under Nev. Rev. Stat. §§ 361.157(2), 361.159(2) (1977) for a number of years, the cities paying in protest. The cities eventually filed suit to avoid payment of the tax and obtain reimbursement of the taxes paid under protest. The trial court entered judgment in favor of the cities and prohibited future tax collection under §§ 361.157(2), 361.159(2) until they were uniformly applied as to California cities and Nevada cities. Upon review, the court modified the trial court's judgment to completely prohibit taxation under §§ 361.157(2), 361.159(2) and, as modified, affirmed the trial court's judgment. The court held that §§ 361.157(2), 361.159(2) facially violated 15 U.S.C.S. § 391, and as a result, the Supremacy Clause of the U.S. Constitution because they imposed a tax on all out-of-state receivers of power but did not on in-state receivers. The court found that Nev. Rev. Stat. §§ 361.157(2), 361.159(2) (1977) were unconstitutional and thus could not be applied to any power receivers.


OUTCOME: The court modified the trial court's judgment to forever prohibit collection of taxes under the statutes and, as modified, affirmed the trial court's judgment.

Las Vegas v. O'Donnell


No. 15503


Supreme Court of Nevada


100 Nev. 491; 686 P.2d 228; 1984 Nev. LEXIS 412



August 24, 1984 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original petition for writ of certiorari.



DISPOSITION: Petition granted. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Before the court was the City's petition for a writ of certiorari, wherein it challenged a decision of the trial court (Nevada), which reversed defendant's conviction for driving under the influence of intoxicating liquor and remanded for a new trial in the municipal court. The trial court had also instructed that the evidence of an Intoxilyzer test could not be admitted at the trial.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged in a municipal court with one count of driving under the influence of intoxicating liquor in violation of Nev. Rev. Stat. § 484.379. Defendant objected to the admission of the Intoxilyzer breath test because the State failed to preserve his breath samples at the time of testing. The municipal court admitted the results of the breath test. On appeal, the trial court remanded to the municipal court for a new trial and determined that the breath test should not have been admitted. The City filed a petition for a writ of certiorari and argued that the trial court did not have the power to remand the trial. The court agreed and granted the writ. The court determined that the trial court only had the power to hold a trial de novo. The court also found that the trial court erred when it determined that the results of the breath test were inadmissible. The court determined that results could be admitted because there was no evidence that the State had acted in bad faith, and defendant failed to show that he was prejudiced by the State's failure to produce his breath samples.


OUTCOME: The court granted the City's petition for writ of certiorari. The court vacated the trial court's order and remanded the matter to the trial court for a trial on the merits.

L-M Architects v. Sparks


No. 14418


Supreme Court of Nevada


100 Nev. 334; 683 P.2d 11; 1984 Nev. LEXIS 382



June 26, 1984 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from an order dismissing complaint for failure to comply with NRS 268.020; Second Judicial District Court, Washoe County; William N. Forman, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant corporation sought review of the judgment of the Second Judicial District Court, Washoe County (Nevada) granting summary judgment to appellee city for the corporation's failure to comply with Nev. Rev. Stat. § 268.020 in the corporation's contract action.


OVERVIEW: The city refused to pay the architectural corporation for contract work because it failed to present a timely demand in accord with Nev. Rev. Stat. § 268.020. The corporation brought a contract action against the city, and the city filed a motion for summary judgment based upon the corporation's noncompliance with § 268.020. The trial court granted the motion and dismissed the action. On appeal, the court affirmed the grant of summary judgment. The court ruled that § 268.020 required a contractor to present a demand for payment within six months after such account became due. The court noted that the statute had been held to be discriminatory as to tort claims because no notice or demand was required against private tortfeasors. However, the court ruled that the same rule did not extend to contract cases because the legislature had never expressed an intent to place governmental and non-governmental promisors on an equal footing. Thus, the court ruled that the statute was not discriminatory as to contract actions and that the corporation was responsible for complying with the statutory procedures for satisfying claims.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's grant of summary judgment to the city in the corporation's contract action.

Hughes Properties v. State


No. 14621


Supreme Court of Nevada


100 Nev. 295; 680 P.2d 970; 1984 Nev. LEXIS 372



May 10, 1984 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from an order granting summary judgment to respondents and denying appellants' cross motion for summary judgment. Second Judicial District Court, Washoe County; Peter I. Breen, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayers challenged an order of the Second Judicial District Court, Washoe County (Nevada), which granted summary judgment to respondents, State of Nevada and the Nevada Gaming Commission, and which denied the taxpayers' cross motion for summary judgment. The taxpayers argued that the plain meaning of Nev. Rev. Stat. § 463.0114, defining "gross revenue," precluded taxation of sums received as "rake-offs" and percentage buy-ins.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayers sought a refund of allegedly overpaid quarterly license fees. They argued that the plain meaning of former Nev. Rev. Stat. § 463.0114 (recodified Nev. Rev. Stat. § 463.0161), defining "gross revenue," precluded taxation of sums received as "rake-offs" and percentage buy-ins. The trial court granted respondents' motion for summary judgment. The court affirmed the judgment and held that the state licensed gambling games primarily as a means of producing revenue, and if the taxpayers' construction of the statute had been adopted, the state would have been precluded from including the revenue produced by all percentage games in the calculation of a licensee's gross revenue. That would not have been a reasonable interpretation of the statute, nor would it have been consistent with legislative intent. Further, Nevada Gaming Commission Regulation 6.080(1)(d) was a valid implementing regulation consistent with the Gaming Control Act and the legislative intent behind that Act. The court noted that when the legislature amended Nev. Rev. Stat. § 463.0114, it specifically included rake-offs and buy-ins in the definition of gross revenue, consistent with the regulation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order granting summary judgment to respondents in an action by the taxpayers to recover taxes paid to the state.

Ybarra v. State


No. 13590


Supreme Court of Nevada


100 Nev. 167; 679 P.2d 797; 1984 Nev. LEXIS 344



March 28, 1984 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied July 27, 1984.

Post-conviction relief denied at Ybarra v. State, 103 Nev. 8, 731 P.2d 353, 1987 Nev. LEXIS 1572 (1987)
Post-conviction relief denied at Ybarra v. Warden, 115 Nev. 606, 24 P.3d 304, 1999 Nev. LEXIS 1703 (1999)

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment by the Seventh Judicial District Court, White Pine County (Nevada), which convicted him of first-degree murder, first-degree kidnapping, battery with intent to commit sexual assault, and sexual assault, and sentenced him to the death penalty and three consecutive life sentences without the possibility of parole. Defendant argued that there were errors in the guilt and penalty phases of his trial.


OVERVIEW: A jury convicted defendant of first-degree murder, first-degree kidnapping, battery with intent to commit sexual assault, and sexual assault. Defendant was thereafter sentenced to the death penalty and three consecutive life sentences without the possibility of parole. The court affirmed on appeal. Next, on the penalty phase of defendant's trial, the court rejected defendant's argument that § 200.030(4), under which he was sentenced to death, was unconstitutional. The court found that the statute provided for the consideration of aggravating and mitigating factors and permitted the death penalty where the aggravating factors outweighed the mitigating factors. The court held that the statute consisted of sufficient guarantees that the death penalty would not be imposed arbitrarily and capriciously.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

Allen v. State


No. 14703


Supreme Court of Nevada


100 Nev. 130; 676 P.2d 792; 1984 Nev. LEXIS 334



February 24, 1984 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from summary judgment in a class action suit. Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County; James Brennan, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a class action, plaintiff early retirees, who were public employees, filed a claim against defendant state and officials to recover retirement money after a new statute, Nev. Rev. Stat. 286.551, reduced the early retirees benefits. The Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County (Nevada) entered summary judgment in the state's favor. The early retirees appealed.


OVERVIEW: The early retirees asserted that Nev. Rev. Stat. 286.551 was unconstitutional. The court affirmed the grant of summary judgment and held that the statute, which did not increase early retirees' benefits while giving other retirees a "raise," did not violate substantive due process under the U.S. Constitution. The court found that the state had a large turnover of employees and that the new law was enacted to retain state employees. The court held that early retirees had already left government service, so there was no need to attract them to state employment. The court found that Nev. Rev. Stat. 286.551 was grounded in a rational basis and not enacted arbitrarily. The court found that Nev. Rev. Stat. 286.551 did not violate the Equal Protection Clause because early retirees were not a suspect class and the statute met rational basis review, which was all that was required. The court held that the statute did not violate the Contract Clause because the early retirees' contracts were not impaired. The court found that the early retirees received the same benefits after the amendment and their only complaint was that they did not receive an increase as later retirees would receive.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's summary judgment against the early retirees and held that the new law that reduced their benefits was constitutional.

Republic Entertainment v. Clark County Liquor & Gambling Licensing Bd.


No. 14168


Supreme Court of Nevada


99 Nev. 811; 672 P.2d 634; 1983 Nev. LEXIS 548



December 1, 1983 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from order denying motion for preliminary injunction and dissolving temporary restraining order, Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County; Thomas J. O'Donnell, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant escort services sought review of a judgment of the Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County (Nevada), which dissolved a temporary restraining order and denied the escort services' motion for a preliminary injunction in their action against appellee liquor and gaming license board (board) challenging its enactment of Title 8, Chapter 8.32, which regulated the performance of services as an escort in the county.


OVERVIEW: Chapter 8.32 prohibited anyone from working as an escort in the county unless employed by a licensed escort bureau or licensed as an escort bureau and permitted only service oriented escorts and escort bureaus to obtain a license. The escort services contended that Chapter 8.32 was more accurately characterized as an ordinance and that it was invalid because the board did not have the power to enact ordinances. The court affirmed the trial court and held that Chapter 8.32: (1) was a validly enacted regulation because there was statutory authority for the promulgation of regulations relating to licensing and for their criminal enforcement; (2) did not violate the First Amendment by prohibiting sexually oriented escort bureaus from advertising their services because commercial speech was subject to wider regulation, particularly when related to activities that the county could prohibit, such as prostitution; (3) was not unconstitutionally overbroad because it did not lend itself to an interpretation that reached constitutionally protected conduct and the overbreadth doctrine did not apply to commercial speech; and (4) was not vague and provided adequate standards for its application.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order dissolving a temporary restraining order and denying the escort services' motion for a preliminary injunction in their action challenging the constitutionality of a regulation imposed on performance of escort services.

Gilbert v. State


No. 14187


Supreme Court of Nevada


99 Nev. 702; 669 P.2d 699; 1983 Nev. LEXIS 517



September 27, 1983 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a four year prison sentence and a $ 2,000 fine for a conviction for driving under the influence of intoxicating liquor when death results. First Judicial District Court, Carson City; Michael E. Fondi, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment from the First Judicial District Court, Carson City (Nevada), which convicted him of driving under the influence of intoxicating liquor when death resulted under Nev. Rev. Stat. 484.3795(6) (1981). Defendant was sentenced to four years in prison and a $ 2,000 fine was imposed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that he was entitled to elect rehabilitative treatment under Nev. Rev. Stat. 484.379(6) (1981) and that the state could not imprison him for nonpayment of the fine. Upon review, the court found that as defendant was not convicted under Nev. Rev. Stat. 484.379(1), (2), he could not elect treatment. Under the terms of Nev. Rev. Stat. 176.065, defendant could be incarcerated an additional day for each four dollars of the fine imposed until it was discharged. The court stated that before he could be imprisoned for nonpayment of the fine, he was entitled to a hearing to determine his present ability to pay the fine. If he was found indigent, he could discharge the fine through one of the alternatives under Nev. Rev. Stat. 176.085. The court observed that no constitutional impediment existed to imposing a mandatory fine on an indigent defendant as long as the state did not automatically convert the fine to a sentence of imprisonment for nonpayment of the fine. As defendant had not yet been imprisoned for nonpayment, the court affirmed his sentence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction of driving under the influence of intoxicating liquor when death resulted. The court affirmed defendant's four-year prison sentence and the fine of $ 2,000.

Metropolitan Water Dist. v. State


No. 13063


Supreme Court of Nevada


99 Nev. 506; 665 P.2d 262; 1983 Nev. LEXIS 486



June 22, 1983 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied October 5, 1983.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from an order granting respondents' motion to dismiss; First Judicial District Court, Carson City; Michael R. Griffin, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant water district sought review of a decision of the First Judicial District Court, Carson City (Nevada), which granted appellee Department of Taxation's motion to dismiss on grounds that the water district brought an action to recover taxes paid under a discriminatory method of assessment without having first exhausted administrative remedies.


OVERVIEW: The Department of Taxation assessed taxes against the water district which were allegedly discriminatory. The water district brought an action against the Department of Taxation, and the trial court dismissed on the grounds that the water district had not exhausted its administrative remedies. The water district appealed and the court reversed. The court held that the water district had absolutely no reason to suspect that it was being singled out for the discriminatory tax assessment. To put the burden of investigation upon the water district would have required it to make gratuitous inquiries as to the methods used to assess not only itself but also other similar entities. The court found it would be unfair to impose such a duty upon a taxed entity, and held that no such duty existed. The court held that the water district's cause of action had not accrued until the water district learned that it was subject to discriminatory taxation.


OUTCOME: The decision of the lower court granting the Department of Taxation's motion to dismiss the water district's action to recover taxes paid was reversed.

 

180 of 423 DOCUMENTS


Sheriff of Washoe County v. Martin


No. 14604


Supreme Court of Nevada


99 Nev. 336; 662 P.2d 634; 1983 Nev. LEXIS 442



April 29, 1983 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from order granting pretrial writ of habeas corpus. Second Judicial District Court, Washoe County; James J. Guinan, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state appealed from an order of the Second Judicial District Court, Washoe County (Nevada), which granted defendant a pretrial writ of habeas corpus and dismissed charges against him for cheating in violation of New. Rev. Stat. 465.015 on the ground that the statute was unconstitutionally vague.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and an accomplice were caught crimping cards at a casino, and they were arrested and charged with two counts each of card cheating in violation of Nev. Rev. Stat. 465.083 and conspiracy to commit card cheating in violation of New. Rev. Stat. 199.480 and Nev. Rev. Stat. 465.083. The district court dismissed the charges on the ground that the definition of cheating in Nev. Rev. Stat. 465.015 was unconstitutionally vague. The court reversed and remanded for trial, holding that laws are presumed to be constitutional, and that if an enactment does not implicate constitutionally protected conduct, the court may strike it down as vague on its face only if it is impermissibly vague in all of its applications. In this case, using standard definitions, the cheating statutes clearly proscribed the acts committed by defendant. By crimping cards, defendant eliminated the element of chance as to himself and thereby altered the basic feature of the game, unlike a card counter who uses mental skills to take advantage of the same information that is available to all players. The evidence presented showed conduct and intent sufficient to warrant binding him over for trial.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the district court dismissing the charges and remanded the matter for trial.

Personius v. Ninth Judicial Dist. Court


No. 14506


Supreme Court of Nevada


99 Nev. 334; 661 P.2d 1307; 1983 Nev. LEXIS 443



April 29, 1983 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Writ of Mandamus or, in the alternative, Writ of Prohibition.



DISPOSITION: Petition denied. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner sought a writ of mandamus, or alternatively, a writ of prohibition, to order respondent trial court to hold a hearing on the petitioner's suitability for civil commitment in a drug or alcohol rehabilitation program.


OVERVIEW: The petitioner pleaded guilty to conspiracy to possess stolen property and conspiracy to possess a controlled substance. The petitioner announced his intention to elect civil commitment to a treatment program for alcoholics or drug addicts. At a hearing to determine his eligibility to elect civil commitment, evidence was adduced that he had pleaded nolo contendere to battery. Petitioner claimed that the battery conviction had been unconstitutionally obtained and should not have been considered. The trial court found the petitioner ineligible for civil commitment. Petitioner sought a writ of mandamus or a writ of prohibition to order the trial court to hold a hearing on his suitability for civil commitment. The court denied the writ. Because a denial of eligibility for civil commitment based on a prior conviction of a crime of violence was not tantamount to an enhanced penalty, a constitutional challenge to the prior conviction was inappropriate at the time eligibility was under consideration. The trial court's refusal to countenance the petitioner's challenge to his earlier criminal conviction was proper.


OUTCOME: The court denied the petition.

 

182 of 423 DOCUMENTS


Spilotro v. State


No. 12615


Supreme Court of Nevada


99 Nev. 187; 661 P.2d 467; 1983 Nev. LEXIS 423



March 31, 1983 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied September 19, 1983.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from judgment affirming order of Nevada Gaming Commission excluding appellant from licensed gaming establishments. Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County; John F. Mendoza, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed and remanded in part. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant casino patron sought review of a judgment from the Eighth Judicial District Court of Clark County (Nevada), which affirmed respondent state gaming commission's order that excluded appellant from the licensed gaming establishments.


OVERVIEW: The state gaming commission (commission) had issued an order pursuant to Nev. Rev. Stat. §§ 463.151, and 463.155, that excluded the casino patron from the licensed gaming establishments. The trial court rendered a judgment that affirmed the commission's order. On appeal, the court found §§ 463.151 and 463.155 were constitutional, but reversed the trial court's judgment because the commission failed to make factual findings in support of its order. Pursuant to Nev. Rev. Stat. § 463.312(18), the commission was required to make findings to support its ultimate findings that the casino patron fell within the meaning of §§ 463.151 and 463.155 for excluding him from the licensed gaming establishments. Next, §§ 463.151 and 463.155 were constitutional because they were valid on their face, and were equally applied to the casino patron. Further, §§ 463.151 and 463.155 was not overbroad because they did not infringe upon any rights under U.S. Const. amend. I. Finally, the casino patron's due process rights were not violated because he had received adequate notice of the administrative hearing against him.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment, and remanded for a statement of the basic factual findings on which the state gaming commission rested its ultimate finding that the casino patron fell within the meaning of the statute for excluding him from the licensed gaming establishments.

 

183 of 423 DOCUMENTS


Stanfill v. State


No. 12806


Supreme Court of Nevada


99 Nev. 247; 660 P.2d 1003; 1983 Nev. LEXIS 424



March 31, 1983 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied June 24, 1983; See 99 Nev. 499, 665 P.2d 1146 (1983).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from judgment of conviction and sentence for possession of a stolen credit card, First Judicial District Court, Carson City; Michael E. Fondi, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and remanded for new sentence. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the First Judicial District Court, Carson City (Nevada), which convicted him of possession of a stolen credit card. Defendant contended that Nev. Rev. Stat. § 205.690(2) and Nev. Rev. Stat. § 205.760, the statutes governing the offense with which he was charged, allowed for arbitrary enforcement in violation of his equal protection rights.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was indicted and convicted under Nev. Rev. Stat. § 205.690(2), which was a felony. However, defendant could have been charged with violating Nev. Rev. Stat. § 205.760, which required proof of essentially the same elements but permitted offenses involving less than $ 100 to be punished as a misdemeanor. Defendant's offense did not involve more than $ 100. Upon review, the court found that the statutes mandated different punishments for what was essentially the same act. The court compared the statutes and found that there was no intelligent standard for distinguishing the conduct proscribed by the two statutes. The court held that insofar as the statutes permitted defendant to be incarcerated for either a misdemeanor or a felony at the discretion of the prosecutor, they violated the Equal Protection Clause of U.S. Const. amend. XIV. The court concluded that defendant's sentence had to be modified.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for possession of a stolen credit card but reversed his sentence and remanded the action for further proceedings.

 

184 of 423 DOCUMENTS


State Farm Fire & Casualty Co. v. All Elec.


Nos. 13228, 13443


Supreme Court of Nevada


99 Nev. 222; 660 P.2d 995; 1983 Nev. LEXIS 425



March 31, 1983 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing in Case No. 13443 Denied June 20, 1983.


PRIOR HISTORY: Consolidated appeals from summary judgments; Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County; Paul S. Goldman, Judge (Case No. 13228); J. Charles Thompson, Judge (Case No. 13443).



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant insurance companies sought review of the order of the Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County (Nevada), which entered summary judgment in favor of respondents, architects and contractors, on the basis that the suits were barred under Nev. Rev. Stat. 11.205.


OVERVIEW: The suits of insurance companies, which were representing the interests of insured property owners against the architects and contractors, were barred under Nev. Rev. Stat. 11.205 by the district court. The insurance companies appealed, contending that § 11.205 violated the equal protection and due process clauses of the state and federal constitutions. The court agreed, and concluded that the equal protection claim was dispositive. Although the architects and contractors contended that a legitimate distinction existed between architects and contractors as opposed to owners and manufacturers, the court concluded that there was no rational basis for making such a distinction so as to justify granting immunity to one group while denying it to another. The court found that § 11.205 arbitrarily discriminated against a certain class of individuals, i.e., owners and material suppliers. Public policy reasons might exist to justify precluding legitimate claims from being litigated after the lapse of a certain number of years. However, because one class of defendants was arbitrarily excluded from this protection, the equal protection clauses were violated.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the lower court granting summary judgment in favor of the architects and contractors, and remanded the matter for further proceedings.

 

185 of 423 DOCUMENTS


List v. Whisler


No. 14440


Supreme Court of Nevada


99 Nev. 133; 660 P.2d 104; 1983 Nev. LEXIS 413



March 4, 1983 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied June 10, 1983.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a declaratory judgment holding taxation statutes violative of the Nevada Constitution, Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County; Howard W. Babcock, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, governor, the Nevada Tax Commission, executive director of state taxation department, and Legislative Commission of the State of Nevada, sought review of the declaratory judgment of the Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County (Nevada) holding certain taxation statutes in a tax package violative of the Nevada Constitution in the declaratory judgment action of respondents, county officials and taxpayers.


OVERVIEW: Respondents filed a complaint for declaratory relief alleging that § 31 of S.B. 69 (Nev. 1981) (§ 31) violated Nev. Const. art. 10, § 1. Respondents argued that use of two separate sets of weighted factors for determining the adjusted cash value of property, one for residential improvements and a second set for other property, was unconstitutional. Section 31 of S.B. 69 was part of a tax package contained in 1981 amendments to Nevada tax statutes that were intended to provide property tax relief. The trial court entered a declaratory judgment in favor of respondents with regard to the entire tax package because it was not severable from § 31. Appellants sought review of the judgment. On appeal, the court reversed the declaratory judgment. The court held that the intent of the factoring system contained in § 31 was not to favor a particular class of property, but to provide a limited adjustment mechanism by which prior inequitable valuations were made into the more uniform valuation and assessment procedures established under the 1981 tax package. The court noted that § 31 did not expressly impose two different rates of taxation. Thus, § 31 did not violate Nev. Const. art. 10, §1.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the declaratory judgment in favor of respondents which held that certain tax statutes violated the Nevada Constitution in respondents' declaratory judgment action against appellants.

 

186 of 423 DOCUMENTS


In re Ross


No. 11114


Supreme Court of Nevada


99 Nev. 1; 656 P.2d 832; 1983 Nev. LEXIS 375



January 5, 1983 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied September 12, 1983.


PRIOR HISTORY: Applications for review of "Decision and Recommendation" of Board of Bar Governors, in Bar disciplinary proceedings.



DISPOSITION: On "Motion to Dismiss and Quash the Action of the Board of Governors," motion granted. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner attorneys moved for review of determinations of the State Bar of Nevada's Board of Governors, which recommended that the attorneys be disciplined.


OVERVIEW: The attorneys argued that the conduct of their disciplinary hearing by the State Bar of Nevada Board of Governors (board) violated their due process right to an impartial tribunal because that body was primarily responsible for the finances of the state bar. The court held that the procedure violated due process. The test for violation of due process was whether temptation might exist for the adjudicator, even in the absence of direct, personal pecuniary interest, when his executive responsibilities for finances may make him partisan. The same group that was permitted to try the attorneys in the disciplinary matter was also charged with the executive functions of the state bar, including responsibility for revenues, expenditures, and management of the bar's finances. The board functioned in a quasi-judicial role.


OUTCOME: The proceedings against the attorneys were dismissed.

 

187 of 423 DOCUMENTS


State v. Glusman


Nos. 12946, 13217


Supreme Court of Nevada


98 Nev. 412; 651 P.2d 639; 1982 Nev. LEXIS 490



September 30, 1982 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Consolidated appeals from order granting a preliminary injunction to respondents (Case No. 12946), and the order denying appellants' request for declaratory relief (Case No. 13217). Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County; Robert G. Legakes, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed as to Case No. 12946; qualifiedly affirmed as to Case No. 13217. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, corporation and owner, filed an action against defendants, State and state agencies, for a declaration that Nev. Rev. Stat. § 463.160(8)(a) was unconstitutional. The corporation and owner moved for an injunction. The Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County (Nevada), initially granted the injunction but subsequently found the statute constitutional and dissolved the injunction. All parties challenged the decision.


OVERVIEW: The State maintained that the trial court did not have the authority to enjoin enforcement of the statute. The corporation and owner argued that the statute was vague and facially invalid. The court reversed the order granting the injunction and qualifiedly affirmed the constitutionality of the statute. Section 463.160(8)(a) granted the state agency the power to require a non-gaming business being operated at a gaming location to apply for a determination of suitability. Nev. Rev. Stat. § 463.343(5)(b), the declaratory judgments provision of the gaming chapter, effectively deprived the trial court of jurisdiction to entertain injunctive relief. The court determined that the statute was not constitutionally infirm by reason of vagueness and overbreadth. It was a reasonable exercise of police power to subject the corporation, which shared premises with certain gaming establishments, to a determination of suitability. However, requiring the corporation to pay all the expenses of the State's investigation was an unreasonable financial burden on the corporation and thus unenforceable as an invalid and excessive use of the police power.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order granting an injunction to the corporation and qualifiedly affirmed the judgment that found the statute to be constitutional.

 

188 of 423 DOCUMENTS


Carter v. State


No. 12702


Supreme Court of Nevada


98 Nev. 331; 647 P.2d 374; 1982 Nev. LEXIS 466



June 29, 1982 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a judgment of conviction following a guilty plea for the crimes of sexual assault with use of a deadly weapon and robbery with use of a deadly weapon, both upon a person over sixty-five years of age, Second Judicial District Court, Washoe County; William N. Forman, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part and remanded. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Second Judicial District Court, Washoe County (Nevada) convicting and sentencing him pursuant to Nev. Rev. Stat. §§ 193.165, 193.167 following a guilty plea for the crimes of sexual assault with use of a deadly weapon and robbery with use of a deadly weapon, both upon a person over 65 years of age.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended on appeal that the trial court erred in imposing consecutive sentences for multiple enhancements under Nev. Rev. Stat. §§ 193.165, 193.167 and that § 193.167 was unconstitutional. The court affirmed the judgment in part, reversed it in part, and remanded the case. The court noted that where the legislative intent of a criminal statute was ambiguous, the statute had to be strictly construed against imposition of a penalty for which it did not provide clear notice. The court held that the sentencing court could not impose consecutive enhancement penalties under Nev. Rev. Stat. §§ 193.165, 193.167 for the same offense. The court stated that due process was not violated merely because § 193.167 did not require knowledge of the victim's advanced age and that the argument to the effect that an accused's right to equal protection was violated because § 193.167 distinguished between perpetrators of crimes against victims over 65 years old and those who were younger was without merit.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part the judgment of the trial court convicting and sentencing defendant for sexual assault with use of a deadly weapon and robbery with use of a deadly weapon, both upon a person over 65 years of age, reversed the judgment in part, and remanded the case to the trial court for resentencing in accordance with the court's decision.

 

189 of 423 DOCUMENTS


Bludsworth v. State


No. 13100


Supreme Court of Nevada


98 Nev. 289; 646 P.2d 558; 1982 Nev. LEXIS 453



June 18, 1982 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appellant Curt Bludsworth appeals from a judgment of conviction for murder in the second-degree and for child abuse and neglect. Appellant Judi Bludsworth appeals from a judgment of conviction for child abuse causing serious bodily harm. First Judicial District Court, Carson City; Howard D. McKibben, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, the stepfather and the mother, sought review after the First Judicial District Court, Carson City (Nevada) convicted them of second-degree murder and child abuse and neglect, and child abuse causing serious bodily harm, respectively.


OVERVIEW: The two-year old victim died after sustaining severe head injuries. The jury convicted the stepfather of child abuse and second-degree murder. The same jury convicted the mother of child abuse. The court affirmed. A number of expert witnesses testified that the victim was a battered child. The expert opinion that the victim was a battered child, coupled with additional proof, was sufficient to permit a jury to conclude that the child's injury occurred at the culpable hands of its parents. Proof that a child had experienced injuries in many purported accidents was evidence that the most recent injury might not have resulted from yet another accident. The trial court did not commit prejudicial error in refusing to sever the trials on the murder and child abuse charges. The child abuse and murder counts were properly joined because they arose out of the same series of acts. Nev. Rev. Stat. § 173.115 permitted joinder in such instances. Nev. Rev. Stat. § 200.508, which authorized criminal penalties for any adult who willfully caused or permitted a child to suffer unjustifiable physical pain or mental suffering as a result of abuse or neglect, was not unconstitutionally vague.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendants' convictions.

Jiminez v. State


No. 13298


Supreme Court of Nevada


98 Nev. 204; 644 P.2d 1023; 1982 Nev. LEXIS 429



May 12, 1982 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from dismissal of complaint, First Judicial District Court, Carson City; Michael E. Fondi, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate brought an action against respondent state resulting from personal injuries he suffered while incarcerated. The First Judicial District Court, Carson City (Nevada), dismissed his complaint for failure to comply with the statute of limitations, and he appealed.


OVERVIEW: The state was served with the inmate's complaint and moved pursuant to Nev. R. Civ. P. 12(b)(1) to dismiss the complaint for failure to name the state as a party and consequent failure to invoke the subject matter jurisdiction of the court. Following dismissal, the inmate filed an amended complaint naming the state. The lower court granted the state's motion to dismiss on the grounds that the inmate had not complied with the one-year statute of limitations under Nev. Rev. Stat. Ann. 11.190(5)(c). On review, the court agreed the complaint was filed well after the limitation period of § 11.190(5)(c); however, the court found that a subsequent court decision had overturned the one-year limitation. The court held that the standard two-year tort statute of limitations was applicable, Nev. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 11.190(4)(e). The court found that the inmate's amended complaint should relate back to the original filing date because the failure to name the state was not a conscious election. Because the amended complaint related back to the filing of the original complaint, the court held that the inmate had complied with § 11.190(4)(e).


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of dismissal and remanded for further proceedings.

Burleigh v. State Bar


No. 12989


Supreme Court of Nevada


98 Nev. 140; 643 P.2d 1201; 1982 Nev. LEXIS 412



April 28, 1982 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from decision of hearing panel, Southern Disciplinary Board of the State Bar of Nevada.



DISPOSITION: Disbarment, public reprimand, fine and assessment of costs ordered in accordance with recommendations. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant attorney challenged the decision of a hearing panel of respondent Southern Nevada Disciplinary Board of the State Bar of Nevada (bar), which recommended that the attorney be disbarred, publicly reprimanded, fined, and assessed the costs of the disciplinary proceedings against him.


OVERVIEW: After the attorney's license, temporarily suspended due to his indictment, was reinstated, the bar charged the attorney with unethical conduct. Finding that the attorney participated in a plot to kill his former wife and failed to disclose such involvement and that he violated his temporary suspension, the panel of the disciplinary board recommended disbarment and assessment of the proceedings' costs plus a fine and public reprimand. Confirming the panel's recommendations, the court ruled that the disciplinary proceedings conducted by the panel were not inconsistent with due process because of the potential for recovery by the bar of fines and costs. Disciplinary board members received no compensation for their services and were not members of the bar's board of governors. Further, the disciplinary board's sole function was to adjudicate and make recommendations regarding bar discipline matters. The court held that the temporary suspension had been warranted because the attorney's continued practice with serious charges leveled against him would erode public confidence in the legal profession.


OUTCOME: The court adopted the hearing panel's findings and recommendations. The court ordered that the attorney be disbarred from the practice of law in the State of Nevada and be publicly reprimanded for his conduct in violating the attorney disciplinary rules and that he pay to the bar a fine for violating the court's temporary suspension order, together with the costs incurred in connection with his proceedings before the disciplinary board.

Ewing v. State


No. 12835


Supreme Court of Nevada


98 Nev. 81; 640 P.2d 922; 1982 Nev. LEXIS 391



February 25, 1982 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a judgment of commitment, Ninth Judicial District Court, Douglas County; Howard D. McKibben, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, a juvenile, sought review of a decision of the Ninth Judicial District Court, Douglas County (Nevada), which ordered that she was to have been committed as a juvenile delinquent to the Nevada Girls Training Center.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged the trial court's authority to commit her. The court held that defendant never committed a delinquent act, she was not a "child" under the Juvenile Court Act after her 18th birthday when the proceedings below occurred as required by Nev. Rev. Stat. § 62.020(2). Thus, the provisions of Nev. Rev. Stat. § 62.070, which allowed the extension of juvenile court jurisdiction over "any child" until the "child" reached 21, did not apply. The court held that the trial court's commitment of defendant and its exercise of jurisdiction over her were not authorized under the Juvenile Court Act, Nev. Rev. Stat. ch. 62 because she was 18 at the time of the commitment. Further, the adjudication that she was a child in need of supervision (CHINS) was invalid on several grounds. Most importantly, defendant was adjudicated to be both a CHINS and a delinquent in contravention of Nev. Rev. Stat. § 62.040(1)(b). Because defendant was invalidly adjudicated a CHINS, the trial court had no authority to put her on probation for a nondelinquent act.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the commitment and ordered the adjudication of delinquency by the trial court vacated.

Board of Regents v. Oakley


No. 13011


Supreme Court of Nevada


97 Nev. 605; 637 P.2d 1199; 1981 Nev. LEXIS 601; 29 Empl. Prac. Dec. (CCH) P32,845



December 21, 1981 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from summary judgment in favor of respondent, Second Judicial District Court, Washoe County; William N. Forman, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, the members of the Board of Regents of the University of Nevada System and a community college and its dean, sought review of a decision by the Second Judicial District Court, Washoe County (Nevada) to grant summary judgment in favor of appellee teacher. The teacher had been told that he would not be retained on the faculty of the community college because of his age.


OVERVIEW: Appellants claimed that Nev. Rev. Stat. § 281.370 could not be applied to the university system because it would be an unconstitutional infringement upon their authority. They argued that the unique constitutional status of the Board gave it virtual autonomy and immunity from the non-discrimination policy established by the Nevada legislature. In challenging the constitutionality of § 281.370, the Board intimated that its own regulations were equal in status and dignity to the legislative enactment. The court held that: (1) King v. Board of Regents did not stand for the proposition that the Board was free from all legislative regulation but that the legislature could not invade the constitutional powers of the Board through legislation that directly interfered with essential functions of the university; (2) because § 281.370 simply prescribed duties concerning the fair treatment of its personnel, it did not interfere with the Board's essential management and control of the university; and (3) § 281.370 did not interfere with any constitutional rights or prerogatives of the Board.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

Princess Sea Indus. v. State

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a brothel owner and two publishing corporations, appealed an order of the Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County (Nevada), which denied their request to have Nev. 195 of 423 DOCUMENTS


Litteral v. State


No. 12054


Supreme Court of Nevada


97 Nev. 503; 634 P.2d 1226; 1981 Nev. LEXIS 576



October 26, 1981 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied December 9, 1981.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from conviction, after a jury trial, of robbery with the use of a deadly weapon, battery with the intent to commit robbery, and battery with a deadly weapon; Second Judicial District Court, Washoe County; William N. Forman, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his convictions from the Second Judicial District Court, Washoe County (Nevada) for robbery with the use of a deadly weapon, battery with the intent to commit robbery, and battery with a deadly weapon.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court erred by not instructing the jury that specific intent was an essential element of robbery, and the constitutional prohibition against double jeopardy precluded convictions for both batteries. Defendant had requested the trial court to instruct the jury that to find him guilty of robbery, defendant had to have taken the property with a specific intent to deprive the victim permanently of his property. The court found that Nev. Rev. Stat. § 200.380 defined robbery as a general intent crime which was meant to include all violent takings from the person or presence of another. Therefore, the trial court did not err in refusing to give the requested specific intent instruction. The court also found that because defendant was convicted of the crime of robbery with the use of a deadly weapon and battery with intent to commit robbery, there was no additional factual finding needed to satisfy all the elements of the crime of battery with the use of a deadly weapon. Therefore, to allow the conviction for a second battery to stand constituted an impermissible double punishment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions from the trial court for robbery with the use of a deadly weapon, battery with the intent to commit robbery. The court reversed defendant's conviction of battery with a deadly weapon and remanded the matter to the trial court.

State v. Chumphol


No. 12610


Supreme Court of Nevada


97 Nev. 440; 634 P.2d 451; 1981 Nev. LEXIS 555



October 13, 1981 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from an order dismissing an information charging respondent with a violation of NRS 202.360(2), Second Judicial District Court, Washoe County; William N. Forman, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State of Nevada sought review of an order of the Second Judicial District Court (Nevada), which dismissed an information charging defendant with a violation of Nev. Rev. Stat. § 202.360(2). The district court concluded that the statute, as it applied to aliens, was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Section 202.360(2) criminalized the ownership or possession by aliens of firearms capable of concealment. Police officers found a pistol on defendant's person. On appeal, the court held that (1) classifications based on alienage were subject to strict judicial scrutiny, and cases cited by the State that held otherwise were not relevant because they involved classifications excluding aliens from fundamental government activities, which were a recognized exception; (2) § 202.360(2) was constitutional only if the State showed that its purpose was both constitutionally permissible and substantial, and that the classification was necessary accomplish its purpose or safeguard its interest; (3) the fact that a person was a noncitizen did not make then likely to exhibit a tendency toward crime, and classification based upon alienage was an anachronistic remnant of an improper xenophobic attitude; and (4) even if the State's purpose was constitutionally permissible, the statute was not necessary to safeguard the argued interest because Nev. Rev. Stat. § 202.350 prohibited the unlawful carrying of firearms capable of concealment without regard to alienage.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

197 of 423 DOCUMENTS


State Bar v. List


No. 13359


Supreme Court of Nevada


97 Nev. 367; 632 P.2d 341; 1981 Nev. LEXIS 536



August 13, 1981 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original proceeding in mandamus.



DISPOSITION: Writ issued. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, the State Bar of Nevada, the Washoe County Bar Association, and citizens, sought a writ of mandamus to compel respondent Governor of the State of Nevada to declare vacant under Nev. Rev. Stat. § 3.080(1) two judgeships that had been created by Nev. Rev. Stat. § 3.012.


OVERVIEW: Petitioners' action sought the writ to force the Governor declare vacant two district court judgeships. The Governor argued that there were no vacancies because the number of judges in the district could not have been increased at the time under Nev. Const. art. VI, § 5. The court issued petitioners the writ of mandamus. The declaration of vacancy required under Nev. Rev. Stat. § 3.080(1) was ministerial. Further, 1981 Nev. Stat. 286, which had created the vacancies, was constitutional. As a result, a writ of mandamus could be used to force the Governor to make a vacancy declaration if a citizen filed an action to compel such a declaration. The purpose of Nev. Const. art. VI, § 5 was to preserve the security of district judges while they were in office. Nev. Rev. Stat. § 3.012 did not undermine this purpose. As a result, § 3.012 was also constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court issued the writ of mandamus.

 

198 of 423 DOCUMENTS


Ottenheimer v. Real Estate Div. of Nev. Dep't of Commerce


No. 11377


Supreme Court of Nevada


97 Nev. 314; 629 P.2d 1203; 1981 Nev. LEXIS 519



June 24, 1981 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from judgment denying declaratory and injunctive relief, Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County; Paul S. Goldman, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant registered representative filed suit against respondents, the Real Estate Division of the Nevada Department of Commerce and the State of Nevada, seeking a declaration that the 1973 amendment to Nev. Rev. Stat. § 119.180 be determined unconstitutional. The representative challenged the decision of the Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County (Nevada), which entered judgment in favor of respondents.


OVERVIEW: The amendment required that to sell land under Nev. Rev. Stat. ch. 119, a "registered representative" had to be licensed as a salesman or broker. The representative attempted to show that the legislation was insufficiently related to the ends sought to be achieved, arguing that it was unnecessary because the Division could have controlled any problems that arose by virtue of land sales by registered representatives by other means. However, the fact that there were problems with unethical conduct on the part of some registered representatives indicated that the legislature was justified in adopting the amendment to protect the land buying public. Thus, the court ruled that the trial court properly entered judgment in favor of respondents because the representative failed to make a "clear showing" of the statute's invalidity. The Division established that the legislation was calculated to promote the general welfare. The requirement that representatives be licensed salesmen was reasonably related to remedying the claimed inaction on the part of the Division, establishing competence in the representatives, and providing additional controls over land sales operations to protect buyers.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision.

 

199 of 423 DOCUMENTS


A Minor v. Juvenile Div. of Seventh Judicial Dist. Court


Nos. 12482, 12645


Supreme Court of Nevada


97 Nev. 281; 630 P.2d 245; 1981 Nev. LEXIS 511



June 16, 1981 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Consolidated appeals from Orders of Commitment; Third Judicial District Court, Churchill County; Stanley A. Smart, Judge; and Seventh Judicial District Court, Lincoln County; Merlyn H. Hoyt, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: On consolidated review, appellant male child sought review of the decision of the Judicial Division of the Seventh District Court of the State of Nevada and appellant female child sought review of the decision of the Juvenile Division of the Third Judicial District Court, County of Churchill (Nevada). The decisions failed to adjudicate appellants as delinquents but ordered their confinement in a juvenile correctional institution.


OVERVIEW: The male child and female child appeared before different juvenile courts regarding petitions that asserted they required additional monitoring and supervision. The juvenile courts failed to adjudicate either male child or female child a delinquent child, but ordered their confinement in a juvenile correctional institution. The male child and female child sought review of the orders of confinement. The court reversed the orders of confinement and found that only children who had been adjudicated by the juvenile court to be delinquent may be committed to a juvenile correctional facility. Also, the court found that because neither appellant had been charged with delinquency, neither could be adjudicated a delinquent child.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the orders of confinement entered by the juvenile courts. The court also reversed and remanded with instructions that the juvenile court proceeding against male child be dismissed. Finally, the court vacated and remanded the decisions regarding female child for proceedings consistent with the court's opinion.

Nevada State Bd. of Dental Examiners v. Toogood


No. 11304


Supreme Court of Nevada


97 Nev. 255; 628 P.2d 301; 1981 Nev. LEXIS 502



May 26, 1981 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from judgment. Second Judicial District Court, Washoe County; John E. Gabrielli, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Nevada Board of Dental Examiners (Board) sought review of a decision from the district court (Nevada), which entered judgment vacating the Board's order suspending a dentist from practice for three months upon the ground that the order was arbitrary and capricious. The Board had filed an administrative complaint against respondent dentist.


OVERVIEW: The complaint had alleged that the dentist was guilty of dishonorable and unprofessional conduct. The district court had found that Nev. Rev. Stat. 631.050(2) was unconstitutionally overbroad and vague as applied in this case and had vacated the Board's order suspending the dentist from practice for three months upon the ground that the order was arbitrary and capricious. On appeal, the court held that a review of the record in this case clearly established unprofessional and dishonorable conduct on the part of the dentist. The court held that the dentist's conduct clearly fell within Nev. Rev. Stat. 631.050(1)(o): willful negligence in the practice of dentistry. The court held that the action of the Board could have been affirmed on that ground and that it was unnecessary for the district court to reach the questions of the constitutionality of § 631.050(2). The court held that the record failed to show that the Board acted in an arbitrary or capricious manner or abused its discretion in imposing the three-month suspension.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the district court's modification of the dentist's suspension in this case and reinstated the Board's findings of fact, conclusions of law, and decision. The court held that the dentist's conduct clearly constituted willful negligence in the practice of dentistry under state law and that it was unnecessary for the district court to reach the questions of the constitutionality of a separate state statute.
